The Argument from Contingency to Divine Attributes
Juwayni presents a rational proof for divine attributes from contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni uses the contingency of created attributes to prove that the Creator must possess power, will, knowledge, and life.

Core Idea
Contingent attributes in creation prove necessary attributes in the Creator.

Juwayni begins a new section on what must be affirmed of Allah. He argues that by observing the contingent attributes of creatures—attributes that could be otherwise—one is led to recognize what attributes the Creator must necessarily possess. This passage presents a logical chain from contingency to the necessity of four key divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting premise
Recognize that Juwayni begins from the contingency of created attributes (like existence and change). Note that contingency means something could be or not be.
2
Follow the logical chain
Trace how contingency leads to the necessity of a Maker, then to the Maker's power, will, knowledge, and life. Notice each step is justified by a rational principle.
Pay attention to the causality: power alone does not produce an act without will.
3
Summarize the conclusion
Understand that the contingency of attributes in creation directly implies that the Creator must possess these attributes necessarily—not contingently.
This is the foundation for affirming divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام فيما يجب لله تبارك وتعالى. أحاط بالصفات الجائزة للمخلوقات أرشدته إلى ما يجب لبارئها من الصفات فدل جواز وجود الحوادث على وجوب وجود صانعها فإن الجائز لا يقع بنفسه كما سبق ولا يتصف وجود صانعه بالجواز فإنه لو كان جائزا لافتقر إلى صانع كما أن المصنوع مفتقر وقد تقرر تقدير ذلك يدل جواز الحادثات على كون بارئها قادرا فإنا على الاضطرار نعلم أن المؤثر الفعال يجب أن يكون مقتدرا على فعله ويجب أن يكون مريدا له فإن القدرة لا توقع الفعل لعينها بل بفعل القادر بالقدرة متى أراد ثم يستحيل أن يريد مالا يعلمه ثم يستحيل الاتصاف بهذه الصفات دون الاتصاف بالحياة فلاح أن جواز الصفات الثابتة للحوادث دال على وجوب هذه الصفات للصانع. فصل: اعترف كل من انتسب إلى الإسلام بكونه تعالى حيا عالما قادرا ففي العلم والحياة والقدرة طوائف وطال النزاع في ذلك بين الفرق وتفاقم الخطب وانتهى غالون إلى التكفير والتبرى. والقول في ذلك قريب المدرك عندنا. فنقول: إذا وصفتم الباري تعالى وتقدس بكونه قادرا حيا عالما فلا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما فإن اعترفتم بكونه عالما فهو العلم بعينه فسبحان من أغوى أمما في اعتقاد نفي العلم.
Speech on what is necessary for Allah, Blessed and Exalted. Considering the contingent attributes of creatures guided one to what is necessary for their Creator of attributes. So the contingency of the existence of events indicates the necessity of the existence of their Maker, for the contingent does not occur by itself as previously, nor is the existence of its Maker described with contingency, for if it were contingent it would need a maker just as the made thing is in need. And it has been established that the estimation of that indicates the contingency of events indicates that their Creator is powerful, for we know necessarily that the effective cause must be capable of its act and must be willing for it, for power does not bring about the act by itself, but rather by the act of the capable through power when he wills. Then it is impossible that He wills what He does not know, then it is impossible to be described with these attributes without being described with life. So it became clear that the contingency of the attributes established for events indicates the necessity of these attributes for the Maker. Chapter: Everyone who ascribes to Islam acknowledged that He, exalted, is living, knowing, powerful. But concerning knowledge, life, and power, there are factions, and the disagreement between the sects has been prolonged, the matter worsened, and extremists ended up declaring disbelief and disassociation. And the statement regarding that is near of attainment with us. So we say: When you describe the Creator, exalted and sanctified, as being powerful, living, knowing, there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing. For if you acknowledge that He is knowing, that is knowledge itself. So glorified is He who misled nations in the belief of negating knowledge.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification. Juwayni begins a new section on what is necessary for God. He argues: considering the contingent attributes of creatures (like existence, change) leads one to recognize what attributes the Creator must have. The very fact that events are contingent (they could be or not be) shows they need a necessary Maker. That Maker cannot be contingent Himself, otherwise He would need another maker. Then, from the contingency of events, we infer that their Creator must be powerful (qādir), because only a capable agent can bring about a contingent act. Moreover, the Creator must be willing (murīd), because power alone does not produce an act unless the agent wills it. But will requires knowledge of what is willed, so the Creator must be knowing ('ālim). And these attributes (power, will, knowledge) cannot exist without life, so the Creator must be living (ḥayy). Thus, the contingency of attributes in creatures proves the necessary possession of these attributes in the Creator. Juwayni then notes that all Muslims agree God is living, knowing, powerful, but there have been disputes among sects about the nature of these attributes, leading some to extremes of takfīr. Juwayni gives a simple resolution: when we say God is knowing, knowledge is nothing other than the fact that the knower is knowing. Acknowledging that God is knowing is itself the affirmation of knowledge. Those who deny knowledge (like some Mu'tazilites?) have been led astray.

Key Terms
واجب
جائز
قادر
مريد
عالم
حي
علم
قدرة
حياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that contingent events can occur without a cause or by themselves.
Correction: Juwayni asserts that the contingent does not occur by itself; it requires a necessary Maker.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, why must the Creator be willing (murīd)?
A) Because power alone is sufficient to bring about an act.
B) Because the act of the capable is only produced when he wills it.
C) Because all contingent things must be willed by God.
D) Because without will, God would be like a lifeless force.

Key Takeaway
The contingency of created attributes rationally proves that the Creator must be powerful, willing, knowing, and living.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live in a world of change and dependence. After reading this proof, do you truly rely on the Necessary Being, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What would change today if you fully acknowledged your contingency?
?
Your own power, will, and knowledge are gifts from the Creator who possesses them necessarily. Are you using them in a way that honors that source? How can you consciously attribute your abilities to Him in your next action?
?
Juwayni emphasizes that life is necessary for the other attributes. Your life is borrowed. If you truly believed that every moment is a gift from the Living One, would you live differently? What small step can you take today to live with that awareness?

The Nature of Divine Attributes and the Resolution of Disputes
Juwayni comments on the dispute over divine attributes and offers a concise resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's simple resolution to the dispute over the nature of divine attributes: affirming that God is knowing is the same as affirming His knowledge.

Core Idea
Saying God is knowing is the same as affirming His knowledge.

After establishing the necessity of divine attributes, Juwayni addresses the historical disagreements among Muslim sects about the nature of these attributes. He notes that all Muslims affirm that God is living, knowing, and powerful, but disputes arose regarding whether these attributes are distinct from God's essence. Juwayni presents a simple resolution that cuts through the controversy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the disagreement
Juwayni states that all Muslims acknowledge God is living, knowing, powerful, but factions differed and extremists declared takfīr. Understand the context of this dispute.
This disagreement was over whether attributes are identical to essence or distinct.
2
Analyze Juwayni's resolution
He says: when you say God is knowing, knowledge is nothing other than the knower being knowing. If you acknowledge He is knowing, that is knowledge itself. So there is no separate entity.
This resolves the debate by equating the attribute with the description.
3
Reflect on the warning
Juwayni ends with a statement that God has misled nations who negated knowledge. This underscores the seriousness of denying divine attributes.
It shows that denial of attributes is a grave error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام فيما يجب لله تبارك وتعالى. أحاط بالصفات الجائزة للمخلوقات أرشدته إلى ما يجب لبارئها من الصفات فدل جواز وجود الحوادث على وجوب وجود صانعها فإن الجائز لا يقع بنفسه كما سبق ولا يتصف وجود صانعه بالجواز فإنه لو كان جائزا لافتقر إلى صانع كما أن المصنوع مفتقر وقد تقرر تقدير ذلك يدل جواز الحادثات على كون بارئها قادرا فإنا على الاضطرار نعلم أن المؤثر الفعال يجب أن يكون مقتدرا على فعله ويجب أن يكون مريدا له فإن القدرة لا توقع الفعل لعينها بل بفعل القادر بالقدرة متى أراد ثم يستحيل أن يريد مالا يعلمه ثم يستحيل الاتصاف بهذه الصفات دون الاتصاف بالحياة فلاح أن جواز الصفات الثابتة للحوادث دال على وجوب هذه الصفات للصانع. فصل: اعترف كل من انتسب إلى الإسلام بكونه تعالى حيا عالما قادرا ففي العلم والحياة والقدرة طوائف وطال النزاع في ذلك بين الفرق وتفاقم الخطب وانتهى غالون إلى التكفير والتبرى. والقول في ذلك قريب المدرك عندنا. فنقول: إذا وصفتم الباري تعالى وتقدس بكونه قادرا حيا عالما فلا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما فإن اعترفتم بكونه عالما فهو العلم بعينه فسبحان من أغوى أمما في اعتقاد نفي العلم.
Speech on what is necessary for Allah, Blessed and Exalted. Considering the contingent attributes of creatures guided one to what is necessary for their Creator of attributes. So the contingency of the existence of events indicates the necessity of the existence of their Maker, for the contingent does not occur by itself as previously, nor is the existence of its Maker described with contingency, for if it were contingent it would need a maker just as the made thing is in need. And it has been established that the estimation of that indicates the contingency of events indicates that their Creator is powerful, for we know necessarily that the effective cause must be capable of its act and must be willing for it, for power does not bring about the act by itself, but rather by the act of the capable through power when he wills. Then it is impossible that He wills what He does not know, then it is impossible to be described with these attributes without being described with life. So it became clear that the contingency of the attributes established for events indicates the necessity of these attributes for the Maker. Chapter: Everyone who ascribes to Islam acknowledged that He, exalted, is living, knowing, powerful. But concerning knowledge, life, and power, there are factions, and the disagreement between the sects has been prolonged, the matter worsened, and extremists ended up declaring disbelief and disassociation. And the statement regarding that is near of attainment with us. So we say: When you describe the Creator, exalted and sanctified, as being powerful, living, knowing, there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing. For if you acknowledge that He is knowing, that is knowledge itself. So glorified is He who misled nations in the belief of negating knowledge.

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification. Juwayni begins a new section on what is necessary for God. He argues: considering the contingent attributes of creatures (like existence, change) leads one to recognize what attributes the Creator must have. The very fact that events are contingent (they could be or not be) shows they need a necessary Maker. That Maker cannot be contingent Himself, otherwise He would need another maker. Then, from the contingency of events, we infer that their Creator must be powerful (qādir), because only a capable agent can bring about a contingent act. Thus, the contingency of attributes in creatures proves the necessary possession of these attributes in the Creator. Juwayni gives a simple resolution: when we say God is knowing, knowledge is nothing other than the fact that the knower is knowing. Acknowledging that God is knowing is itself the affirmation of knowledge. Those who deny knowledge (like some Mu'tazilites?) have been led astray.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that divine attributes like knowledge are separate eternal entities distinct from God's essence.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing; affirming God is knowing is itself the affirmation of knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the meaning of 'knowledge' when we say God is knowing?
A) A separate attribute entity
B) The fact that the knower is knowing
C) An eternal concept
D) A created quality

Key Takeaway
Affirming that God is knowing is identical to affirming the attribute of knowledge; there is no distinction between the name and the attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah knows everything,' do you truly believe that this is a real description of Him, or has intellectual pride made you think it is just a metaphor? If you have ever doubted that God's names reflect real attributes, what is preventing you from embracing the simple truth Juwayni presents: that saying He is knowing is the same as affirming His knowledge? Will you today resolve to say His names with full conviction, not as empty titles but as realities that define your worship?
?
Juwayni marvels at how entire nations were misled by denying the attribute of knowledge. Have you ever been swayed by arguments that seem intellectually sophisticated but lead you away from the clear affirmations of the early community? Examine your own heart: is there any area of God's attributes where you hesitate to affirm because of what others might think? Make a firm decision from this moment to affirm every attribute that God has affirmed for Himself, knowing that this is the path of salvation.

The Inseparability of Knowledge from the Knower
Juwayni argues that affirming God is Knowing entails affirming knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that acknowledging God as Knowing necessarily entails affirming the reality of the attribute of knowledge, and why denying the attribute while affirming the description is a contradiction.

Core Idea
To say God is Knowing is to affirm knowledge itself.

Juwayni addresses a theological dispute about the nature of God's attributes. He observes that all Muslims agree God is Knowing, but some deny that knowledge is a real attribute. In this passage, he argues that such a denial is self-contradictory. By following his simple reasoning, you will see why affirming that God is Knowing logically requires affirming the attribute of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice Juwayni's repeated phrase 'لا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما'.
2
Identify the target and claim
Juwayni targets those who affirm God is Knowing but deny the attribute of knowledge. Identify his claim that such a position is contradictory.
He starts by noting universal agreement but then exposes inconsistency.
3
Trace the logical argument
Break down the argument step by step: first the premise that all agree God is Knowing, then the definition of knowledge, then the implication, then the contradiction.
The argument is almost a tautology: knowledge just means being knowing.
4
Reflect on the key phrase
Focus on the sentence 'لا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما بمعلوماته على ما هي عليها'. Why does Juwayni repeat this?
This is the core of his proof.
5
Understand the resolution
Juwayni concludes that the dispute is resolved by this simple logical point. Those who deny knowledge are actually denying what they affirm.
The wonder is that people can be misled into denying something they already accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: اغترف كل من أنتمى إلى الإسلام بكونه تعالى حيا عالما قادرا في العلم والحياة والقدرة طوائف، وطال النزاع في ذلك بين الفرق وتفاقم الخطب وانتهى غالون إلى التكفير والتبرى. والقول في ذلك قريب المدرك عندها. فنقول: إذا وصفتم البارى تعالى وتقدس بكونه قادرا حيا عالما، فلا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما. فإن اعترفتم بكونه عالما، فلا معنى للعلم إلا أن يكون العالم عالما. وإن اعترفتم بكونه عالما فهو العلم بعينه، فسبحان من أغوى أمما في اعتقاد نفي العلم. وما اعترفوا به من كونه عالما هو عين ما أنكروه، فلا معنى للعلم إلا كون العالم عالما بمعلوماته على ما هي عليها.
Section: All those who attribute themselves to Islam have commonly recognized that He, Exalted, is Living, Knowing, Powerful—[this is] regarding knowledge, life, and power, [among] sects. And the dispute prolonged concerning that among the groups, and the matter became grave, and some of them ended up declaring disbelief and disassociation. And the statement concerning that is near to understanding with them. So we say: When you describe the Creator, Exalted and Sanctified, as being Powerful, Living, Knowing, then there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing. So if you acknowledge that He is Knowing, then there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing. And if you acknowledge that He is Knowing, then it is knowledge itself. So exalted is He who misled nations in the belief of denying knowledge. And what they acknowledged of His being Knowing is exactly what they denied. So there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing of His objects of knowledge as they are.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who affirm that God is Knowing yet deny the attribute of knowledge as something distinct. Juwayni begins by noting that all Islamic sects agree that God is Living, Knowing, and Powerful, yet disagreement persists about the nature of these attributes, leading some to declare others disbelievers. The author then presents a simple argument: if you describe God as 'knowing' (ʿālim), the very meaning of 'knowledge' (ʿilm) is nothing other than that the knower is knowing. Thus, admitting that God is Knowing necessarily entails affirming the reality of knowledge as an attribute. Those who acknowledge that He is Knowing but deny knowledge are contradicting themselves, because what they acknowledge (being Knowing) is precisely what they deny (knowledge). The phrase 'there is no meaning to knowledge except that the knower is knowing of His objects of knowledge as they are' underscores that knowledge is relational and real.

Key Terms
علم
عالم
قادر
حياة
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming 'God is knowing' is different from affirming an attribute 'knowledge' over and above the essence; the two are separate.
Correction: Juwayni shows they are inseparable: the meaning of knowledge is simply that the knower is knowing. So affirming the description is affirming the attribute.

Checkpoint
What is Juwayni's main argument against those who affirm God is Knowing but deny the attribute of knowledge?
A) They fail to understand the meaning of the word 'knowing'.
B) They are guilty of innovation (bidʿa) and should be declared disbelievers.
C) Acknowledging that God is Knowing necessarily implies affirming knowledge, as knowledge is the state of being knowing.
D) Knowledge is a separate entity from the knower, so they must accept that.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledging that God is Knowing necessarily affirms the reality of knowledge as an attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though God knows every detail of your life, or do you compartmentalize this belief away from your daily choices? What would change if you acted on the certainty that His knowledge is real and immediate?
?
When you say 'Allah knows best,' is it a worn-out phrase, or does it pierce your heart with accountability? Identify one area where you have been comfortable assuming God's ignorance of your inner state, and resolve to bring it before Him today.
?
Juwayni exposes the self-contradiction of affirming God's knowledge while denying its reality. Where in your life do you verbally affirm a truth about Allah but live as if its consequences are not real? What is one step you can take tonight to align your action with your belief?

The Eternity of Divine Will
Juwayni refutes the view that God's will is created and argues for its eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that God's will is eternal and cannot be created, and the rational consequence of claiming otherwise.

Core Idea
God's will is identical to His essence—eternal, not created in time.

Juwayni confronts a heretical group that claimed God's will is something He creates in time. He asserts the orthodox position: God has always been willing, and His being willing is His very will. He then presents a devastating logical argument: if the will were created, it would either need another will to specify it (infinite regress) or be independent (implying the world needs no specifier). This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key claim: God has never ceased to be willing.
2
Identify the correct position
Find the sentence where Juwayni states the Sunni creed: the Creator has always been willing in eternity.
3
Understand the innovation
The innovators claim God was not willing preeternally but then created wills for Himself. See how Juwayni calls this 'a departure from the way of religion'.
4
Follow the rational refutation
The argument: if the will were generated, it would need a specifier. If it didn't, the world would be independent of a specifier. This shows the necessity of eternal will.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument is powerful: it closes the door to any created attribute in God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: الصانع لم يزل مريدا في أزله لما سيكون فيما لا يزال، وكونه مريدا عين إرادته. وضلت طائفة من المبتدعة ضلالا بعيدا، فزعموا أنه لم يكن مريدا في أزله، ثم أحدث لنفسه فيما لا يزال إرادات للكائنات التي يريدها فصار مريدا بتلك الإرادات الحادثة، وهذا انسلال عن طريقة الدين. فإن الإرادة لو كانت حادثة لافتقرت إلى إرادة لها بها تخصص. وإن استغنت وهي حادثة مختصة عن مخصص، لزم استغناء العالم بما فيه عن مريد مخصص.
Section: The Creator has never ceased to be willing in His eternity for what will be in what does not cease [i.e., the future], and His being willing is identical to His will. And a group of innovators strayed far astray, claiming that He was not willing in His eternity, then He generated for Himself in what does not cease wills for the beings that He wills, so He became willing by those generated wills. And this is a departure from the way of religion. For if the will were generated, it would need a will by which it is specified. And if it were independent, while being generated and specified, from a specifier, then the world including what is in it would be independent of a willing specifier.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that God's will (irāda) is created in time (ḥāditha). Juwayni states the correct position: God has always been willing in eternity, and His being willing is identical with His will (i.e., the attribute is eternal and not separate from His essence). He then criticizes the innovating sect that claims God was not willing preeternally, but then created wills for Himself in time for the things He wills, thereby becoming willing through those created wills. This, Juwayni says, is a departure from the path of religion. The refutation: if the will itself were created, it would need another will to specify it (since every contingent event requires a cause). If it were independent of a specifier despite being contingent and specific, then the entire world would also be independent of a willing specifier—which is absurd. Thus, God's will must be eternal.

Key Terms
إرادة
مريد
حادث
أزل
تخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will can be created in time.
Correction: If God's will were created, it would need another will to specify it (infinite regress) or imply the world needs no specifier, both impossible. Hence, God's will must be eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of claiming that God's will is created (ḥādith) according to Juwayni?
A) It would mean God is not eternal.
B) It would require another will to specify it, leading to infinite regress, or the world would be independent of God.
C) It would mean God's will changes over time.
D) It would make God's will identical with His knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal and identical to His essence; the claim that it is created leads to logical absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is eternal and unchanging, then every event in your life—including your sins—was eternally willed by Him. Does this truth humble you or trouble you? Will you surrender the illusion that some things happen outside His will, or will you finally trust that His eternal will is perfect and just, even when you don't understand it?
?
Juwayni argues that if God's will were created, it would need another will, leading to an infinite regress. This shows the absolute self-sufficiency of God. When you pray for something, do you truly believe that God's will for you was already set from eternity, or do you secretly hope to 'change His mind'? How would your prayers change if you fully internalized that His will is eternal and unchangeable?
?
The innovators claimed God was not willing in preeternity but later generated wills. This implies a deficiency in God that He later remedies. Look at your own heart: do you ever think of God as 'updating' His plans or reacting to your actions? Will you repent of any anthropomorphic notion that diminishes His perfection, and instead worship Him as the one whose will never changes?

intermediate
5 min
The Necessity of Divine Speech: An Incomplete Argument
Juwayni begins to argue for the necessity of the attribute of speech for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beginning of Juwayni's argument for divine speech as an essential attribute and how it departs from the standard principle of the creed.

Core Idea
Divine speech is necessary, but proving it requires a move beyond standard kalam methods.

Juwayni turns to a new attribute: divine speech. He immediately signals that this proof is not like the others—it stands outside the usual principle of his creed. The passage starts an argument from the diversity of creation, but breaks off before the conclusion. Your task is to grasp the opening move and the problem Juwayni sets up.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note its incompleteness
The text ends mid-argument. Read the Arabic and English side by side, and note where it stops. Why might Juwayni consider this proof different?
The full argument likely continues on the next page, which we do not have.
2
Identify the central claim
Juwayni states that being described with speech (al-ittiṣāf bi al-kalām) is necessary for God (mimmā yajibu). This is the thesis.
3
Understand the method introduced
He compares our knowledge of creation's variation to something about the Creator. The analogy ('just as... so likewise') suggests a causal inference from creation to Creator.
The precise inference is cut off, but it likely connects contingent diversity to a commanding will expressed through speech.
4
Reflect on the phrase 'outside the principle'
Juwayni says this proof is khārij ʿan al-qāʿida (outside the principle) that is the basis of this creed. Why might proving speech be different from proving existence or other attributes?
This hints that the standard contingency argument may not directly yield the attribute of speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: مما يجب الله تعالى: الاتصاف بالكلام. وقد تقطعت المهرة في إثبات العلم بوجوب وصف البارى سبحانه بالكلام، وهو خارج عن القاعدة التي هي مستند هذه العقيدة. فنقول: كما تعلم بعقولنا أن تردد الخلق على صنوف التغاير من الجائزات، فكذلك تصرفهم
Section: Among what is necessary for God, Exalted, is being described with speech. And the skilled ones have become divided concerning establishing knowledge of the necessity of describing the Creator, glorified, with speech, and it is outside the principle that is the basis of this creed. So we say: Just as we know by our intellects that the variation of creation among types of difference from contingent things [indicates something], so likewise their actions...
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the necessity of the attribute of speech (kalām) for God. Juwayni notes that there is disagreement among the learned about proving that God must be described with speech, and that this matter is outside the standard principle that forms the basis of this creed (perhaps the principle of using contingency arguments). He then starts an argument: just as we know by our intellects that the variation in creation among different types of contingent things indicates something, so likewise the actions of creatures... The argument is incomplete, as the text breaks off. The full argument likely proceeds to show that the diversity and order in creation point to a commanding will expressed through speech.

Juwayni asserts that divine speech is a necessary attribute, but the proof is complex and departs from the standard method of the creed; the argument from creation's diversity is left incomplete.

The Eternal Divine Will and Its Impossibility of Being Created
Juwayni asserts the eternity of divine will and refutes created will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Juwayni argues that God's will cannot be created and must be eternal.

Core Idea
If God's will were created, it would need another will to specify it — leading to infinite regress.

Juwayni opens a crucial section on the divine will by affirming that God has always been willing eternally. He then refutes a deviant group who claim that God's will is created and temporally originated. The argument he presents is a classic kalam proof against temporal attributes in God, relying on the principle that every contingent event requires a specifier.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the central claim about God's will
Notice how Juwayni states that God has never ceased to be willing and that His being willing is identical to His will.
This establishes the eternity of the attribute.
3
Analyze the refutation of created will
Juwayni describes the heretical view and labels it as straying from the path of religion.
Understand the gravity of the error.
4
Understand the logical proof against created will
Work through the conditional argument: if will were originated, it would need a specifier, leading to an infinite regress or absurdity.
This is the core philosophical proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الصانع لم يزل مريدا فى أزله لما سيكون فيما يزل، وكونه مريدا عين إرادته. وضلت طائفة من المبتدعة ضلالا بعيدا، فزعموا أنه لم يكن مريدا فى أزله، ثم أحدث لنفسه فيما لا يزال إرادات للكائنات التي يريدها فصار مريدا بتلك الإرادات الحادثة، وهذا انسلال عن طريقة الدين. فان الإرادة لو كانت حادثة لافتقرت إلى إرادة لها، بها تخصص. وإن استغنت وهي حادثة مختصة عن مخصص، لزم استغناء العالم بما فيه عن مريد مخصص.
Section: The Maker has never ceased to be willing in His eternity for what will be in what is yet to come, and His being willing is identical to His will. A group of innovators went far astray, claiming that He was not willing in His eternity, then He originated for Himself in what is yet to come wills for the things He wills, and He became willing through those originated wills. This is slipping away from the path of religion. For if will were originated, it would depend on a will for it, by which it would be specified. And if it were independent—being originated and specific—of a specifier, then the world with what it contains would be independent of a willing specifier.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation regarding the divine attribute of will (irāda). Juwayni begins by stating that the Creator (al-Ṣāniʿ) has always been willing (murīdan) in His eternity for what will happen in the future, and that His being willing is identical to His will—meaning the attribute is eternal and not distinct from His essence in the sense of being a separate created thing. He then refutes a heretical group (al-mubtadiʿa) who claim that God was not willing originally, but then originated wills (irādāt ḥāditha) for Himself by which He became willing. Juwayni calls this a departure from the path of religion. The core argument is: if will were originated (ḥāditha), it would need another will to specify it, because any originated thing requires a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ). If it could be independent without a specifier, then the entire world could also be independent without a willing specifier—which is absurd. The logic follows the kalam principle of dependence of all contingent things on a cause.

Key Terms
إرادة
مريد
حادثة
مخصِّص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's will is created and changes over time.
Correction: Juwayni shows that a created will would require another will, leading to an infinite chain, and thus cannot be attributed to God.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, why is it impossible for God's will to be created?
A) Because creation requires time.
B) Because a created will would need another will to specify it, leading to infinite regress.
C) Because will cannot be created by definition.
D) Because God's will is identical to His essence.

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal and identical to His essence; a created will is impossible because it would require an infinite regress of specifiers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is eternal and unchanging, how does that confront your moments of doubt when things don't go as you planned? Are you willing to accept that His will for you was set from eternity, even when you cannot see the wisdom now?
?
The innovators claimed God 'became willing' through new wills. Have you ever acted as if God's will adapts to your desires—praying not for alignment with His will but for Him to change His will for you? What would it look like to truly submit to an eternal, unchanging divine will?
?
Juwayni warns that denying the eternity of God's will is 'slipping from the path of religion.' Examine your heart: do you trust that God's will is perfectly good and sufficient for you, or do you secretly wish He could 'change His mind' about certain trials in your life? Make a concrete commitment to surrender one specific area of your life to His eternal will today.

Establishing the Necessity of Divine Speech
Juwayni proves the necessity of divine speech through rational inference from creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's rational proof that God must possess the attribute of speech based on the existence of command and prohibition among creatures.

Core Idea
Command and prohibition in creation prove that God is a speaking King.

Juwayni begins by asserting that speech is a necessary attribute of God. He uses a unique argument: just as we observe variation among creatures, we also see them subject to commands and prohibitions. This points to a Creator who commands and prohibits, which requires speech. This lesson presents that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand Juwayni's flow.
2
Identify the main proof steps
Notice the progression: observation of creatures' variation → possibility of command and prohibition → inference to Creator's attributes → conclusion that God is a speaker.
3
Connect kingship to speech
Juwayni argues that true kingship requires the power to enforce commands, so God must be a speaker. Reflect on why this link is important.
Kingship implies authority, which is expressed through speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مما يجب لله تعالى: الاتصاف بالكلام. وقد تقطعت المهرة في إثبات العلم بوجوب وصف الباري سبحانه بالكلام، وهو خارج عن القاعدة التي هي مستند هذه العقيدة. فنقول: كما نعلم بعقولنا أن تردد الخلق على صنوف التغاير من الجائزات، فكذلك تصرفهم تحت أمر مطاع ونهي متبع ليس من المستحيلات. وإذا قطع بجواز ذلك، كما قضى بجواز جريان الخلائق على اختلاف الأحوال والطرائق، فكل جائز من صفات الخلق يستدل به إلى صفة واجبة للخالق. فيجب جواز انسلاكهم في الأوامر والزواجر اتصاف ربهم بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وهو الملك حقا. ولا يتم وصف الملك دون الاتصاف بالاقتدار على تغيير الخلق قهرا وإمكان توجيه الأمر والنهي عليهم تعبدا وتكليفا. فتقرر بذلك وجوب كونه تعالى وتقدس متكلما. فظن من لم يحصل علم هذا الباب أن القدرية وصفوا الرب تبارك وتعالى بكونه متكلما وزعموا أن كلامه مخلوق، وليس هذا مذهب القوم. بل حقيقة معتقدهم: أن الكلام فعل من أفعال الله عز وجل كخلقه الجواهر وأعراضها، ولا يرجع إلى حقيقة وجوده حكم من الكلام. فمحصول أصلهم: أنه ليس لله - تعالى عن قولهم - كلام وليس قائلا آمرا ناهيا. وإنما يخلق أصواتا في جسم من الأجسام دالة على إرادته. وليس يخفى على ذي بصيرة أن آيات القرآن نصوص في اتصاف الرب تبارك وتعالى بالقول. فكم في سياق الآي من أخبار الرب عن نفسه بالاتصاف بالقول كما قال تعالى: (قال الله هذا يوم ينفع الصادقين صدقهم)، وقال تبارك وتعالى: (يا نار كوني بردا وسلاما)، وقال جل وعز: (وقال ربكم ادعوني أستجب لكم). ومن لزم الإنصاف وجانب الاعتساف تبين أن هذه الآيات مصرحة باتصاف الرب بقوله. ومن أحدث أصواتا في جسم دالة على غرض له لا يقال قال كذا وكذا. ومما يوضح الحق في ذلك أن من أصل هؤلاء: أنه لا معنى لكون المتكلم متكلما إلا أنه فاعل للكلام. ومساق هذا يقتضي أن من لم يعلم كون المتكلم فاعلا لكلامه لا يعلمه متكلما. ونحن على اضطرار نعلم أن من نراه يتكلم جسم.
Section: Among what is necessary for God Most High is the attribution of speech. The scholars have exhausted themselves in establishing knowledge of the obligation of describing the Creator, glorified be He, with speech, which is outside the principle that is the foundation of this creed. We say: Just as we know by our minds that the variation of creatures among kinds of difference is among possible things, so likewise their being subject to a obeyed command and a followed prohibition is not impossible. And if it is decisively judged that this is possible, just as it is judged possible for creatures to proceed according to differing states and ways, then every possible attribute of creatures indicates an obligatory attribute for the Creator. Thus it is necessary that their being included in commands and prohibitions [necessitates] their Lord being characterized by command, prohibition, promise, and threat, and He is the true King. The description of kingship is not complete without the attribute of power to change creatures by force and the possibility of directing command and prohibition upon them as worship and obligation. So by that the necessity of His being, exalted and sanctified, speaking is established. Someone who has not mastered knowledge of this chapter thought that the Qadariyya described the Lord, blessed and exalted, as speaking and claimed that His speech is created, but this is not the doctrine of the people. Rather, the reality of their belief is that speech is an action from the actions of God, like His creation of substances and their accidents, and it does not refer to the reality of His existence any ruling of speech. So the summary of their principle is that God—exalted above their saying—has no speech and is not a speaker, commander, or prohibitor. Rather, He creates sounds in a body from among bodies indicating His will. It is not hidden from one of insight that the verses of the Qur'an are texts concerning the attribution of the Lord, blessed and exalted, with speech. How many in the context of the verses are reports from the Lord about Himself with the attribution of speech, as He said: 'Allah said, This is the day when the truthful will benefit from their truthfulness'; and He said: 'O fire, be cool and safe'; and He said: 'And your Lord said, Call upon Me, I will respond to you.' Whoever adheres to fairness and avoids injustice will see that these verses explicitly state the attribution of the Lord with His speech. And whoever creates sounds in a body indicating an objective of his is not said to have said such and such. And what clarifies the truth in this is that from the principle of these [people] is that there is no meaning to a speaker being speaking except that he is a doer of speech. The import of this requires that whoever does not know that the speaker is a doer of his speech does not know him to be speaking. And we know by necessity that whoever we see speaking is a body.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation regarding the divine attribute of speech (kalām). Juwayni first asserts that speech is a necessary attribute of God. He acknowledges that scholars have exerted themselves on this topic, but he will use a different method. The proof: We observe that creatures vary in possible ways, and they are subject to command and prohibition—this is not impossible. If such a state is possible for creatures, then it points to an obligatory attribute in the Creator. Specifically, if creatures are commanded and prohibited, then their Lord must have the attributes of command, prohibition, promise, and threat—which constitute speech. Moreover, true kingship requires the power to enforce commands, so God must be a speaker. Juwayni then refutes the Qadariyya's view. Some mistakenly think the Qadariyya affirm that God speaks but consider His speech created. Juwayni clarifies that their actual belief is that speech is merely an action of God, like creating bodies; it does not subsist in God's essence. Thus, in reality, they deny that God has speech or that He is a speaker who commands and prohibits. They only believe He creates sounds in some body to indicate His will. Juwayni then gives scriptural evidence: numerous Qur'anic verses explicitly attribute speech to God, such as 'Allah said...' and 'Your Lord said...'. If someone merely creates sounds in a body to convey a purpose, we do not say 'he said' in the same sense. Finally, he critiques the Qadariyya's principle that being a speaker means being a doer of speech. According to that, no one could know a speaker is speaking unless they perceive him performing the act of speech. But we know by necessity that a speaking person is a body, implying that speech requires a physical basis—contradicting the possibility of God's speech. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continued on the next page.

Key Terms
كلام
أمر
نهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the relationship between creatures being subject to command and prohibition and God's attribute of speech?
A) It is impossible for creatures to be commanded, so God does not speak.
B) It is possible, and this indicates God has speech.
C) Only prophets are commanded, not all creatures.
D) Command and prohibition are irrelevant to God's attributes.

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of speech is rationally necessary because creatures are subject to command and prohibition, which require a commanding God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live under many commands—from your conscience, society, and faith. But have you ever paused to consider that the very existence of these commands points to a Commander who not only issues them but has the right to do so? If you ignore or rationalize away His commands, what does that say about your recognition of His kingship?
?
Juwayni argues that true kingship requires power to enforce commands. In your life, you may obey God's commands only when convenient. What would it mean to truly submit to Him as the King who has absolute authority over you, even when it costs you?
?
If God's speech is necessary, then His words are not optional or negotiable. Which of His commands do you find hardest to accept as a necessary part of your life? What would it take for you to embrace it as binding?

Refuting the Qadariyya on Created Speech
Juwayni refutes the Qadariyya by exposing their true denial of divine speech and citing Qur'anic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's refutation of the Qadariyya belief about God's speech, and see the scriptural evidence that God is truly a speaker.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya deny God's speech; the Qur'an proves God speaks directly.

Some mistakenly think the Qadariyya affirm God's speech as created. Juwayni clarifies their actual position: they reduce speech to an action, denying that God is a speaker in the true sense. He then provides Qur'anic verses that explicitly attribute speech to God, and critiques their definition of 'speaker'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya's mistaken view
Juwayni first corrects a common misconception: the Qadariyya do not simply say God's speech is created; they deny that God is a speaker altogether.
2
Examine the Qur'anic verses
Read the three verses Juwayni quotes: 'Allah said...', 'O fire be cool...', 'Your Lord said...'. Notice how each directly attributes speech to God.
3
Analyze the logical flaw
Juwayni points out that according to the Qadariyya's definition, a speaker is one who performs the act of speech. But we know by necessity that a speaking person is a body, implying God would be a body, which is impossible. The argument is cut off, but the intended conclusion is clear.

The proof: We observe that creatures vary in possible ways, and they are subject to command and prohibition—this is not impossible. If such a state is possible for creatures, then it points to an obligatory attribute in the Creator. Specifically, if creatures are commanded and prohibited, then their Lord must have the attributes of command, prohibition, promise, and threat—which constitute speech. Moreover, true kingship requires the power to enforce commands, so God must be a speaker. Juwayni then refutes the Qadariyya's view. Some mistakenly think the Qadariyya affirm that God speaks but consider His speech created. Juwayni clarifies that their actual belief is that speech is merely an action of God, like creating bodies; it does not subsist in God's essence. Thus, in reality, they deny that God has speech or that He is a speaker who commands and prohibits. They only believe He creates sounds in some body to indicate His will. Juwayni then gives scriptural evidence: numerous Qur'anic verses explicitly attribute speech to God, such as 'Allah said...' and 'Your Lord said...'. If someone merely creates sounds in a body to convey a purpose, we do not say 'he said' in the same sense. Finally, he critiques the Qadariyya's principle that being a speaker means being a doer of speech. According to that, no one could know a speaker is speaking unless they perceive him performing the act of speech. But we know by necessity that a speaking person is a body, implying that speech requires a physical basis—contradicting the possibility of God's speech. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continued on the next page.

Key Terms
قدرية
كلام
متكلم
أمر
نهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe God speaks but His speech is created.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the Qadariyya actually deny that God is a speaker; they consider speech an action, not an attribute.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the Qadariyya's actual belief about God's speech?
A) That God speaks with a speech that is eternal.
B) That God speaks with a created speech that subsists in His essence.
C) That speech is an action of God like creation, and God has no attribute of speech.
D) That God does not speak at all, only creatures speak.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya deny that God is truly a speaker; the Qur'an explicitly shows God speaks, and their definition leads to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you truly believe that you are hearing the very speech of God, or do you unconsciously treat it as a human book? What would change in your heart if you fully embraced that every 'Qāla Allāh' (Allah said) is real and personal from Him to you?
?
If someone denied that God speaks, they would rob you of His guidance, commands, and promises. Do you ever live as if God is silent, ignoring His speech in the Qur'an? What would it take for you to respond to His words as a direct address to you, starting today?
?
The Qadariyya reduced God's speech to a mere action. In your life, have you reduced God's speech to mere information—something to study rather than Someone to obey? Will you commit to reading this lesson's verses as a conversation with your Lord, not just a theological proof?

The Necessity of God Being Speaking (Mutakallim)
Juwayni argues from the reality of divine commands to the necessity of God being mutakallim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Juwayni argues that God must be described with the attribute of speech, based on His role as a commanding and prohibiting King.

Core Idea
God's commands prove He speaks.

Juwayni now turns to another divine attribute: speech (kalam). He argues that this attribute is not optional but necessary. His proof focuses on the fact that God gives commands and prohibitions. Since a king issues orders and is obeyed, and God is the true King, He must possess speech. This passage connects God's kingship to the attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Juwayni uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the key premise
The passage begins by stating that an obeyed command and a followed prohibition are not impossible. This sets up the reality of divine commands.
3
Follow the argument from creation
Juwayni draws an analogy: just as possible attributes of creatures point to necessary attributes of the Creator, the fact that creatures are subject to commands indicates that the Creator must have command and prohibition as attributes.
4
Understand the kingship connection
The true King must have the power to compel and direct. Command and prohibition are expressions of that kingship, so God must be described with them.
5
Grasp the conclusion
Thus, it is established that God is necessarily mutakallim (speaking), because He issues commands and prohibitions.
This concludes Juwayni's proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحت أمر مطاع، ونهى متبع، ليس من المستحيلات. وإذا قطع بجواز ذلك، كما قضى بجواز جريان الخلائق على اختلاف الأحوال والطرائق، فكل جائز من صفات الخلق يستدل إلى صفة واجبة للخالق، فيجب جواز انسلاكهم في الأوامر والزواجر، اتصاف ربهم بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وهو الملك حقا. ولا يتم وصف الملك دون الاتصاف بالاقتدار على تغيير الخلق قهرا، وإمكان توجيه الأمر والنهي عليهم تعبدا وتكليفا. فتقرر بذلك وجوب كونه تعالى وتقدس متكلما.
Under an obeyed command and a followed prohibition, it is not among impossibilities. And if one definitively judges the permissibility of that, just as it has been judged regarding the permissibility of the flow of creatures in various states and ways, then every possible attribute of creation indicates a necessary attribute of the Creator. So the permissibility of their being subject to commands and prohibitions necessitates that their Lord be described with command, prohibition, promise, and threat, and He is the true King. And the description of kingship is not complete without being described with the power to change creation by compulsion, and the possibility of directing command and prohibition upon them as worship and obligation. Thus it is established thereby the necessity that He, exalted and sanctified, be speaking (mutakallim).
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) for the necessity of God being mutakallim (speaking). Juwayni begins by stating that it is not impossible for there to be an obeyed command and a followed prohibition. He then argues that just as it is established that creatures exist in various states, every possible attribute of creatures points to a necessary attribute of the Creator. Since humans are subject to divine commands and prohibitions (which are actual), the attribute of command, prohibition, promise, and threat must be attributed to God. Being the true King requires the power to compel and direct. Therefore, God must be mutakallim.

Key Terms

الأمر والنهي (command and prohibition)
الصفات الواجبة (necessary attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God being mutakallim is optional or metaphorical; it is not a real attribute.
Correction: Juwayni shows it is a necessary attribute based on the reality of divine commands and God's kingship.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does the existence of divine commands and prohibitions necessitate about God?
A) That He is powerful
B) That He is speaking (mutakallim)
C) That He is knowing
D) That He is eternal

Key Takeaway
God's speech is a necessary attribute established by His role as the commanding King.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is necessary because He is the true King, do you treat His commands as the binding decrees of a King, or as mere suggestions? What would change in your daily choices if you truly believed His words are the words of the Sovereign who has absolute authority over you?
?
Juwayni argues that commands and prohibitions are real and not impossible. When you read a prohibition like 'do not approach zina' (Quran 17:32), do you feel the weight of a real prohibition from the King, or do you rationalize it away? Are you willing to obey even when it is difficult?
?
The attribute of speech is necessary for God to be King. If you neglect hearing His speech—the Quran—are you not effectively ignoring the very basis of His kingship over your life? What step will you take today to prioritize listening to His words as the words of the King?

Speech Must Be Eternal: Juwayni's Dilemma
Juwayni argues for the eternity of God's speech via a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's speech cannot be originated and must be an eternal attribute.

Core Idea
God's speech cannot be created because that would make Him a locus of accidents.

In this passage, Juwayni presents a logical dilemma: if speech is an attribute of God, it must be either eternal or originated. He then shows both originated possibilities lead to absurdities, leaving only the eternal position. This argument is central to Sunni theology on the divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Get a feel for Juwayni's tight logical style.
Notice how he sets up the dilemma with a clear 'if...then' structure.
2
Identify the two main options
The passage states that an attribute of God must be either eternal (qadima) or originated (haditha). Look for these terms.
3
Examine the first sub-option
If the attribute is originated and subsists in God, that would make God a locus of accidents. Juwayni rejects this as impossible.
This leads to the conclusion that God is like bodies, which is false.
4
Examine the second sub-option
If the attribute is originated and subsists in a body, then the attribute belongs to that body, not to God. Thus God would not be truly speaking.
This is the Mu'tazilite view, which Juwayni refutes.
5
Conclude the only coherent position
Both originated options fail, so speech must be eternal. This is the stance of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth).
Reflect on how this protects God's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا تقرر أن الكلام صفة للمتكلم، وليس المراد به كونه فاعلا، فما كان صفة لله تعالى لم تخل إما أن تكون حادثة أو قديمة. فإن كانت قديمة فهو الحق الذي اقتحه أهل الحق. وإن كانت حادثة لم تخل، إما أن تقوم به تعالى الله عن قول المبطلين، فيؤدي هذا إلى القول بأنه محل الحوادث. وما قبل الحوادث كالأجسام. وإما أن تقوم بجسم وهو مذهب المخالف. فكل صفة قامت بجسم رجع الحكم منها إلى ذلك الجسم كالحركة والسكون وما عداهما من الأعراض. ولو كان الرب تعالى بخلق كلام في جسم متكلما، لكان بخلق الصوت فيه مصوتا.
And when it is established that speech is an attribute of the speaker, and that what is meant by it is not that he is a doer, then whatever is an attribute of God, exalted, is not free from being either originated (haditha) or eternal (qadima). If it is eternal, that is the truth which the people of truth have affirmed. And if it is originated, it is not free: either it subsists in Him — exalted is God above the saying of the false — and this leads to the saying that He is a locus of accidents, and whatever accepts accidents is like bodies; or it subsists in a body, which is the doctrine of the opponent. And every attribute that subsists in a body, its judgment reverts to that body, like motion and rest and other accidents. And if the Lord, exalted, by creating speech in a body were to be speaking, then by creating sound in it He would be sounding.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents a dilemma. Given that speech is an attribute of the speaker (not merely an act), it must be either eternal or originated. The people of truth affirm it is eternal. If it were originated, it would have to subsist either in God's essence or in a body. It cannot subsist in God because that would imply God is a locus of accidents, which is impossible. If it subsists in a body (the Mu'tazilite view), then the attribute belongs to that body, not to God. For example, if sound is created in a body, that body becomes the sounding one, not God. Thus, the only coherent position is that God's speech is an eternal attribute.

Key Terms
حادثة
قديمة
محل الحوادث
جسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's speech could be created in time and still be His attribute.
Correction: If speech were created, it would either make God a locus of accidents or attribute speech to another object, both of which are impossible.

Checkpoint
What are the two possible options for an originated attribute of God according to Juwayni?
A) It subsists in God or in a body
B) It is eternal or originated
C) It is created in time or before time
D) It is a substance or an accident

Key Takeaway
God's speech must be eternal because any originated attribute would either make God a locus of accidents or belong to a created body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is eternal, then every word of the Quran has existed from before time began. Do you approach the Quran as a timeless address from the Creator, or as a mere book of history? What would change in your recitation, reflection, and obedience if you truly believed each verse was spoken to you from eternity?
?
Juwayni’s dilemma shows that attributing anything created to God leads to absurdity. Yet, in your daily life, do you sometimes project human limitations or temporal qualities onto God in your thoughts? Will you commit to purifying your understanding of God by studying His attributes as the scholars have done?
?
The argument forces a choice: either God’s speech is eternal or it belongs to something else. By your actions, do you treat the Quran as if it is just another created thing—something you can pick up and put down as you please—or as the eternal word that demands your full attention and reverence? What is one step you will take today to honor the speech of God as eternal?

God's Speech: Eternal Attribute, Not Letters or Sounds
Juwayni states the orthodox position on God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Islamic position that God's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence, distinct from created letters and sounds.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not a sequence of letters.

Juwayni presents the final orthodox position on the divine attribute of speech. He distinguishes the Ahl al-Haqq view from those who claim God's speech is composed of letters and sounds. This passage affirms that God's speech is a single, eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that Juwayni begins with 'ثم معتقد أهل الحق' indicating this is the correct belief after refuting false views.
2
Identify what is denied
Juwayni denies that God's speech is 'organized letters' or 'interrupted sounds'. Why are these inappropriate for God?
3
Understand the affirmation
He affirms it is an attribute subsisting in God's essence. What does 'attribute subsisting' mean? How does this differ from created speech?
4
Connect to other attributes
This attribute is eternal like God's other attributes. It indicates command, prohibition, etc. Reflect on how this resolves anthropomorphic ideas.

Source Text

ثم معتقد أهل الحق: أن كلام الله تعالى ليس بحروف منتظمة، ولا أصوات منقطعة، وإنما هو صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى يدل عليها.
Then the belief of the people of truth is that the speech of God, exalted, is not organized letters, nor interrupted sounds, but rather it is an attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted, that indicates.

Commentary
This short passage states the final position. The Ahl al-Haqq (orthodox) affirm that God's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence. It is not composed of letters (huruf) or sounds (aswat) that are sequential and created. Rather, it is a single attribute that subsists in God's essence, and it is what indicates His command, prohibition, etc. This is the doctrine of the Ash'aris and Maturidis.

God's speech is an eternal, non-composite attribute of His essence, not letters or sounds.

Proof that Divine Speech is an Eternal Attribute
Juwayni proves that kalam is an attribute distinct from action and argues for its eternality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that God's attribute of speech is distinct from His action of creating speech, and that this speech must be eternal, not originated.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not merely an action.

Juwayni begins by drawing a distinction between being a speaker (mutakallim) and being an agent (fa'il). Through a simple analogy, he shows that we recognize something as a speaker before considering whether it caused speech. He then applies this to God: if speech were an action, it would be originated, leading to either God being a locus of accidents or speech subsisting in a body—both unacceptable. Therefore, speech must be an eternal attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage begins mid-sentence from a previous page; the argument is self-contained.
2
Identify the analogy
Juwayni uses the example of a moving body and a man speaking. Notice how he distinguishes between recognizing something as 'moving' or 'speaking' and knowing it as an agent of that action.
This analogy is central to establishing that speech is an attribute, not an action.
3
Apply the distinction to God
See how Juwayni concludes that speech is an attribute of God, then argues that it must be either eternal or originated. Follow the disjunctive syllogism.
The argument eliminates both options for originated speech, leaving only eternality.
4
Refute the alternatives
Understand why speech cannot subsist in God (making Him a locus of accidents) nor in a body (making that body the speaker).
This refutes the Mu'tazili position that God creates speech in a body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متكلما، قبل أن يخطر ببالنا كونه فاعلا، ولو لم يكن لكونه متكلما معنى إلا أنه فاعل للكلام لما علمه متكلما من لم يعلمه فاعلا. وليس الأمر كذلك، فإن سبيل معرفة الله تبارك وتعالى متكلما أو سبيل معرفة المتحرك متحركا. ومن رأى جسما يتحرك اعتقد أنه متحرك ولم يتوقف عقله على النظر في أنه فاعل للحركة. كذلك من سمع رجلا اعتقد تكلما ثم نظر في كونه فاعلا للكلام أو غير فاعل. وإذا تقرر أن الكلام صفة للمتكلم وليس المراد به كونه فاعلا، فما كان صفة الله تعالى لم تخل أما أن تكون حادثة أو قديمة. فإن كانت قديمة فهو الحق الذي اقتضه أهل الحق. وإن كانت حادثة لم تخل، إما أن تقوم به - تعالى الله عن قول المبطلين - فيؤدي هذا إلى القول بأنه محل الحوادث. وما قبل الحوادث كالأجسام. وإما أن تقوم بجسم - وهو مذهب المخالف. فكل صفة قامت بجسم رجع الحكم منها إلى ذلك الجسم كالحركة والسكون وما عداهما من الأعراض. ولو كان الرب تبارك وتعالى بخلق كلام في جسم متكلما، لكان بخلق الصوت فيه مصوتا.
Mutakalliman, before it occurs to our mind that He is an agent. And if being mutakallim had no meaning except that He is an agent of speech, then one who does not know Him as an agent would not know Him as mutakallim. But the matter is not like that. For the way of knowing Allah—blessed and exalted is He—as mutakallim is like the way of knowing a moving thing as moving. One who sees a body moving believes it is moving, and his mind does not stop to consider whether it is an agent of movement. Likewise, one who hears a man believes him to be mutakallim, then considers whether he is an agent of speech or not. And when it is established that speech is an attribute of the speaker and that what is meant by it is not that he is an agent, then whatever is an attribute of Allah—exalted is He—cannot but be either originated or eternal. If it is eternal, then that is the truth which the people of truth have adopted. And if it is originated, it cannot but either subsist in Him—exalted is Allah above the saying of the falsifiers—leading to the statement that He is a locus of accidents. And whatever accepts accidents is like bodies. Or it subsists in a body—and that is the doctrine of the opponent. For every attribute that subsists in a body, its judgment refers back to that body, like motion, rest, and other accidents. And if the Lord—blessed and exalted is He—were mutakallim by creating speech in a body, then by creating sound in it He would be a sound-maker.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's attribute of speech (kalam) is not merely His action of creating speech, but a real attribute subsisting in His essence, and that it is eternal, not originated. Juwayni begins with an epistemological point: we can know that something is a 'speaker' (mutakallim) without first knowing it as an 'agent' (fa'il) of speech. He gives the analogy of a moving body: one who sees a body moving immediately believes it is 'moving' without needing to consider whether it is the agent of the movement. Similarly, one who hears a man speaking immediately believes him to be a speaker, and only subsequently considers whether he is the agent of the speech. Thus, being a speaker and being an agent are conceptually distinct. From this it follows that 'speech' is an attribute of the speaker, not the mere fact of being an agent. Juwayni then applies this to God: if God's speech is an attribute, it must be either originated (hadith) or eternal (qadim). The Ash'ari position, which Juwayni defends, is that it is eternal. He argues that if it were originated, it would have to either subsist in God's essence (making Him a locus of accidents, which is impossible and reduces Him to a body) or subsist in a body (the Mu'tazili view). But an attribute subsisting in a body redounds to that body, not to God. For example, if God created speech in a body, then that body would be the speaker, not God. Thus, the only coherent position is that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

Key Terms
كلام
متكلم
فاعل
حادث
قديم
صفة
محل الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'God speaks' means He creates speech in a body (like the Angel or the Tablet), so that body becomes the speaker.
Correction: Juwayni argues that if God created speech in a body, that body would be the speaker (since attributes refer to their substrate), not God. Thus, God's speech must be an eternal attribute in His essence.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni's argument, why can we know something as a 'speaker' without first knowing it as an 'agent'?
A) Because being a speaker is a separate attribute from being an agent, as seen in the analogy of a moving body.
B) Because all speakers are also agents, so one implies the other.
C) Because God's names are all identical in meaning.
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly states that God's speech is an action.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute inhering in His essence, not a created action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you recognize that you are uttering words that are not merely a created message from God but an expression of an eternal attribute of His essence? How does this change the weight of each verse upon your heart? Pause before your next recitation and consciously remind yourself: 'These words are eternal; they are of God Himself.'
?
If God's speech is an eternal attribute, then every command, prohibition, and promise in the Quran is not a temporary decree but an unchanging reality. Is there a command of God in the Quran that you have been treating as optional or outdated? Confront that command now and ask yourself: will you obey it as an eternal obligation from an eternal Speaker?
?
Juwayni's argument shows that thinking of God's speech as created leads to absurdities. Yet in your daily life, you might act as if God's words are merely human interpretations or cultural artifacts. Where have you allowed yourself to relativize the Quran's authority? Commit this week to reading one verse as if God is speaking it to you directly, right now, for the first time.

God's Speech as an Eternal Attribute
Juwayni states the positive doctrine of divine speech as an eternal attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Ash'ari theology, God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinct from the created letters and sounds of the recited Qur'an.

Core Idea
God's speech is single and eternal; the Qur'an points to it but is not identical.

Juwayni opens a positive statement of the Ash'ari belief about divine speech. He clarifies what God's speech is not—neither ordered letters nor discrete sounds—and then affirms what it truly is: a permanent attribute of God. This passage also explains how the recited Qur'an functions as a sign of that uncreated speech, using a simple analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: negation first, then affirmation, then an analogy.
The passage is one sentence but packs a complete doctrine.
2
Identify the negations
Juwayni begins by stating what God's speech is NOT: not ordered letters, not separated sounds. Understand why these are denied: they imply temporality and composition.
Letters and sounds are created, changing, and accidental.
3
Grasp the affirmation
God's speech is an attribute subsisting in His essence. It is one, eternal, and not divisible into parts. This is the core of the Ash'ari position.
This attribute is not a creation; it is inseparable from God.
4
Understand the analogy
Juwayni compares the Qur'an recitation to a person's statement that indicates a meaning. The recited Qur'an points to the eternal speech, just as words point to their meaning.
The analogy shows the relationship: sign and signified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم معتقد أهل الحق: أن كلام الله تعالى ليس بحروف منتظمة، ولا أصوات منقطعة، وإنما هو صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى يدل عليها قراءة القرآن كما يدل قول القائل: على الوجود الأزلي، والمفهوم منه: الرب تبارك وتعالى.
Then the belief of the people of truth is that the speech of Allah—exalted is He—is not composed of ordered letters nor separated sounds. Rather, it is an attribute subsisting in His essence—exalted is He—indicated by the recitation of the Qur'an, just as the saying of the speaker indicates: concerning the preeternal existence, and what is understood from it is the Lord—blessed and exalted is He.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a positive statement of the Ash'ari position (the 'people of truth') regarding the nature of God's speech. Juwayni affirms that God's speech is not made up of letters arranged in sequence nor discrete sounds that occur one after another. Instead, it is a single, indivisible attribute that subsists in God's essence. This eternal speech is not directly perceived; rather, it is indicated (dalil) by the recitation of the Qur'an. Juwayni gives an analogy: just as someone's saying something (e.g., a statement about preeternal existence) points to the meaning intended, so the recited Qur'an points to the eternal speech of God. The understood referent of the Qur'anic recitation is the Lord Himself, i.e., His eternal attribute of speech. This establishes that the Qur'an in recitation is created, but it signifies the uncreated attribute.

Key Terms
كلام الله
حروف
أصوات
صفة قائمة بالذات
قراءة القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the recited Qur'an (the Arabic words) is exactly identical to God's eternal speech.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the recited Qur'an is a created sign (dalil) that points to the uncreated attribute of speech; they are not identical.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the relationship between the recited Qur'an and God's eternal speech?
A) The recited Qur'an is exactly identical to the eternal speech.
B) The recited Qur'an is a created sign that indicates the eternal attribute of speech.
C) The recited Qur'an is a part of the eternal speech.
D) The recited Qur'an is an accident in God's essence.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute; the recited Qur'an is a created sign that points to it, not the attribute itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is one eternal attribute, then every verse you recite points to that single reality. When you read the Qur'an, are you truly connecting with the eternal Speech of your Lord, or do you treat it as mere words on a page? What would change in your recitation if you were fully aware that each ayah is a sign pointing to the very attribute of the One who spoke it?
?
Juwayni says divine speech is not letters or sounds. That means the Qur'an you memorize in Arabic is a created expression of something far greater. Does this humble you, or do you take pride in your recitation as if it were your own achievement? How can you let this truth transform your relationship with the Qur'an?
?
The analogy given compares the recited Qur'an to a speaker's utterance indicating his inner meaning. If you were to examine your own speech, does it always point to truth? Are there words you speak that contradict the eternal attribute of truth? How can you align your speech with the reality that God's speech is perfect and eternal?
