Answering the Objection of Eternal Command before Existence
Juwayni answers the objection that an eternal command implies the existence of the commanded before it exists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni defends the eternal nature of God's command despite the non-existence of the commanded beings at the time of command.

Core Idea
God's eternal command is a dispositional readiness, not a temporal occurrence.

This lesson addresses a classic objection in Islamic theology: if God's speech is eternal, then His commands and prohibitions would be eternal, yet the beings to be commanded did not yet exist. Juwayni responds by drawing an analogy from human psychology and comparing eternal command to eternal power. The passage you are about to read shows how the eternal attribute of command does not require the present existence of the commanded.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Begin by reading the objection stated at the start of the passage. The opponent claims that an eternal command before the existence of the commanded is impossible.
Notice the key term 'muhal' (impossible) – this is a strong claim.
2
Understand Juwayni's analogy
Juwayni gives an example from human psychology: a person who resolves to speak later already has the meanings in his soul. Reflect on how this analogy applies to God.
The analogy uses the concept of 'ma'ani' (meanings) existing in the soul before utterance.
3
Connect the analogy to divine attributes
Juwayni compares God's eternal speech to His eternal power. Just as power is eternal yet its objects are created later, so speech is eternal yet its commanded beings are created later.
This comparison shows the consistency of divine attributes.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question. It will reinforce the main point of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل: إذا قضيتم بأن كلام الله تبارك وتعالى أزلي لزمكم أن تصفوه بكونه آمرا ناهيا قبل وجود المخاطبين، وثبوت الأمر قبل وجود المأمورين: محال. قلنا: ما لبس به المخالف يدرأه ضرب مثال. وهو: أن من بعزم على مفاوضه صاحب له بعد شهر، فالمعاني التي سيوردها عند جريان الجواز يجدها بأعيانها قائمة في نفسه، ثم إذا حان الوقت أداها، فأنهاها والعالم بأنه سيكلم فلانا لا تخلو نفسه عن وجود ثبوت ذلك الكلام على تقدير وجوده في العبارات من حين المفاوضة تبلغ تلك المعاني والرب في أزله كان عالما بأنه يتعبد عباده إذا وجدوا وهو العالم المقدس عن أن يسهو أو يهفو، فلا يخلو وجوده الأزلي عن معنى ما سيصل إلى العباد إذا وجدوا. وسبيل ذلك الكلام القائم بنفسه كسبيل قدرته القديمة ولم تزل. وإن كان يستحيل وجود مقدوراتها، فالمقدور حادث مستفتح ولكنه كان منعوتا أزلا بصفة صالحة لتعلق القدرة بالمقدورات فيما لا يزال.
For it is said: If you have judged that the speech of Allah—blessed and exalted is He—is preeternal, it would necessitate that you describe Him as commanding and prohibiting before the existence of the addressed. And the establishment of a command before the existence of the commanded is impossible. We say: What the opponent has confused is removed by giving an example. That is: One who resolves to converse with his companion after a month, the meanings that he will produce at the time of the occurrence of the occasion finds them actually existing in his soul. Then when the time comes, he produces them and completes them. And the one who knows that he will speak to so-and-so—his soul is not devoid of the fixed existence of that speech upon the assumption of its existence in expressions from the time of the conversation. Those meanings reach [the addressee]. And the Lord in His preeternity was knowing that He would worship His servants when they exist—and He is the Holy One, far above forgetfulness or error. So His preeternal existence is not devoid of the meaning of what will reach the servants when they exist. And the way of that speech subsisting in His essence is like the way of His preeternal power—it has not ceased. And even if the existence of its objects of power is impossible, the object of power is originated and begun, but it was described preeternally with an attribute fit for the attachment of power to objects of power in the future.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair dealing with a classic problem: if God's speech is eternal, then His commands and prohibitions would be eternal, yet the beings commanded (e.g., angels, humans) did not yet exist. How can there be a command before there is someone to command? Juwayni begins with the objection stated succinctly: an eternal command before the existence of the commanded is impossible (muhal). His response uses an analogy drawn from human psychology. Consider a person who resolves to have a conversation with a friend a month from now. The meanings (ma'ani) that he will later express in words are already present in his soul (nafs) — they have a kind of fixed existence there. He knows he will speak, so his soul is not empty of those meanings, even though they are not yet uttered. Similarly, God in His preeternity knew that He would address His servants when they come into existence, and His knowledge is free from forgetfulness or error. Thus, His preeternal essence is not devoid of the meaning (ma'na) of what will later be conveyed to the servants. The eternal speech subsisting in God's essence is analogous to His eternal power: God's power is eternal, yet its objects (mawjudat) are created later. The power is described preeternally as being fit to attach to future objects. So the eternal attribute of command does not require the current existence of the commanded; it is a preparation (salahiyya) for commanding when the time comes.

نهي
المأمور
المخاطب
أزلي
كلام نفسي
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal command would be absurd because it demands a present addressee.
Correction: The eternal attribute is a dispositional readiness (salahiyya) in God's essence, not a temporal occurrence requiring the current existence of the commanded.

Checkpoint
How does Juwayni analogize God's eternal command with human psychology?
A) He compares it to a king issuing a decree before his subjects exist.
B) He compares it to a person who resolves to speak later, with the meanings already present in his soul.
C) He compares it to a sword that is sharp before it cuts.
D) He compares it to a law that is written before it is enforced.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal command is not a temporal utterance but a dispositional meaning in His essence, analogous to His eternal power being ready to create objects in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that God's command to you was eternally ready before you were born. What does that imply for your resistance to obeying a command you find difficult? Can you still claim it's 'not the right time'?
?
If God's eternal attribute of command is like a dispositional readiness, what does that say about your own intentions? Are your resolutions to obey merely temporary, or do you cultivate a steadfast disposition like the one described in this lesson?
?
The lesson compares eternal command to eternal power—both are ready before their objects exist. How does this shape your trust that God's plan for you, even if not yet visible, is already settled and effective? Will you rely on that readiness today?

Hearing the Qur'an: Sound or Speech?
Juwayni clarifies the sense in which God's speech is heard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the eternal speech of Allah and the created sound heard during recitation, and why both are affirmed.

Core Idea
We hear the reciter's sound; we understand God's eternal speech.

Juwayni addresses a subtle but crucial point: when we say we 'hear' the Qur'an, what exactly is being perceived? The answer guards against two extremes: denying that God's speech is heard, or imagining that the eternal attribute itself becomes audible sound. This short passage clarifies the Ash'ari position with precision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms: مسموع, مدرك, صوت القارئ, المفهوم.
The passage is cut off at the end, but the core idea is complete.
2
Identify the two senses of 'hearing'
Juwayni first affirms that God's speech is heard (masmu'). Then he clarifies what this does NOT mean: direct perception of the eternal attribute. Instead, what is perceived is the sound of the reciter.
The distinction is between the physical sound and the eternal meaning.
3
Understand the role of 'understanding'
Juwayni says that what is understood (al-mafhum) from the recitation is God's speech. The sound is a vehicle for the divine message.
This preserves the reverence for the Qur'an as God's speech while acknowledging the created nature of the recitation.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding with the multiple-choice question. This will reinforce the key distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب اطلاق القول بأن كلام الله تبارك وتعالى مسموع، وليس المراد بذلك تعلق الادراك بالكلام الأزلي القائم بالبارى تعالى. ولكن المدرك صوت القارىء. والمفهوم عند قراءته كلام الله سبحانه، ولا بعد في
It is necessary to declare that the speech of Allah—blessed and exalted is He—is heard. But what is meant by that is not the attachment of perception to the preeternal speech subsisting in the Creator—exalted is He. Rather, what is perceived is the sound of the reciter. And what is understood at the time of its recitation is the speech of Allah—glorified is He. And there is no harm in...
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a definition and clarification of the sense in which God's speech is said to be 'heard'. Juwayni affirms that it is necessary to say that God's speech is heard (masmu'), but with an important qualification: this does not mean that the eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence is directly perceived by the senses. Rather, what is actually perceived (al-mudrak) is the sound (sawt) of the reciter (al-qari'). Yet, what is understood (al-mafhum) from the recitation is indeed the speech of God. In other words, the physical sound is created, but it signifies and conveys the uncreated attribute. Juwayni leaves the sentence incomplete ('and there is no harm in...'), likely to continue with the explanation that there is no harm in saying 'I heard the speech of God' metaphorically or in a qualified sense, since the listener perceives the created expression that points to the eternal meaning.

صوت القارىء
المفهوم

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Juwayni clarifies that what is actually perceived by hearing is the created sound of the reciter, not the eternal attribute. The eternal attribute is not a sound; it is a meaning subsisting in God's essence.

Checkpoint

B) The sound of the reciter, which indicates the eternal speech.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni distinguishes the created sound heard in recitation from the eternal speech of Allah, affirming that we hear the former but understand the latter.

Are you careful to understand what you recite, or do you rush through the words? Commit to one change in your daily recitation habit.

Answering the Objection to Eternal Speech
Juwayni presents an objection to God's eternal speech and provides an analogy-based answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni defends the eternal nature of God’s speech against the objection that it would imply commanding and prohibiting before any addressees exist.

Core Idea
Eternal speech includes potential commanding, not actual commanding.

Juwayni now faces a sharp objection: if God’s speech is eternal, then He must be eternally commanding and prohibiting—before any creatures exist, which seems impossible. He answers with a powerful analogy from human intention. Let’s see how he resolves this.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection that if God's speech is eternal, it would require Him to be described as commanding and prohibiting before any addressees exist. Note the claim that this is impossible.
The objector uses 'محال' (impossible) to emphasize the apparent contradiction.
2
Examine Juwayni's analogy
Juwayni gives an example of a person who intends to speak with a friend after a month. The meanings of the speech are already present in his soul. Then, notice how Juwayni applies this to God: God knew He would address His servants when they exist, so the meanings are eternally present in His speech.
The analogy shows that potential commanding is compatible with eternity.
3
Connect to God's eternal attributes
Juwayni compares the eternal speech to God's eternal power: power is eternally described as suitable for creating, even before any created things exist. Similarly, speech is eternally suitable for commanding.
This reinforces the idea that attributes are described as potential in eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قراءة القرآن كما يدل قول القائل (۱) : على الوجود الأزلي (۳) ، ) ويعتبر المسمى : أصوات (۳) ( والمفهوم منه : الرب تبارك وتعالى .. فان قيل : اذا قضيتم بأن كلام الله تبارك وتعالى أزلي . لزمكم أن تصفوه بكونه آمرا ناهيا قبل وجود المخاطبين ، وثبوت الأمر قبل وجود المأمورين : محال . قلنا : ما لبس به المخالف يدرأه ضرب مثال . وهو : أن من بعزم على مفاوضه صاحب له بعد شهر ، فالمعانى التي سيوردها عند جريان الجواز يجدها بأعيانها قائمة فى نفسه ، ثم اذا حان الوقت أداها ، فأنهاها والعالم بأنه سيكلم فلانا لا تخلو نفسه عن وجود ثبوت ذلك الكلام على تقدير وجوده فى العبارات من حين المفاوضة تبلغ تلك المعانى والرب فى أزله كان عالما بأنه يتعبد عباده اذا وجدوا وهو العالم المقدس عن ان يسهو أو يهفو ، فلا يخلو وجوده الأزلى عن معنى ما سيصل الى العباد اذا وجدوا . وسبيل ذلك الكلام القائم بنفسه . كسبيل قدرته القديمة ولم تزل . وان كان يستحيل وجود مقدوراتها .. أراد (٤) فان المقدور حادث مستفتح ولكنه كان منعونا أزلا بصفة صالحة لتعلق القدرة بالمقدورات فيما لا يزال .
The recitation of the Quran as indicated by the saying of the speaker: upon eternal existence, and it is considered named: sounds, and what is understood from it: the Lord, Blessed and Exalted. For if it is said: Since you have judged that the speech of God, Blessed and Exalted, is eternal, it follows that you describe Him as commanding and prohibiting before the existence of those addressed, and the establishment of the command before the existence of those commanded is impossible. We say: What the opponent confuses is repelled by giving an example. That is: One who intends to converse with his companion after a month, the meanings he will deliver when the occasion arises he finds precisely standing in his soul, then when the time comes he delivers them, so he performs them, and the one who knows that he will speak to so-and-so does not lack his soul having the existence of that speech upon the assumption of its existence in expressions from the time of the conversation conveys those meanings. And the Lord in His eternity was knowing that He would worship His servants when they exist, and He is the knowledge sanctified from forgetfulness or mistake. So His eternal existence is not devoid of the meaning of what will reach the servants when they exist. And the way of that speech subsisting in Himself is like the way of His ancient power, unceasing. Even if the existence of its objects of power is impossible... He intended, for the object of power is originated, beginning, but it was eternally described with a quality suitable for the attachment of power to objects of power in what is to come.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format. The objector argues: If you (the Ash'ari school) maintain that God's speech is eternal, then you must also say that God is eternally commanding and prohibiting before any addressees exist, and that a command before the existence of the commanded is impossible. Juwayni responds by drawing an analogy: A person who intends to speak with a friend after a month already has the meanings of his speech present in his soul. When the time comes, he utters them. Similarly, God in His eternity knew that He would address His servants when they exist. His eternal self is not devoid of the meaning of what will later be expressed. Juwayni then analogizes this to God's eternal power: Even if no originated objects of power exist eternally, God's power is eternally described as being suitable to attach to objects of power when they come into existence. Thus, the eternal attribute of speech includes the potential for commanding and prohibiting, not their actual occurrence before addressees exist.

How God's Speech is Heard: Meaning and Metaphor
Juwayni clarifies that 'God's speech is heard' does not mean hearing the eternal attribute, but hearing the recited sound and understanding the meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that when we say God's speech is heard, it refers to hearing the recited sounds and understanding the meaning, not perceiving the eternal attribute directly.

Core Idea
Hearing God's speech is understood metaphorically through the recited sounds, not the eternal attribute.

Juwayni clarifies a common misunderstanding about hearing God's speech. He affirms that the Quran is heard, but not in the sense that the eternal attribute itself is perceived. Instead, what is heard is the reciter's voice, and the meaning understood is God's speech. This lesson unpacks his argument and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice Juwayni's careful phrasing to avoid misunderstanding.
2
Identify the clarification
Find where Juwayni states what is meant and not meant by 'heard'. He says 'ليس المراد بذلك تعلق الادراك بالكلام الأزلى' — that is the negation.
The positive explanation follows: 'المدرك صوت القارىء'.
3
Examine the king's analogy
Read the analogy of the king's message. Understand how it parallels hearing God's speech: the messenger conveys the message, but the king's own voice is not heard.
Juwayni uses this to show it is proper to say 'I heard the king' meaning I understood his message.
4
Apply the Moses example
Note that Juwayni says anyone who claims to hear God without an intermediary is like Moses. This reinforces that direct hearing is exceptional.
This also shows that ordinary hearing of the Quran is mediated through recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب اطلاق القول بأن كلام الله تبارك وتعالى مسموع ، وليس المراد بذلك تعلق الادراك بالكلام الأزلى القائم بالبارى تعالى . ولكن المدرك صوت القارىء . والمفهوم عند قراءته كلام الله سبحانه ، ولا بعد في تسمية المفهوم عند مسموع : مسموعا ، فهذا بمثابة ما لو بلغ مبلغ رسالة ملك فيحسن ممن بلغته الرسالة أن يقول : سمعت الملك ورسالته . وكلام الملك حديث نفسه وأصواته .. ومن بلغ الرسالة لم ينقل صوت مرسله ولا حديث نفسه أنه ومن زعم سمع كلام الله تعالى من غير واسطة ، فلا فرق بينه وبين موسى عليه السلام تبارى وتعالى من بين عالمى ازی خصصه زمانه بتكليمه . واصطفاه باستماعه عزيز كلامه .
It is necessary to apply the statement that the speech of God, Blessed and Exalted, is heard. But what is meant by that is not the attachment of perception to the eternal speech subsisting in the Exalted. Rather, what is perceived is the sound of the reciter. And the understood meaning when reciting it is the speech of God, Glorified. And there is no far-fetchedness in naming the understood meaning when heard as 'heard'. This is like the case of one who receives the message of a king; it is proper for the one who received the message to say: I heard the king and his message. And the speech of the king is his inner thoughts and his sounds. And the one who conveyed the message did not transmit the sound of the sender nor his inner thoughts. And whoever claims to have heard the speech of God, Exalted, without an intermediary, there is no difference between him and Moses, peace be upon him, whom the Exalted specially chose from among the worlds by addressing him and chose him for hearing His precious speech.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a clarification (tafsir) of the statement 'God's speech is heard.' Juwayni begins by stating that it is necessary to affirm that God's speech is heard, but not in the sense that the eternal attribute itself is perceived by hearing. Rather, what is perceived is the sound of the reciter, and what is understood from that recitation is God's speech. There is no problem in calling that understood meaning 'heard' metaphorically. He gives an analogy: If a king's message is delivered, the recipient can properly say 'I heard the king and his message,' even though he did not hear the king's own voice or thoughts. Similarly, when one hears the Quran recited, it is as if he hears God's speech. Then Juwayni adds that anyone who claims to have heard God's speech without an intermediary (i.e., directly) is no different from Moses, whom God specially chose to address directly. This implies that only prophets like Moses can hear God's speech directly; for others, it is through recitation.

Key Terms
مسموع
مدرك
صوت القارىء
مفهوم
رسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that when we say we hear God's speech, we hear the eternal attribute itself.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies we hear the recited sounds and understand the meaning, which is metaphorically called hearing God's speech.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, in what sense is God's speech said to be heard?
A) The eternal attribute of speech is directly perceived by the ear
B) The sound of the reciter is heard, and the meaning understood is God's speech
C) Only Moses heard God's speech, so the statement is false for others
D) The written letters in the mushaf are heard

Key Takeaway
When Muslims say they hear God's speech, they mean they hear the recited Quran and understand its meaning, not that they perceive the eternal attribute directly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you truly believed that the understood meaning of the Quran is God's speech to you personally, what would you change about the way you read, memorize, or apply it? Are you willing to make that change starting today?

God's Speech in Mushafs: Presence Without Dwelling
Juwayni affirms the written nature of God's speech while denying its physical indwelling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni distinguishes between God's eternal speech and its written/recited forms, and why it is a mistake to think the attribute dwells in physical objects.

Core Idea
God's speech is truly written in mushafs, but as His eternal attribute, it does not physically reside in them.

Juwayni addresses a critical point: the Quran we recite and write is truly God's speech, yet we must not imagine that God's eternal attribute moves or dwells in created matter. This lesson clarifies the subtle distinction between the eternal kalam and its written/recited manifestations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice Juwayni's concise style and the shift from doctrinal statement to historical critique.
2
Identify the three affirmations and one negation
Juwayni affirms that God's speech is written in mushafs, recited by tongues, and preserved in hearts. Then he immediately negates that it dwells in these places as accidents dwell in bodies.
The negation is crucial: 'wa la yahillu' means 'it does not indwell'.
3
Understand the reason for the negation
The reason given is that the eternal speech does not depart from God's essence nor separate from it. Change and movement are attributes of bodies, not of the Eternal.
This is a rational argument: what is eternal cannot change place or undergo transformation.
4
Learn from the historical example
Juwayni recounts the confusion during Imam Ahmad's time when ignorant people heard that God's speech is in the mushafs and wrongly concluded that the eternal speech itself existed inside the physical books.
This highlights the danger of taking statements literally without proper theological framework.
5
Reflect on the lesson's application
Consider how this teaching guards against corporealism: the attribute of speech is not a physical entity that can be located in space.
The principle applies to all divine attributes: they are not like created things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام الله تبارك وتعالى مكتوب في المصاحف ، مقروء بالألسنة ، محفوظ فى الصدور ولا يحل الكلام هذه المحال حلول الأعراض الجواهر . فإن كلام الله الأزلي (۱) لا يفارق الذات ولا يزايلها ، ومن شد طرفا من قضايا العقول لم يسترب فى أن التحول والانتقال والزوال من صفات الأجسام ، ومن الغوائل التى بلى الخلق بها ، أن القول في قدم كلام الله تبارك وتعالى ، وكونه مكتوبا في المصاحف أشبع في زمن الامام أحمد بن حنبل - رحمه الله - من جهلة العوام والرعاع الهمج ، وضرب من لا دراية له بالكلام فى هذا الأصل ، فسمعوا مطلقا : أن كلام الله فى المصاحف ، فسبقوا الى اعتقاد ثبوت وجود الكلام الأزلي فى الدفاتر وارتبكوا في جهالات (۲) لا يبوء بها محصل تطاول الدهر .
The speech of God, Blessed and Exalted, is written in the mushafs, recited by tongues, preserved in breasts, and speech does not indwell these places as accidents indwell in bodies. For the eternal speech of God does not depart from the Essence nor separate from it. And whoever has taken a glance at rational matters will not doubt that transformation, transfer, and removal are among the attributes of bodies. And among the calamities with which creation has been tested is that the discussion concerning the eternity of the speech of God, Blessed and Exalted, and its being written in the mushafs became widespread in the time of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal - may God have mercy on him - among the ignorant commoners and the rabble of the mob, and a group with no knowledge of kalam regarding this principle. They heard absolutely that the speech of God is in the mushafs, so they rushed to the belief in the established existence of the eternal speech in books, and they became entangled in ignorances from which no accomplished person would benefit for a long time.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an assertion and a refutation of a misunderstanding. Juwayni first affirms that God's speech is written in mushafs (physical copies of the Quran), recited by tongues, and preserved in hearts. However, he immediately clarifies that this does not mean the speech (the eternal attribute) physically dwells in these places as accidents dwell in bodies. The eternal speech is an attribute of God's essence; it does not separate from Him or move. He then notes that it is a rational certainty that movement and change are properties of bodies. Juwayni then critiques the historical controversy during the time of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, when ignorant commoners and those lacking knowledge of kalam heard the statement 'God's speech is in the mushafs' in an unqualified sense. They wrongly assumed that the eternal speech itself exists within the physical books, leading to confusion and errors. Juwayni implies that such crude literalism is a 'calamity' and that the correct understanding requires distinguishing between the eternal speech (God's attribute) and its created expressions (the recited and written Quran).

Key Terms
مكتوب في المصاحف
حلول
الأزلي
ذات
أجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's eternal speech literally resides inside the physical mushafs as a substance would dwell in a container.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the speech is written, recited, and memorized, but as an eternal attribute of God, it does not dwell in created objects or change location.

Checkpoint
What mistake did the ignorant people in the time of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal make regarding God's speech being in the mushafs?
A) They denied that the Quran is written in mushafs
B) They believed the eternal speech literally existed inside the physical books
C) They claimed the Quran was created
D) They rejected the concept of eternal speech entirely

Key Takeaway
Juwayni teaches that God's eternal speech is written and recited, but as an attribute of His essence, it does not physically dwell in created objects.

Hearing God's Speech: Direct or Through an Intermediary?
Juwayni clarifies what it means to hear divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni distinguishes between hearing God's speech directly and hearing it through an intermediary, and why ordinary believers hear via prophets.

Core Idea
Hearing a message is not the same as hearing the speaker's voice directly.

Juwayni addresses a subtle point: when we hear the Qur'an recited, do we hear God's speech directly? He clarifies using the analogy of a king's message. This passage lays the foundation for understanding divine speech and prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, noting its structure. Then read the literal translation. Be aware that the Arabic is partially corrupt due to OCR issues, but the main argument is clear.
The beginning 'تسمية المفهوم عند مسموع' may be garbled; focus on the king analogy.
2
Identify the analogy and its parts
Find the analogy of the king and his messenger. Note that hearing the messenger's report is considered hearing the king indirectly. Understand that the king's speech consists of inner speech and sounds, which are not conveyed by the messenger.
3
Understand the special case of Moses
Juwayni mentions Moses as one who heard God's speech directly without an intermediary. Recognize that this is exceptional and a mark of prophethood, not a general experience.
This guards against the misconception that ordinary recitation is direct divine speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تسمية المفهوم عند مسموع عند مسموع : مسموعا ، فهذا بمثابة ما لو بلغ مبلغ رسالة ملك فيحسن ممن بلغته الرسالة أن يقول : سمعت الملك ورسالته . وكلام الملك حديث نفسه وأصواته .. ومن بلغ الرسالة لم ينقل صوت مرسله ولا حديث نفسه أنه ومن زعم سمع كلام الله تعالى من غير واسطة ، فلا فرق بينه ويين موسى عليه السلام تبارى وتعالى من بين عالمى ازی خصصه زمانه بتكليمه . واصطفاه باستماعه عزيز كلامه .
Naming the concept of what is heard: hearing, so this is like the case when a message of a king reaches a person, then it is fitting for the one who received the message to say: I heard the king and his message. And the king's speech is his inner speech and his sounds. And the one who delivered the message did not convey the sound of the sender nor his inner speech. And whoever claims to have heard the speech of God Almighty without an intermediary, then there is no difference between him and Moses, peace be upon him, who is exalted and high above the worlds, He specially distinguished him by addressing him and chose him by hearing His mighty speech.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an argument clarifying the concept of hearing divine speech. Juwayni begins by explaining that when a person receives a message from a king, he can say 'I heard the king and his message' even though he did not hear the king's actual voice. The king's speech consists of his inner speech (hadith nafs) and his sounds. The messenger only conveys the message, not the king's actual sounds or inner speech. Similarly, hearing God's speech through a prophet is comparable. Juwayni then states that whoever claims to hear God's speech without any intermediary is like Moses, whom God specially distinguished by direct address. However, the implication is that such a claim requires prophetic rank, and ordinary people cannot claim it. The passage guards against equating the ordinary experience of hearing the Qur'an recited with hearing God's speech directly.

Key Terms
كلام الله (divine speech)
واسطة (intermediary)
مسموع (what is heard)
حديث النفس (inner speech)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that hearing the recitation of the Qur'an is hearing God's speech directly.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that hearing through a messenger (or reciter) is indirect. Direct hearing is exclusive to prophets like Moses.

Checkpoint
What is the example Juwayni gives to explain that hearing a message is like hearing the speaker indirectly?
A) A king and his messenger
B) Moses and God
C) The Quran and its recitation
D) A teacher and a student

Key Takeaway
Hearing God's speech through a prophet is like hearing a king's message through a messenger; it is not the same as direct hearing, which is reserved for prophets like Moses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you listen to the Qur'an recited, do you ever catch yourself feeling as though you are hearing Allah's actual voice? How does Juwayni's analogy of the king's message change your perception of that experience? What will you do the next time you listen to the Qur'an to remind yourself of this truth?
?
If direct hearing of God's speech is a privilege reserved for prophets like Moses, how does that affect your humility in approaching the Qur'an? Does it make you more grateful for the indirect access we have, or more longing for direct communion? How can you cultivate both gratitude and longing?
?
The passage says one who claims direct hearing 'equates himself to Moses'. Have you ever, even subtly, thought your spiritual experiences put you on par with the prophets? How does this warning pierce your self-image? What specific change in your attitude toward your own spirituality must this truth force?

Divine Speech: Written in Musahif but Not by Indwelling
Juwayni defines the orthodox position on divine speech and refutes the indwelling misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Juwayni insists that God's eternal speech is written in the Musahif but does not physically indwell them.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal and inseparable from His essence; it does not move into books.

This lesson examines a key passage from Juwayni's al-Aqida al-Nizamiyya where he clarifies the nature of the Quran as God's speech. He affirms that the Quran is written, recited, and memorized, but strongly denies that the eternal attribute of speech resides in these physical mediums. Juwayni critiques those who misunderstood this point, particularly during the Mihna era.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp Juwayni's precise wording.
Notice the strong negation: 'لا يحل الكلام هذه المحال'.
2
Identify the three affirmations and one negation
Juwayni affirms that divine speech is written, recited, and memorized. He then negates that it indwells these places like accidents in substances.
3
Understand the rational proof
Juwayni argues that eternal speech does not separate from God's essence; change and transfer are attributes of bodies, not of the Creator.
This is the key rational argument against indwelling.
4
Analyze the historical context
Juwayni criticizes the Hashwiyya and ignorant commoners during Imam Ahmad's time who misunderstood 'in the Musahif' as physical indwelling.
Reflect on why this error is a 'calamity' in his view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كلام الله تبارك وتعالى مكتوب في المصاحف ، مقروء بالألسنة ، محفوظ فى الصدور ولا يحل الكلام هذه المحال حلول الأعراض الجواهر . فإن كلام الله الأزلي لا يفارق الذات ولا يزايلها ، ومن شد طرفا من قضايا العقول لم يسترب فى أن التحول والانتقال والزوال من صفات الأجسام ، ومن الغوائل التى بلى الخلق بها ، أن القول في قدم كلام الله تبارك وتعالى ، وكونه مكتوبا في المصاحف أشبع في زمن الامام أحمد بن حنبل - رحمه الله - من جهلة العوام والرعاع الهمج ، وضرب من لا دراية له بالكلام فى هذا الأصل ، فسمعوا مطلقا : أن كلام الله فى المصاحف ، فسبقوا الى اعتقاد ثبوت وجود الكلام الأزلي فى الدفاتر وارتبكوا في جهالات لا يبوء بها محصل تطاول الدهر . وتمادى العصر ، فرسخ هذا الكلام فى قلوب الحشوية ، ولولا ذلك لما خفى على من معه مسكة من عقل : أن الكلام لا ينتقل من متكلم الى دفتر .
Chapter: The speech of God Almighty is written in the Musahif (copies of the Quran), recited by tongues, preserved in hearts, and it does not take up these places by the indwelling of accidents in substances. For the eternal speech of God does not separate from the Essence nor does it leave it. And whoever stretches his glance into the matters of the intellects will not doubt that change, transfer, and departure are attributes of bodies. And among the calamities that afflicted creation is that the saying about the pre-eternity of God's speech and that it is written in the Musahif became widespread in the time of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may God have mercy on him, among the ignorant commoners and the rabble, and that sort who have no knowledge of kalam on this matter. They heard absolutely that God's speech is in the Musahif, so they rushed to believe in the existence of the eternal speech in the books and became entangled in ignorances from which no accomplished person would ever exculpate himself, no matter how long time passed. And then the age continued and this talk became ingrained in the hearts of the Hashwiyya. Were it not for that, it would not have been hidden from anyone possessing a shred of intellect that speech does not transfer from a speaker to a book.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a doctrinal definition and refutation passage. Juwayni first states the orthodox position: God's speech is written in the Musahif, recited by tongues, and memorized in hearts. However, this does not mean it enters those things by way of accidents residing in substances (hulul al-a'rad fi'l-jawahir). He then provides a rational proof: the eternal speech does not separate from God's essence, and transition and movement are properties of bodies, not of the Creator. He then criticizes the historical error during Imam Ahmad's time when ignorant people, including the Hashwiyya, misunderstood the phrase 'speech of God is in the Musahif' to mean that the eternal speech itself physically resides in the books. This is an impossibility because speech does not transfer from a speaker to a book. The passage establishes that while the written text is the expression of God's speech, it is not the speech itself in its eternal attribute.

Key Terms
كلام الله (divine speech)
الأزلي (eternal)
الحلول (indwelling)
المصاحف (Musahif)
الحشوية (Hashwiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's eternal speech physically resides in the paper and ink of the Quran copies.
Correction: Juwayni explains that speech is an eternal attribute of God, not a physical entity that can dwell in created objects. The written text is an expression, not the attribute itself.

Checkpoint
What is the key reason Juwayni gives that God's speech cannot indwell in a book?
A) Because it is eternal and does not separate from God's essence
B) Because it is created
C) Because books are made of paper
D) Because the Hashwiyya said so

Key Takeaway
The eternal speech of God does not enter created mediums; it is written, recited, and memorized as an expression of the divine attribute, not by indwelling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a Mushaf, do you ever catch yourself thinking that the very words of God are physically in your hands, or do you remind yourself that His speech is an eternal attribute inseparable from His essence? How does that shift your reverence and understanding of what you are reciting? Commit today to reciting with the awareness that you are engaging with an expression of an eternal reality, not a created object.
?
Juwayni rebukes those who 'jumped to conclusions' without using their intellect. Have you ever accepted a belief about God simply because it sounded familiar or from a trusted source, without examining it with your God-given reason? What assumption about God's attributes might you be holding that needs to be tested against the teachings of the scholars? Resolve to question one belief this week and seek the orthodox understanding.
?
The Hashwiyya became so entrenched in their error that 'this talk became ingrained in their hearts.' Is there a theological error that you have adopted out of loyalty to a group or because you've always heard it? Are you willing to let go of it if it contradicts the truth taught by the imams? Pray for the strength to submit to truth even when it is uncomfortable.

Refuting the Pre-Eternity of the Letters of the Basmala
Juwayni quotes al-Baqillani to refute those claiming the letters of the basmala have no beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the letters of the basmala cannot be pre-eternal based on al-Baqillani's argument from necessary knowledge and self-contradiction.

Core Idea
The letters of the basmala are sequential and thus created, not eternal.

Imam Juwayni quotes the great scholar al-Baqillani to settle a debate about the nature of the letters of the basmala. Some had claimed that these letters have no beginning, implying they are eternal. Al-Baqillani counters that such a claim defies rational necessity and sensory intuition. This lesson unpacks that refutation and its implications for the createdness of the Qur'an's physical form.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the disputed claim
Identify the claim that the letters of the basmala (e.g., the 'seen' after 'ba') have no beginning. Understand why this claim matters for the nature of the Qur'an.
The basmala is 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'.
2
Understand al-Baqillani's refutation
Read the quote from al-Naqd al-Kabir. Note that he first states the claim, then says it contradicts 'the necessary' (al-daruri) and 'the intuitive' (al-badiha).
Necessary knowledge is self-evident truths.
3
See the consequence of self-contradiction
Al-Baqillani argues that if someone admits the letters have a beginning (awwaliyya) but still claims they have no beginning, they fall into sophistry. Reflect on why this is a fatal error.
Sophistry undermines all rational discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينقلب معنى النفس الى الأصوات سطورا ورسوما وأشكالا ورقوما ، فاذن تقول - بعد الاحاطة بحقيقة هذه الفصول - كلام الله. وقد نقل المؤلف في الشامل عن النقض الكبير للباقلاني : « من زعم أن السين من بسم بعد الباء . والمميم بعد السين الواقعة بعد الباء ، لا أول له : فقد خرج عن المعقول وجحد الضرورة وانكر البديهة ، فان اعترف بأوليته و أدعى أنه لا أول له ، فقد سقطت محاجنه ، وتعين لحوقه بالسفسطة وكيف يرجى أن يرشد بالدليل من يتواقح فى جحد الضرورى ؟ « اهـ فيكون موقفهم أخطر مما يتصور . والله سبحانه الهادي
And the meaning of the self does not transform into sounds, lines, forms, and notations. So then we say, after encompassing the reality of these chapters, that the speech of God... And the author has related in al-Shamil from al-Naqd al-Kabir of al-Baqillani: 'Whoever claims that the seen of "bism" is after the ba', and the mem after the seen occurring after the ba', that it has no beginning, has indeed left the intelligible, denied the necessary, and rejected the intuitive. For if he admits its beginning and still claims it has no beginning, his arguments have collapsed, and he is determined to fall into sophistry. How can one hope to guide by evidence the one who is shameless in denying the necessary?' So their position is more dangerous than imagined. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a proof by refutation. The author first restates that the psychological meaning (ma'na al-nafs) does not transform into physical sounds and letters. Then he introduces a quote from al-Baqillani's work al-Naqd al-Kabir via al-Shamil. The quote targets those who assert that the letters of the basmala (e.g., the 's' after 'b') have no beginning. Al-Baqillani argues that such a claim contradicts both rational necessity and sensory experience. If one admits that the letters have a beginning (i.e., they are sequential) yet insists they are eternal, then they fall into self-contradiction and sophistry. The author concludes that such people are in grave error and that only God can guide them. This refutes any notion that the physical letters of the Quran are eternal.

Key Terms
بسملة (basmala)
الضروري (necessary/immediate knowledge)
السفسطة (sophistry)
النقض الكبير (al-Naqd al-Kabir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The physical letters of the basmala are pre-eternal because the Qur'an is eternal.
Correction: Juwayni and Baqillani argue that sequential letters imply a beginning, so they cannot be eternal; only the divine speech (kalam nafsi) is eternal, not its physical expression.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what happens if someone claims the letters of basmala have no beginning?
A) They are correct
B) They fall into sophistry
C) They are guided by evidence
D) They are excused

Key Takeaway
The physical letters of the basmala are not eternal because they are sequential and contingent; claiming otherwise leads to self-contradiction and sophistry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever insisted on a belief about Allah that, if you honestly examined it, contradicts something you know to be true? What would it cost you to admit the contradiction and realign your understanding with rational necessity?
?
Al-Baqillani says that someone who admits a beginning yet denies it 'has no hope of being guided by evidence.' Where in your life do you cling to a belief that requires you to overlook the obvious? What is at stake if you let God's evidence overrule your comfort?
?
The letters of the basmala are sequential, yet some claimed they have no beginning. This is sophistry—the denial of objective truth. Are there areas where you, out of fear or pride, have allowed yourself to accept contradictions in your faith? Will you ask Allah to guide you to the clear truth, even if it humbles you?

Eternal Speech vs Temporal Utterance
Marginal note explaining eternal psychological speech vs temporal uttered letters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why uttered letters and sounds are temporal, while God's psychological speech is eternal, and how this applies to the case of Moses.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal; uttered sounds are created and temporal.

In this note, the commentator elaborates on a crucial distinction in the doctrine of divine speech: the uttered letters we hear are sequential and temporal, while the meaning subsisting in God's essence is eternal. He uses the example of Moses to clarify that the sound heard at Mount Sinai was a created sound, not God's speech itself, upholding divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice how the author first rules out pre-eternity for utterance, then affirms it for psychological speech, and finally addresses Moses.
Pay attention to the key terms: lafz, kalam nafsi, and taklim.
2
Identify the two categories
Spot where the note distinguishes between the temporal utterance (lafz) and the eternal psychological speech. Notice the conditional 'yes' (naʿam) introducing the exception for cognitive existence.
The author references Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Ibn Hazm in support.
3
Analyze the Moses example
Understand how the commentator uses the verse from Surah ash-Shura to argue that taklim (addressing) does not require sound. The sound Moses heard was from behind a veil, a created sound, not God's eternal speech.
Reflect on how this guards against the misconception that God's speech is a sound.
4
Summarize the key doctrine
In your own words, explain the difference between God's eternal speech and the temporal uttered sounds. Ensure you can articulate why the utterance is not eternal.
This directly connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللفظ متعاقب الحروف فى الاسماع، فلا يتصور العاقل في ذلك قدما، وكذلك الصوت، نعم ليس للفظ باعتبار وجوده العلمى والنفسى عند الله سبحانه تعاقب فيكون قديما كما قال بذلك أحمد، وتابعه ابن حزم وهو الموافق لتحقيق القوم فى الكلام النفسى الا أن وجوده أصلى بخلاف العلم فانه بالاضافة الى المعلوم فيكون ظليا، ولالم فرق بين موسى عليه السلام وبين غيره فى خلق السمع فيهما . وأما المسموع فان أريد به الصوت المكيف فكذلك وأن أريد ما هو قائم بالله فجل الاله من أن يقوم به عرض سیال و اهتزاز متلاحق . والوارد في الكتاب أنه تعالى كلم موسی - بدون ذکر صوت اصلا - والتكليم لا يستلزم الصوت . قال الله تعالى : ( ما كان لبشر أن يكلميه لله الا وحيا ، أو وراء حجاب ، أو يرسل رسولا ( اذ لا صوت فى الوحي الى القلب ، والصوت فى الثالث صوت الرسول لا المكلم . فليكن من وراء حجاب كذلك ، وهو الذى حصل لموسى فمهما كان النبي بسماعه صوت الرسول اليه بعد أن الله كلمه فلا يكون أى مانع من أن يعد موسى ربه ، از نودى من الشجرة .. وأى رائع يتصور حلول الله في الشجرة حتى يقول ان الذي سمعه صوت الله ؟ تعالى الله أن يكون كلامه صوتا . والآية قاضية على جميع الأوهام في هذا البحث عند أحسن التدبير فيها . راجع لفت اللحظ إلى ما فى الاختلاف في اللفظ وما علقناه على الأسماء و الصفات ) للبيهقى (۱۹۳) و ۲۵۱) (ز) .
The utterance (lafz) is sequential in letters concerning audition, so no rational person can conceive of it having pre-eternity. And likewise, the sound. Yes, there is no sequentiality for the utterance according to its cognitive and psychological existence with God Almighty, so it is eternal. As Ahmad stated, and Ibn Hazm followed him. And this is in agreement with the verification of the people concerning the psychological speech. However, its existence is original, unlike knowledge, which is relative to the known and thus is shadow-like. And there is no difference between Moses, peace be upon him, and others in the creation of hearing in them. As for what is heard (al-masmu'), if what is intended by it is the qualified sound, then similarly. And if what is intended is what subsists in God, then exalted is God from having a fluid accident and continuous vibration subsisting in Him. And what is mentioned in the Book is that God spoke to Moses without mentioning any sound at all. And speaking (taklim) does not necessitate sound. Allah says: 'It is not for a human that Allah should speak to him except by revelation, or from behind a veil, or by sending a messenger.' There is no sound in revelation to the heart, and the sound in the third is the sound of the messenger, not the Speaker. So let it be from behind a veil likewise. And that is what happened to Moses. So whenever the prophet hears the sound of the messenger after God spoke to him, there is no preventer from considering Moses as having heard his Lord, since he was called from the tree. And what awe can imagine God indwelling in the tree so that one says what he heard is God's voice? Exalted is God that His speech should be a sound. And the verse rules over all illusions in this research when properly pondered. Refer to ...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This note is an explanatory commentary on the preceding discussion. It distinguishes between the utterance (lafz) as a sequence of letters, which cannot be eternal because it is sequential, and the psychological speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) which, being a single eternal meaning in God's knowledge, is indeed eternal. The note aligns this view with Imam Ahmad and Ibn Hazm. It further discusses the case of Moses: the hearing of the sound does not imply that the sound itself is God's speech; rather, the sound is created and heard. The verse from Surah ash-Shura is cited to show that God's direct address (taklim) does not involve sound. The 'veil' for Moses was the tree, and the sound he heard was a created sound, not God's speech itself. The note strongly refutes anthropomorphism (tashbih) and asserts God's transcendence from being the subject of accidents.

الصوت
التكليم
الحجاب

Correction: The note clarifies that the sound was a created sound from behind a veil; God's speech is without sound.

Checkpoint

God's Hearing and Sight: True Perception Without Organs
Juwayni proves divine hearing and sight as true perception without organs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for God's attributes of hearing and sight, and why they do not involve physical organs.

Core Idea
God perceives truly and immediately, without any physical process or organ.

Imam al-Juwayni presents a compelling proof that God is Hearing and Seeing in a real sense, distinct from human perception. He argues that true perception is a perfection, and God, being all-perfect, must possess it without the physical limitations of creatures. This passage clarifies a key theological principle: divine attributes are real but transcendent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof structure
Notice that Juwayni begins with a necessary description then gives a proof based on human perception and the perfection of true perception.
The proof uses an analogy from human experience to establish a general principle.
2
Identify the negation of organs
Juwayni explicitly denies that God has physical processes like focusing, sensation, or eardrums. He affirms a true perception that is independent of matter.
3
Grasp the reductio argument
The final part shows the absurdity of denying God true perception, as it would imply a creature is more perfect than the Creator.
This is a logical argument from perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب وصف الله تعالى بكونه سميعا بصيرا .. والدليل عليه : أن الواحد منا اذا أبصر فانه يجرى منه تحديق فى جهة المرئى ، واتصال أشعة به ، على مجرى العادة واذا سمع فقد يقرع الهواء صماخيه ، والادراك الحقيقى يقع وراء الاتصالات التي ذكرناها . وذلك الادراك مزية على العلم بالمغيب الذى لم يدرك فالرب تعالى يدرك المبصر والمسموع على الحقيقة التى ندركها عليه ويتعالى عما تتصف به الحواس ، والحدق ، والأصمخة ، كما يعلم ذلك من غير نظر واستدلال . ويقدر من غير فرض جارحة ، وأداة . فمن وصف الاله بما ذكرناه من تحقيق الادراك فقد وافق المعنى ، ونحن نقطع باستحالة اتصافه بالاحساس والتحديق والاصاخة . وان أنكر منكر كونه مدركا لحقيقة الأشياء . فقد أثبت المخلوق فى الاحاطة والدرك مزية على الخالق ، ولا خفاء بطلان ذلك. وكيف يصح فى العقل : أن يخلق الرب للعبد الدرك الحقيقى ، وهو لا يدرك حقيقة ما خلق للعبد ادراك ..
It is necessary to describe God, exalted, as being Hearing, Seeing. And the proof of that is: when one of us sees, there occurs from him focusing towards the direction of the seen object, and connection of rays to it, according to custom. And when he hears, the air strikes his eardrums. True perception occurs beyond the connections we mentioned. That perception is an advantage over knowledge of the unseen that has not been perceived. So the Lord, exalted, perceives the seen and the heard according to the reality by which we perceive them, and He is exalted above what the senses, pupils, and ear canals are characterized by. He knows that without looking or deduction, and He perceives without positing an organ or tool. Whoever describes the Divine with what we mentioned of realizing perception has agreed with the meaning, and we are certain of the impossibility of His being described with sensation, focusing, and listening. If a denier denies that He is perceiver of the reality of things, then he has affirmed for the created being an advantage over the Creator in encompassing and perceiving, and the falsehood of that is not hidden. And how can it be sound in reason that the Lord creates for the servant true perception, while He does not perceive the reality of what He created for the servant's perception?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) for the divine attributes of hearing (sam') and sight (basr). Juwayni begins by stating it is obligatory (wajib) to describe God as Hearing and Seeing. He then provides the proof by analogy to human perception: When a person sees, there is physical focusing and connection of rays; when they hear, air strikes the eardrums. However, true perception occurs beyond these physical processes. This true perception is a perfection superior to mere knowledge of the absent. Therefore, God—who is the source of all perfections—must possess true perception of seen and heard realities, but without the physical organs and processes that characterize creatures. God knows without looking or reasoning, and perceives without any tool. Juwayni then emphasizes that whoever attributes true perception to God has correctly understood, and we definitively deny that God has sensation, focusing, or listening (since these involve physical change). He then gives a reductio argument: If someone denies that God perceives the true reality of things, then they would be giving the created being an advantage over the Creator in perception, which is clearly false. Moreover, it is unreasonable that God creates true perception in the servant while not perceiving the reality of what He created—this would imply deficiency in God.

Key Terms
سميع بصير
الإدراك
التحديق
الأصمخة
الحواس
الاحساس
الجارحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's hearing and sight require physical organs like ears and eyes.
Correction: Juwayni explains that God perceives truly but is exalted above all physical processes and organs.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the key difference between human perception and divine perception?
A) Humans perceive without physical processes, God requires them.
B) God perceives without physical organs, humans require them.
C) Both perceive through the same physical mechanisms.
D) God does not perceive at all.

Key Takeaway
God hears and sees through true perception, without any physical organs or processes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your limited eyes and ears are an obstacle to knowing God more fully? How does this lesson's affirmation that God's perception is perfect and without organ comfort or challenge you?
?
If you truly believed that God sees every detail of your life with direct perception—not as vague knowledge but as a real, present awareness—what would you change about the way you live today?
?
Juwayni says it is absurd that God would create true perception for the servant while lacking it Himself. Yet do you sometimes act as if God is less aware of your struggles than those around you? How can you repurpose that belief?

Proof that Allah is Hearing and Seeing
Juwayni proves Allah's hearing and seeing and refutes deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for Allah's attributes of hearing and seeing, and why it is necessary to affirm true perception for Allah while denying physical senses.

Core Idea
Allah's perception is real without organs; denying it gives creatures superiority.

Imam al-Juwayni presents a clear rational proof for the divine attributes of hearing and seeing. By reflecting on human perception and its physical accompaniments, he shows that true perception is distinct from physical processes. He then applies this distinction to Allah, affirming that He perceives all things without any need for limbs or instruments. This lesson unpacks that proof and refutes the misconception that Allah's attributes resemble human ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the structure: a claim, a proof, a clarification, and a refutation. Do not skip the translation.
Pay attention to the key terms: سميع, بصير, إدراك.
2
Understand the proof from human experience
Juwayni starts with human perception: we see by directing gaze and connecting rays, we hear by air striking the ears. Identify this premise and note that he calls these 'habitual' processes.
He says 'according to habit' – implying these are contingent, not essential.
3
Distinguish true perception from physical processes
True perception lies beyond those physical connections. It is a distinct quality superior to mere knowledge of the unseen. For Allah, He perceives the seen and heard in their true reality, but is exalted above having senses or organs.
Allah knows without sight or inference, and has power without limbs.
4
Analyze the refutation of deniers
If someone denies that Allah perceives things truly, they give the creature a higher degree of perception. Juwayni argues this is absurd – how can the Creator lack what He gives the creature?
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
5
Summarize the conclusion
Affirming true perception for Allah without anthropomorphism is correct. We must avoid both denying the attributes and likening them to human attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب وصف الله تعالى بكونه سميعا بصيرا .. والدليل عليه : أن الواحد منا اذا أبصر فانه يجرى منه تحديق فى جهة المرئى ، واتصال أشعة به ، على مجرى العادة واذا سمع فقد يقرع الهواء صماخيه ، والادراك الحقيقى يقع وراء الاتصالات التي ذكرناها . وذلك الادراك مزية على العلم بالمغيب الذى لم يدرك . فالرب تعالى يدرك المبصر والمسموع على الحقيقة التى ندركة عليها ويتعالى عما تتصف به الحواس ، والحدق ، والأصمخة ، كما يعلم ذلك من غير نظر واستدلال . ويقدر من غير فرض جارحة ، وأداة . فمن وصف الاله بما ذكرناه من تحقيق الادراك فقد وافق المعنى ، ونحن نقطع باستحالة اتصافه بالاحساس والتحديق والاصاخة . وان أنكر منكر كونه مدركا لحقيقة الأشياء . فقد أثبت المخلوق فى الاحاطة والدرك مزية على الخالق ، ولا خفاء بطلان ذلك. وكيف يصح فى العقل : أن يخلق الرب للعبد الدرك الحقيقى ، وهو لا يدرك حقيقة ما خلق للعبد ادراك .. [وفي نسخة زاهد : لا يوجد ( كونه )]
It is necessary to describe Allah Almighty as Hearing and Seeing. The proof for it is that when one of us sees, he directs his gaze towards the visible object and rays connect to it, according to habit. And when he hears, air strikes his ear canals. But true perception occurs beyond the connections we have mentioned. That perception is a superiority over knowledge of the unseen which has not been perceived. So the Lord Almighty perceives the visible and the audible in the true reality in which we perceive them, and He is exalted above what the senses, pupils, and ear canals are characterized by, just as He knows that without seeing and inference. And He has power without assuming a limb or instrument. So whoever describes the deity with what we have mentioned of the reality of perception has agreed with the meaning, and we are certain of the impossibility of His being described with sensing, gazing, and listening. And if a denier denies that He is a perceiver of the reality of things, then he has affirmed for the creature a superiority over the Creator in comprehension and perception, and the falsehood of that is not hidden. And how can it be rational that the Lord creates for the servant true perception while He does not perceive the reality of what He created perception for? [And in the copy of Zahid: does not exist (كونه)]
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a proof for Allah's attributes of hearing and seeing. Juwayni begins by stating that it is obligatory to describe Allah as Hearing and Seeing. He provides a proof based on human experience: when we see, there are physical processes like directing the gaze and connection of rays; when we hear, air strikes the ears. However, true perception lies beyond these physical connections. This perception is superior to mere knowledge of the unseen. For Allah, He perceives the seen and heard in their true reality, but He is exalted above the physical processes of the senses. He knows without seeing and deducing. He has power without needing limbs. So whoever describes Allah as having true perception (idrak) has agreed with the correct meaning. We are certain that it is impossible for Allah to be described with sensation, gazing, or listening as humans do. If someone denies that Allah perceives the reality of things, they have given the creature superiority over the Creator, because the creature perceives things through senses, but if Allah does not perceive, then the creature would have a higher degree of perception. That is clearly false. Juwayni then poses a rhetorical question: how can it be rational for the Lord to create true perception for the servant while He Himself does not perceive the reality of what He created perception for? This is absurd. The footnote indicates a variant reading where the word 'كونه' (His being) is missing in some copies.

Correction: Juwayni clarifies that Allah's perception is true perception (idrak) without any physical organs or processes, unlike human perception which involves eyes, ears, etc.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of hearing and seeing must be affirmed as true perception free from all physical limitations; denying them would imply a deficiency in the Creator that is rationally impossible.

The Eternal Attribute of Speech and Created Letters
Juwayni distinguishes the eternal speech of Allah from created letters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's distinction between the eternal speech of Allah (kalam nafsi) and the created physical expressions (letters, sounds) of the Quran.

Core Idea
The Quran's eternal meaning is with Allah; its written and recited forms are created.

Juwayni, a leading Ash'ari theologian, clarifies a critical point about the Quran: it is both eternal and created, but in different respects. The divine attribute of speech is eternal and subsists in Allah's essence. However, the letters we write, recite, and memorize are temporal, created entities. This passage lays out that distinction to prevent confusion and refute extreme views.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms qadim (eternal) and hadith (temporal).
The passage uses a contrast structure.
2
Identify the two categories
Find where Juwayni says 'that which subsists with Allah is qadim' and then lists the things that are hadith. Note each item: letters in hearing, shapes in pages, letters in minds, sounds in air.
All the physical and mental representations are temporal.
3
Understand the refutation
Juwayni rejects the claim that Allah speaks on every tongue. This would conflate the created recitation with the eternal attribute. Understand why this is considered ignorance.
The Ash'ari position affirms the Quran as uncreated in its essence but created in its expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله تبارك وتعالى فى المصاحف مكتوب ، وعلى ألسنة القراء مقروء : والصدور محفوظ ، وهو قائم بذات البارى وجودا . فيكون القائم بالله قديما ، وتكون الحروف المترتبة في استماع السامعين ، وأشكال الحروف المرسومة في الصحف والألواح ، والحروف المتخيلة في أذهان الحفاظ والأصوات التي هي عرض سيال قائم بالهواء حادثة جميعها ، فمن زعم أن الله يتكلم على لسان كل قائل ، تعالى الله عن جهالات الجاهلية .
Allah, blessed and exalted, is written in the Mus-hafs, recited on the tongues of reciters, and preserved in the hearts. And it is subsisting with the essence of the Creator as existence. So that which subsists with Allah is qadim (pre-eternal), while the letters arranged in the hearing of listeners, and the shapes of letters drawn in pages and tablets, and the letters imagined in the minds of memorizers, and the sounds that are a flowing accident subsisting in the air—all of them are hadith (temporal). So whoever claims that Allah speaks on the tongue of every speaker, exalted is Allah above the ignorances of the ignorant.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the Qur'an as the speech of Allah. Juwayni begins by stating that Allah is written in the Mus-hafs, recited on tongues, and preserved in hearts. The speech (qawl or kalam) subsists with the essence of the Creator as an existence (wujud). Then he explains: that which subsists with Allah is qadim (eternal), while the letters that are arranged when people recite, the shapes of letters in written copies, the letters imagined in minds, and the sounds that are accidents (arad) in the air—all of these are created (hadith). Therefore, it is false to claim that Allah speaks on the tongue of every speaker (i.e., that the created recitation is the same as the eternal attribute). Such a view is ignorance. This clarifies the Ash'ari position: the internal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) is eternal, but the verbal expressions are created.

Key Terms
قديم
حادث
كلام
حروف
صوت
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is entirely created, including the divine attribute of speech.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the speech subsisting with Allah is eternal, while its expressions (letters, sounds) are created.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is qadim in relation to the Quran?
A) The written letters
B) The sounds recited
C) The speech subsisting with Allah's essence
D) The pages and tablets

Key Takeaway
The Quran is eternal as Allah's attribute of speech, but its written and recited forms are created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Juwayni's Rule for Interpreting Ambiguous Attributes
Juwayni states the rule for interpreting ambiguous attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's principle for interpreting ambiguous divine attributes — that the attribute is affirmed in reality while its modality is unknown and not to be inquired into.

Core Idea
Affirm the attribute, leave the how to Allah.

Imam al-Juwayni presents a concise, authoritative rule that has shaped Sunni theology on the ambiguous verses (mutashabihat). He affirms the reality of attributes like istiwa' while categorically rejecting questions about how they are. This passage is a key reference for the salaf methodology of tafwid (consigning modality to Allah).

Guided Path
1
Read and translate the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the literal English translation. Notice the concise phrasing and the sequence of points.
The passage is a single sentence in Arabic, so pay attention to the flow.
2
Identify the key terms
Find the terms: 'al-istiwa' (استواء), 'al-kayfiyya (كيفية), 'bid'a (بدعة). Understand their meanings in context.
These terms are central to the methodology.
3
Understand the principle and its application
Juwayni first states the principle regarding istiwa', then extends it to other attributes (majd', hands, face, eyes) and the hadith of descent. Recognize the pattern: affirm the attribute, deny modality, forbid asking about it.
This principle guards against both anthropomorphism (tashbih) and denial (ta'til).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستواء معلوم والكيفية مجهولة والسؤال عنه بدعة فلتجرى آية الاستواء والمجيء وقوله لما خلقت بيدي ويبقى وجه ربك وقوله تجري بأعيننا وما صح من أخبار الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم كخبر النزول وغيره على ما ذكرناه فهذا بيان ما يجب لله تبارك وتعالى
Al-istiwa' is known, and the modality is unknown, and asking about it is an innovation. So let the verse of istiwa' and majd', and His statement 'when I created with My hands' and 'the Face of your Lord will remain' and His statement 'under Our eyes', and whatever is authentically reported from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, like the hadith of descent and others, be carried upon what we have mentioned. So this is an explanation of what is obligatory for Allah, blessed and exalted.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a methodological statement on how to deal with Qur'anic verses and prophetic reports that contain anthropomorphic attributes (mutashabihat). Juwayni affirms the principle that the meaning (al-istiwa') is known, meaning that the attribute is affirmed in a way befitting Allah, but the modality (al-kayfiyya) is unknown and not to be inquired into. Asking about how (kayf) is declared an innovation (bid'a). He then extends this rule to all such texts: the verses mentioning istiwa' (the Throne), 'majd'' (coming), the 'hand' in creation, the 'face' of Allah, and 'eyes' under which the ark sailed, as well as the prophetic report about divine descent (nuzul). All are to be interpreted in this manner—affirming the reality of the attribute without asking how. The passage concludes by stating that this is the explanation of what is obligatory to affirm concerning Allah.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الكيفية
البدعة
المعنى
النزول
المجيء
اليد
الوجه
العين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming attributes like 'hand' or 'descent' implies anthropomorphism (tashbih).
Correction: Juwayni affirms the attribute in reality but denies modality, so it does not imply similarity to creation.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the ruling on asking about the modality (kayfiyya) of Allah's attributes?
A) It is recommended
B) It is an innovation
C) It is obligatory
D) It is permissible

Key Takeaway
Juwayni's rule is to affirm the attribute without inquiring into its modality, guarding against both anthropomorphism and denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse about Allah's attributes that you cannot fully understand, do you find yourself trying to figure out 'how'? How does Juwayni's rule challenge your default response? Will you commit to stopping such inquiries?
?
You have likely heard debates about 'how' Allah descends or how His hand is. Do you now see that engaging in such debates is considered bid'a? Will you refrain from asking and instead affirm without modality?
?
What does it say about your heart if you feel unsatisfied with 'unknown modality'? Are you demanding that Allah's nature fit within your comprehension? Write down one attribute you struggle with and make a dua to accept it without asking how.

God's Acts Are Not Morally Differentiated
Juwayni states that God's acts are equal in divine judgment and cites a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that from the divine perspective, all of God's acts are equal in moral judgment, and that moral distinctions only apply from the human perspective.

Core Idea
God's acts are beyond human moral categories.

This passage from Imam al-Juwayni presents a foundational principle in Islamic theology: that God's acts are not subject to moral evaluation from the divine standpoint. Juwayni argues that all acts are equal in God's judgment, and any moral differentiation arises only from the human perspective. He supports this with a hadith where God declares His absolute authority over the division of souls.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Understand the key principle
Juwayni states that with respect to divine judgment, all acts are equal. This is a critical theological point: God's attributes and actions are not comparable to human ones.
The term 'حكم الإلهية' (divine judgment) is central.
3
Note the distinction between perspectives
Juwayni clarifies that acts only differ in moral rank from the perspective of servants (human beings). This means moral categories like good and evil are relative to us, not to God.
This prevents attributing human-like reasoning to God.
4
Examine the hadith as evidence
The hadith describes God dividing souls into blessed and wretched, and then saying 'I do not care'. This illustrates that God's decree is absolute and not subject to human notions of fairness.
The hadith reinforces the principle that God's will is not morally evaluable.
5
Reflect on common misunderstandings
Some might mistakenly think this means God does not care about good and evil. But Juwayni's point is that God is the source of good, and His judgments are not bound by human moral categories.
God is good and not evil, as stated at the beginning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله تبارك وتعالى خير ولا شر ، بالاضافة الى حكم الالهية فان الأفعال متساوية فى حكمه ، وانما تختلف مراتبها بالاضافة الى العباد ، وهذا المقدار مقنع فى هذا الأصل العظيم ، لا حاجة معه الى غيره . وقد نبه على هذا المعنى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذ قال في مساق حديث طويل : ( قسم الله الأرواح فوقفت أرواح السعداء على يمين العرش، وأرواح الأشقياء على يسار العرش ثم قال : هؤلاء أهل الجنة ، ولا أبالى . وهؤلاء أهل النار ، ولا أبالى .
God, Blessed and Exalted, is good and not evil. With respect to the judgment of divinity, acts are equal in His judgment; they only differ in degrees with respect to servants. And this amount is sufficient in this great principle; there is no need for anything else besides it. And the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, alerted to this meaning when he said in the course of a long hadith: 'God divided the souls: the souls of the blessed stood on the right side of the Throne, and the souls of the wretched on the left side of the Throne. Then He said: These are the people of Paradise, and I do not care. These are the people of Hell, and I do not care.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a statement of a key principle in Juwayni's theology: God's acts are not subject to moral evaluation from the divine perspective. It opens by affirming that God is good, not evil. But when it comes to the divine judgment (حكم الإلهية), all acts are equal; the moral differentiation we perceive (good vs. evil) is only relative to human beings (بالاضافة الى العباد). Juwayni declares this sufficient for this great principle, meaning no further argument is needed. He then supports it with a hadith: God divided souls into those destined for Paradise and those for Hell, and He says 'I do not care' (لا أبالى), meaning His decree is absolute and not contingent on human notions of fairness. The hadith reinforces the idea that God's will is not subject to moral evaluation.

السعداء
الأشقياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God does not care about good and evil.
Correction: God is the source of good, and His judgments are not bound by human moral categories. The hadith's 'I do not care' refers to His absolute sovereignty, not indifference to good and evil.

Checkpoint

A) From God's perspective
B) From the perspective of servants
C) From the perspective of angels

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
