Allah's Will Encompasses All Contingent Things
Juwayni argues for the uniformity of Allah's will and refutes a human analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all contingent events are uniformly willed by Allah and how human analogies fail to apply to the divine will.

Core Idea
Allah's will is one, undifferentiated by the outcomes of actions.

Juwayni begins by stating a fundamental principle: all contingent things are willed by Allah. He then anticipates a potential objection: if Allah gives wealth to someone who will misuse it, does that contradict His will? Through a powerful analogy, Juwayni shows that such reasoning is a confusion of human standards with divine attributes. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening principle
Start by reading the first sentence and understand the claim that all contingent events are willed by Allah.
This is the central thesis.
2
Examine the analogy of the king and the servant
Juwayni presents a hypothetical about a king who provides wealth to a servant who will misuse it. Consider why this analogy is used.
The analogy illustrates the flaw in applying human reasoning to Allah's will.
3
Identify the conclusion
Read how Juwayni concludes that the purpose is achieved in one of the two divisions of permissibility.
This connects to the broader discussion of divine actions.
4
Reflect on the key takeaway
After studying, ask yourself: what does this passage teach about the uniformity of Allah's will?
This reinforces the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادثات كلها مرادة الله تبارك وتعالى، وهذا مقتضب من القاعدة التي ذكرناها آنفا. فإذا تقرر أن الأفعال لا تتفاوت في حق الإله تبارك وتعالى فتعلق الإرادة بها على قضية واحدة لا تختلف، ونخصص هذا الفصل بأمر قاطع منزل على ما يرتضيه مولانا فنقول: أضلكم تنزيل أحكام الله تبارك وتعالى على مجارى أفعال الحكماء. وليس يخفى أن من علم أنه لو أمد عبدا من عبيده بالمال وضروب العدد لفسق وفجر وانتهك الحرمات واقتحم الكبائر والموبقات، فلو آمده مع علمه البات في ذلك ثم زعم أنه أراد بامتداده بعتاده أن يستمد به في أبواب الخيرات ويتخذه ذريعة في القربات، كانت هذه الإرادة مع العلم بنقيضها مشعرة بنهاية السفه والخبط في العقد، سيما إذا علم أنه لو قطع عنه مادته لاشتغل بما يعنيه، ورب الأرباب يمد الكفار بما يشد أزرهم ويقوي منهم ويكمل عدتهم. وإذا مهدنا المسلك فلا معنى للإطناب بعد وضوح العرض. وقد لاح للموفق ما أردناه. انجز الغرض في أحد قسمي الجواز في أحكام الإلهية.
All contingent things are willed by Allah, Blessed and Most High, and this is an excerpt from the principle we mentioned earlier. Since it is established that actions do not differ in respect to the Divine, Blessed and Most High, then the attachment of will to them is upon one uniform decree, not differing. And we specify this chapter with a decisive matter based on what our Master approves, so we say: You are misguided [if you] apply the rulings of Allah, Blessed and Most High, to the course of the actions of the wise. And it is not hidden that whoever knows that if he were to provide a servant among his servants with wealth and various numbers, and he would become corrupt and sinful, violate sanctities, and commit major sins and deadly offenses, then if he provided him while having definitive knowledge of that, then claimed that he intended by his provision and equipment that he [the servant] would use it in the doors of good deeds and take it as a means for acts of devotion, this will, together with knowledge of its opposite, would indicate utmost foolishness and confusion in doctrine, especially if he knows that if he cut off his resource he would occupy himself with what concerns him. And the Lord of lords provides the disbelievers with what strengthens their arms, empowers them, and completes their numbers. And when we have paved the way, there is no meaning to prolixity after the clarity of the topic. And it has become clear to the successful one what we intended. The purpose is accomplished in one of the two divisions of permissibility regarding the Divine rulings.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing that Allah's will is uniform and not subject to variation based on the apparent outcomes of actions. Juwayni begins by stating the principle: all contingent events are willed by Allah. He then argues that since actions do not differ in relation to Allah (i.e., they are all equally within His power and will), the attachment of His will to them is one and the same, without distinction. He then addresses a potential misunderstanding: people mistakenly apply human analogies to Allah, thinking that if a king gives wealth to a servant knowing he will misuse it, then the king cannot have intended good. But Allah provides disbelievers with wealth and strength despite their disbelief, yet His will is not contradictory. Juwayni uses this analogy to show that attributing defect to Allah's will based on apparent outcomes is foolish. He concludes that the argument is clear and the purpose is achieved.

Key Terms
إرادة
حادثات
جواز
أفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's will can be judged by human analogies of benefit and harm.
Correction: Allah's will is uniform and not subject to human standards; providing wealth to a servant who will misuse it does not contradict divine will.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, why is it misguided to judge Allah's actions by the standards of human rulers?
A) Because Allah's actions are not subject to human analogies.
B) Because Allah is above all creation.
C) Because human rulers are fallible.
D) Because the example is not relevant.

Key Takeaway
All contingent events are uniformly willed by Allah, and human analogies cannot be applied to judge His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a time when you wanted something good for someone but they misused it. Did that affect your view of your own will? How does that differ from Allah's will? What does this teach you about tawakkul and trusting Allah's decree even when outcomes seem unfair?
?
Are there areas of your life where you secretly judge Allah's will based on human standards of benefit and harm? What would it look like for you to truly believe that all contingent things—including your trials—are uniformly willed by Allah for a wisdom you may not grasp?

The False Assumption of Sensation in Seeing Allah
Juwayni refutes the false assumption of physical sensation in ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's refutation of the deniers' claim that seeing Allah requires physical sensation, and the alternative possibility of a special perception.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah does not depend on physical eyesight.

Juwayni begins by acknowledging the difficulty of the topic. He then identifies a fundamental error in the deniers' reasoning: they assume that the people of truth claim a physical sensation like staring at an object. Juwayni corrects this, explaining that the perception of Allah is not based on rays or physical contact. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sensation
Read the Arabic passage carefully from 'فأما القسم الثاني' down to 'وهي لا تتناهى'. Focus on how Juwayni describes the deniers' assumption and his correction.
Notice the technical terms 'إحساس' and 'إدراك'.
2
Identify the deniers' error
Juwayni says the deniers built their doctrine on a corrupt assumption: they think the people of truth claim that seeing Allah involves 'sensation' (إحساس) like staring. Identify this in the text.
3
Understand Juwayni's correction
Juwayni clarifies that Allah is above being sensed, but there can be a special attribute of perception (إدراك) that is not physical. This attribute is possible in Allah's power.
The key point: perception is not restricted to physical sensation.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: why is this correction important for the overall argument about ru'ya? How does it open the door for its possibility?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القسم الثاني وهو القول في جواز رؤية الإله تبارك وتعالى، وهذا قد طال فيه ارتباك طبقات الخلق، وحسبه الشادون [؟] الجليات، والانتهاء إلى درك القطع فيه عسير جدا، فإن الإحاطة بحقائق الإدراكات من أدق أحكام المعقولات. ونحن نستعين بالله، ونذكر ما يشهد العقل له بالسداد. فليعلم الناظر في هذا الفصل: أن الذين أحالوا رؤية الإله، بنوا عقدهم على ظن فاسد، وذلك أنهم ظنوا أن الإحساس الذي هو تحديق في صوب المرئي، هو الذي يدعى أهل الحق تعلق قبيله [؟] بوجود الإله، وهذا زلل، وسوء ظن بعصبة أهل الحق، تعالى الله أن يحس، ولكن ما أحسناه من المرئيات ندرك حقيقته، وإدراكنا حقيقته ليس هو المحسوسات المفسرة بمقابلة باتصال أشعة. فقال أهل الحق: لا يمتنع في قدرة الله سبحانه أن يخصص من أراد بصفة هي في التعلق بوجوده بالإضافة إلى العلم كالإدراك إلى المعلق بالمدركات شاهد بالإضافة إلى العلم بها على الغيب من غير درك، ثم تلك الصفة من مقدورات الباري تبارك وتعالى، وهي لا تتناهى. ومن لم يحله العقل التحق بالجائزات، سيما إذا اعتقد بالنصوص القاطعة في الكتاب والسنة. وأقوى متمسك في السمع شيئان: أحدهما: سؤال موسى عليه السلام الرؤية، مع الوفاق على أن من كان من منصب النبوة يستحيل أن يعتقد في حكم ربه ما يوجب تضليله. ونفاة الرؤية إذا اقتصدوا ولم يبوحوا بسوء عقدهم في الخصوم اقتصروا على تضليلهم. وكيف يستجيز منتم إلى الدين أن يفضل مسفلة نفاة الرؤية في معرفة الله تبارك وتعالى على موسى صلى الله عليه وسلم. نعم لا يمتنع أن يذهل النبي عن الغيب، ويستفزه الوله على سؤال ما علم جوازه، وإن لم يبلغه دخول وقته. فهذا أحد الشيئين.
As for the second division, which is the statement concerning the permissibility of seeing Allah, Blessed and Most High, this is something in which the confusion of the levels of creation has been prolonged, and the obstinate ones consider it among the clear matters, yet reaching decisive certainty regarding it is very difficult, for encompassing the realities of perceptions is among the most subtle of the judgments of intelligibles. We seek help from Allah, and we mention what reason testifies to its correctness. Let the examiner in this chapter know that those who denied the vision of Allah built their doctrine on a corrupt assumption. That is because they assumed that sensation, which is staring in the direction of the visible object, is what the people of truth claim its attachment [؟] to the existence of Allah. This is a slip and a bad opinion of the party of the people of truth. Exalted is Allah above being sensed, but what we perceive of visible things, we perceive its reality, and our perception of its reality is not the sensibles explained by facing through connection of rays. So the people of truth said: It is not impossible in the power of Allah, glorified, to single out whom He wills with an attribute that is, in its attachment to His existence, relative to knowledge, like perception relative to the object attached to perceptions, witnessing relative to knowledge of the unseen without perception. Then that attribute is among the capabilities of the Creator, Blessed and Most High, and they are limitless. And whatever the intellect does not deem impossible belongs to the possible things, especially if one believes in the definitive texts of the Book and the Sunnah. The strongest reliance in transmitted evidence is two things: One of them is the request of Moses, peace be upon him, for vision, with the agreement that whoever is of the station of prophethood cannot believe about his Lord's decree what would require his misguidance. And the deniers of vision, if they are moderate and do not disclose the evil of their belief in argument, they restrict themselves to declaring them misguided. How can someone affiliated with religion dare to prefer the lowest of the deniers of vision in knowledge of Allah, Blessed and Most High, over Moses, may Allah bless him and grant him peace? Indeed, it is not impossible that the prophet be heedless of the unseen, and yearning incite him to ask for what he knows is permissible, even if its time of occurrence has not reached him. This is one of the two things.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) and presents the first proof from transmitted evidence. Juwayni begins by acknowledging the difficulty of the topic. He then identifies the error of the deniers: they mistakenly think that the people of truth claim a physical sensation (like staring at an object) for seeing Allah. Juwayni clarifies that the people of truth do not assert physical sensation; rather, they affirm a special attribute of perception that is not like physical sight. He explains that Allah can create, in the believers, a perception that is not based on rays or physical contact. Then he presents the first transmitted proof: the request of Musa (AS) to see Allah. Since Musa was a prophet and cannot be misguided, his request implies that seeing Allah is permissible. The deniers, if they are consistent, would have to declare Musa misguided, which is absurd. He also allows that a prophet might be unaware of the timing of such an event. This concludes the first of the two proofs (the second is presumably on subsequent pages).

Key Terms
رؤية
إحساس
إدراك
جواز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeing Allah requires physical sensation like human eyesight.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that the people of truth do not claim physical sensation; rather, they affirm a special perception that is not based on rays or physical contact.

Checkpoint
What is the 'corrupt assumption' that Juwayni attributes to the deniers of ru'ya?
A) That Allah cannot be seen because He is not a body.
B) That the people of truth claim physical sensation (staring) as the mode of seeing Allah.
C) That the Quran does not mention seeing Allah.
D) That prophets never asked to see Allah.

Key Takeaway
The deniers' case rests on a false equation of seeing Allah with physical sensation, which Juwayni rejects and replaces with the possibility of a special perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unintentionally limited Allah by imagining that His actions must fit within your own physical experiences? What change in your perspective does Juwayni's argument demand from you today?
?
When you think about seeing Allah, do you subconsciously picture it with your physical eyes? How can you train your heart to accept a reality beyond your senses?
?
If you truly believed that Allah can grant a perception beyond all physical limits, how would that change the way you seek closeness to Him in your daily worship?

The Proof from Musa's Request for Ru'ya
Juwayni presents the proof from Musa's request for ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's transmitted proof from the Prophet Musa's request to see Allah, and why it establishes the permissibility of ru'ya.

Core Idea
Musa's request proves ru'ya is possible because prophets do not ask for the impossible.

After clearing the conceptual ground, Juwayni presents the strongest transmitted evidence: the request of Musa (AS) to see Allah. He argues that since Musa was a prophet, it is inconceivable that he would ask for something impossible or harmful to his faith. Therefore, his request implies that seeing Allah is permissible. This lesson unpacks that argument and its defense against potential objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Musa's request
Read from 'وأقوى متمسك في السمع شيئان' to 'فهذا أحد الشيئين'. Focus on how Juwayni uses Musa's request as proof.
Note that this is the first of two transmitted proofs.
2
Identify the main argument
Juwayni says that Musa's request is strong proof because it is agreed that prophets cannot be misguided. If ru'ya were impossible, Musa would be asking for something wrong, which is not allowed.
3
Understand the defense against objection
Juwayni anticipates an objection: perhaps Musa was heedless of the unseen or asked out of yearning. He allows that a prophet can ask for something permissible even if its timing is unknown.
This preserves the infallibility of the prophet while upholding the permissibility.
4
Reflect on the implication for deniers
Juwayni argues that the deniers, if consistent, would have to declare Musa misguided, which is absurd. This shows the strength of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القسم الثاني وهو القول في جواز رؤية الإله تبارك وتعالى، وهذا قد طال فيه ارتباك طبقات الخلق، وحسبه الشادون [؟] الجليات، والانتهاء إلى درك القطع فيه عسير جدا، فإن الإحاطة بحقائق الإدراكات من أدق أحكام المعقولات. ونحن نستعين بالله، ونذكر ما يشهد العقل له بالسداد. فليعلم الناظر في هذا الفصل: أن الذين أحالوا رؤية الإله، بنوا عقدهم على ظن فاسد، وذلك أنهم ظنوا أن الإحساس الذي هو تحديق في صوب المرئي، هو الذي يدعى أهل الحق تعلق قبيله [؟] بوجود الإله، وهذا زلل، وسوء ظن بعصبة أهل الحق، تعالى الله أن يحس، ولكن ما أحسناه من المرئيات ندرك حقيقته، وإدراكنا حقيقته ليس هو المحسوسات المفسرة بمقابلة باتصال أشعة. فقال أهل الحق: لا يمتنع في قدرة الله سبحانه أن يخصص من أراد بصفة هي في التعلق بوجوده بالإضافة إلى العلم كالإدراك إلى المعلق بالمدركات شاهد بالإضافة إلى العلم بها على الغيب من غير درك، ثم تلك الصفة من مقدورات الباري تبارك وتعالى، وهي لا تتناهى. ومن لم يحله العقل التحق بالجائزات، سيما إذا اعتقد بالنصوص القاطعة في الكتاب والسنة. وأقوى متمسك في السمع شيئان: أحدهما: سؤال موسى عليه السلام الرؤية، مع الوفاق على أن من كان من منصب النبوة يستحيل أن يعتقد في حكم ربه ما يوجب تضليله. ونفاة الرؤية إذا اقتصدوا ولم يبوحوا بسوء عقدهم في الخصوم اقتصروا على تضليلهم. وكيف يستجيز منتم إلى الدين أن يفضل مسفلة نفاة الرؤية في معرفة الله تبارك وتعالى على موسى صلى الله عليه وسلم. نعم لا يمتنع أن يذهل النبي عن الغيب، ويستفزه الوله على سؤال ما علم جوازه، وإن لم يبلغه دخول وقته. فهذا أحد الشيئين.
As for the second division, which is the statement concerning the permissibility of seeing Allah, Blessed and Most High, this is something in which the confusion of the levels of creation has been prolonged, and the obstinate ones consider it among the clear matters, yet reaching decisive certainty regarding it is very difficult, for encompassing the realities of perceptions is among the most subtle of the judgments of intelligibles. We seek help from Allah, and we mention what reason testifies to its correctness. Let the examiner in this chapter know that those who denied the vision of Allah built their doctrine on a corrupt assumption. That is because they assumed that sensation, which is staring in the direction of the visible object, is what the people of truth claim its attachment [؟] to the existence of Allah. This is a slip and a bad opinion of the party of the people of truth. Exalted is Allah above being sensed, but what we perceive of visible things, we perceive its reality, and our perception of its reality is not the sensibles explained by facing through connection of rays. So the people of truth said: It is not impossible in the power of Allah, glorified, to single out whom He wills with an attribute that is, in its attachment to His existence, relative to knowledge, like perception relative to the object attached to perceptions, witnessing relative to knowledge of the unseen without perception. Then that attribute is among the capabilities of the Creator, Blessed and Most High, and they are limitless. And whatever the intellect does not deem impossible belongs to the possible things, especially if one believes in the definitive texts of the Book and the Sunnah. The strongest reliance in transmitted evidence is two things: One of them is the request of Moses, peace be upon him, for vision, with the agreement that whoever is of the station of prophethood cannot believe about his Lord's decree what would require his misguidance. And the deniers of vision, if they are moderate and do not disclose the evil of their belief in argument, they restrict themselves to declaring them misguided. How can someone affiliated with religion dare to prefer the lowest of the deniers of vision in knowledge of Allah, Blessed and Most High, over Moses, may Allah bless him and grant him peace? Indeed, it is not impossible that the prophet be heedless of the unseen, and yearning incite him to ask for what he knows is permissible, even if its time of occurrence has not reached him. This is one of the two things.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'ya) and presents the first proof from transmitted evidence. Juwayni begins by acknowledging the difficulty of the topic. He then identifies the error of the deniers: they mistakenly think that the people of truth claim a physical sensation (like staring at an object) for seeing Allah. Juwayni clarifies that the people of truth do not assert physical sensation; rather, they affirm a special attribute of perception that is not like physical sight. He explains that Allah can create, in the believers, a perception that is not based on rays or physical contact. Then he presents the first transmitted proof: the request of Musa (AS) to see Allah. Since Musa was a prophet and cannot be misguided, his request implies that seeing Allah is permissible. The deniers, if they are consistent, would have to declare Musa misguided, which is absurd. He also allows that a prophet might be unaware of the timing of such an event. This concludes the first of the two proofs (the second is presumably on subsequent pages).

Key Terms
رؤية
نبوة
موسى
جواز
سمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Musa's request implies he was ignorant or mistaken about Allah's nature.
Correction: Juwayni clarifies that prophets are infallible in their beliefs, so Musa must have known that ru'ya was permissible, even if he was unaware of the timing.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does the request of Musa (AS) to see Allah prove?
A) That seeing Allah is impossible because Musa was denied.
B) That seeing Allah is permissible because prophets do not ask for impossible things.
C) That only prophets can see Allah.
D) That seeing Allah requires physical sensation.

Key Takeaway
Musa's request for ru'ya serves as a decisive transmitted proof for its permissibility, relying on the infallibility of prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider Musa's intense longing to see Allah, do you feel a similar urgency in your own heart? How often do you even ask Allah for the ultimate vision? What is holding you back from that yearning? Commit today to making du'a for ru'ya in the afterlife.
?
Juwayni argues that to prefer the reasoning of deniers over Musa is absurd. Yet how often do you trust your own doubts and reservations over the clear testimony of the prophets? Are you willing to submit your intellect to the prophetic example, even when it challenges your assumptions? Examine one area where you elevate your reasoning over revelation.
?
The proof hinges on the infallibility of prophets. Do you truly believe that the prophets are never mistaken about Allah's attributes, or do you harbour some reservations? How would that affect your trust in revelation? Ask Allah to purify your heart from any doubt about the perfection of His messengers.

Refuting the Denial: The Error of Sensory Assumption
Juwayni refutes the denial by correcting the confusion about sensation and presenting the correct theological principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the denial of seeing God is based on a false assumption about sensory perception and how the true position affirms a divinely created attribute.

Core Idea
Seeing God does not require physical sensation; it is a divinely granted attribute.

Juwayni begins by acknowledging the difficulty of this topic and identifies the root error of those who deny the vision of God: they mistakenly equate the perception of visible objects with the mode of seeing God. He then clarifies the true stance of Ahl al-Haqq, which distinguishes between sensory perception and an intellectual apprehension enabled by God. Read on to see how he dismantles the faulty premise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to Juwayni's description of the opponents' error and the alternative he presents.
The key phrase is 'ظنوا أن الاحساس الذى هو تحديق' — they thought sensation (staring) is what is claimed.
2
Identify the opponents' false assumption
Find where Juwayni states what the opponents thought. What is their mistake?
They confused physical sensation with the attribute of vision of God.
3
Understand the true position of Ahl al-Haqq
Juwayni explains that God can create an attribute that relates to His existence like perception relates to perceived things. What does this mean?
It is a special knowledge, not physical sight.
4
Connect to the broader topic
Consider why this distinction matters for the permissibility of seeing God in the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القسم الثانى وهو القول في جواز رؤية الاله تبارك وتعالى، وهذا قد طال فيه ارتباك طبقات الخلق، وحسبه الشادون الجليات، والانتهاء الى درك القطع فيه عسير جدا فان الاحاطة بحقائق الادراكات من أدق أحكام المعقولات ونحن نستعين بالله، ونذكر ما يشهد العقل له بالسداد. فليعلم الناظر في هذا الفصل: أن الذين أحالوا رؤية الاله، بنوا عقدهم على ظن فاسد وذلك أنهم ظنوا أن الاحساس الذى هو تحديق فى صوب المرئى، هو الذى يدعى أهل الحق تعلق قِبَلِهِ بوجود الاله، وهذا زلل، وسوء ظن بعصبة أهل الحق، تعالى الله أن يحس، ولكن ما أحسناه من المرئيات ندرك حقيقته، وادراكنا حقيقته ليس هو المحسوسات المفسرة بمقابلة باتصال أشعة. فقال أهل الحق: لا يمتنع في قدرة الله سبحانه أن يخصص من أراد بصفة هى فى التعلق بوجوده بالاضافة الى العلم كالادراك الى المعلق بالمدركات شاهد بالاضافة الى العلم بها على الغيب من غير درك، ثم تلك الصفة من مقدورات البارى تبارك وتعالى، وهى لا تتناهى ومن لم يحله العقل التحق بالجائزات، سيما اذا اعتقد بالنصوص القاطعة في الكتاب والسنة، وأقوى متمسك فى السمع شيئان. أحدهما: سؤال موسى عليه السلام الرؤية، مع الوفاق على أن من كان من منصب النبوة يستحيل أن يعتقد في حكم ربه ما يوجب تضليله ونفاة الرؤية اذا اقتصدوا ولم يبوحوا بسوء عقدهم في الخصوم اقتصروا على تضليلهم وكيف يستجيز منتم الى الدين أن يفضل مسألة نفاة الرؤية في معرفة الله تبارك وتعالى على موسى صلى الله عليه وسلم. نعم لا يمتنع أن يذهل النبي عن الغيب، ويستفزه الوله على سؤال ما علم جوازه، وان لم يبلغه دخول وقته. فهذا أجد الشيئين. والثاني: أن تعلم قطاعات علم من لا يتمارى - أن الأولين كانوا مبتهلين - الى الله تبارك وتعالى في سؤال المطر، وبه ابتهالهم اليه فى سؤال كل ممكن من ثواب أو مغفرة. ومن جحد هذا فهو معاند والأمة معصومة لا تجتمع على الضلالة، ولسنا ندعى الاجماع مع ظهور الخلاف الآن. ولكنا ندعى تقدم الاجماع من سلف الأمة قبل ظهور الآراء، واختلاف الأهواء. فذلك ما أردناه في هذا الفصل، وقد نجز بانتهاء هذا الفصل: غرضنا من هذا المعتقد في أقسام الأحكام الالهية
As for the second division, which is the discussion on the permissibility of seeing God, Blessed and Exalted—this has greatly entangled various classes of people, and those who seize upon clear proofs suffice themselves, yet reaching certainty in it is very difficult, for encompassing the realities of perceptions is among the subtlest judgments of the intellect. We seek help from God and mention what reason testifies to as correct. So let the observer in this chapter know that those who deny the vision of God built their creed on a false assumption, for they thought that the sensation which is staring toward the visible object is what the people of truth claim attaches to the existence of God. This is an error and an evil assumption about the group of the people of truth. Exalted is God above being sensed; rather, what we perceive of visible things we apprehend its reality, and our apprehension of its reality is not the sensibles defined by direct encounter through the connection of rays. So the people of truth said: It is not impossible in the power of God, Glorified, that He specifies whomever He wills with an attribute that, in its relation to His existence, is like perception in relation to perceived things, as a witness in relation to knowledge of the Unseen without direct apprehension. Then that attribute is among the possibilities of the Creator, Blessed and Exalted, and they are limitless. What the intellect does not deem impossible falls under the category of contingent things, especially when one believes in the definitive texts from the Book and the Sunnah. The strongest scriptural support is two things: One of them is the request of Moses, peace be upon him, for vision, with the agreement that one who is in the station of prophethood cannot believe of his Lord that which would necessitate his misguidance. And the deniers of vision, if they are moderate and do not reveal their evil creed in dispute, suffice themselves with declaring them misguided. How can one who claims adherence to religion consider it permissible to prefer the matter of the deniers of vision in knowledge of God, Blessed and Exalted, over Moses, may God's peace and blessings be upon him? Indeed, it is not impossible that the prophet become heedless of the Unseen and be agitated by distraction to ask about what he knows is permissible, even if the time of its occurrence has not reached him. This is the stronger of the two things. The second: that you know the segments of knowledge from one who does not doubt—that the early generations were supplicating to God, Blessed and Exalted, in asking for rain, and by their supplication to Him in asking for every possible thing of reward or forgiveness. Whoever denies this is obstinate, and the community is protected from erring collectively. We do not claim consensus in the face of manifest disagreement now, but we claim the precedence of consensus from the predecessors of the community before the emergence of opinions and the divergence of passions. That is what we intended in this chapter, and it has been completed with this chapter: our purpose from this creed regarding the divisions of divine rulings.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the denial of the possibility of seeing God and an affirmation of its permissibility, supported by two scriptural proofs. Juwayni begins by noting the difficulty and confusion surrounding this topic, then identifies the root error of the opponents: they mistakenly think that the sensory perception (al-ihsas) involved in looking at an object is what the Ahl al-Haqq claim as the mode of apprehending God. Juwayni clarifies that God is beyond being sensed physically; rather, we perceive the reality of visible things, but that perception is not the same as the sensibles defined by direct encounter through rays. The Ahl al-Haqq then state the true position: God can create in whomever He wills an attribute that relates to His existence in a way analogous to perception relating to perceived things, serving as a witness to knowledge of the Unseen without direct apprehension. This attribute is among the contingent possibilities (al-ja'izat) and is not impossible for God. Juwayni then presents the two strongest scriptural evidences. The first is Moses' request to see God. The fact that a prophet would ask for something impossible for God is inconceivable, so Moses must have known it was permissible. The second is the consensus of the early community, who would supplicate to God for rain and other permissible things, which implies they believed it was permissible to ask for vision. Juwayni clarifies that he does not claim consensus after the emergence of disagreement, but rather the precedent consensus of the Salaf before sects arose.

الجواز
الإحساس
التحديق
الشعاع
القدرة
الصفة
المقدورات
الجائزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That seeing God requires physical sensation/eyes.
Correction: Seeing God is an intellectual apprehension through a divinely created attribute, not physical sight.

Checkpoint
What do the opponents mistakenly think Ahl al-Haqq claim about seeing God?
A) That God can be seen through physical eyes
B) That God is beyond being sensed
C) That seeing God is impossible
D) That vision of God is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Seeing God is not a physical sensation but a divinely created cognitive attribute that is possible for God to bestow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unconsciously limited Allah's power by assuming He can only be perceived through your physical senses? What would it take for you to truly believe in a perception beyond all physical limits?
?
Your intellect tells you that seeing God is not impossible, but does your heart yearn for that vision? What is holding you back from longing for the highest reward in Paradise?
?
If you truly accepted that Allah can grant you direct perception of Him without any sensory medium, how would that change the way you seek Him in this life—through His signs, His names, and His book?

Scriptural Proofs: Moses' Request and Early Consensus
Juwayni presents two scriptural proofs: Moses' request and early consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scriptural proofs Juwayni uses to support the permissibility of seeing God: Moses' request and the consensus of the early community.

Core Idea
Moses would not ask the impossible, and the early consensus affirms the permissibility.

After establishing the rational possibility, Juwayni turns to scripture for support. He presents two powerful proofs: Moses' request to see God, which would be unimaginable if it were impossible, and the consensus of the early Muslim community, who consistently supplicated to God for various needs, implying they believed it permissible to ask for vision. Let's examine these proofs and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the two proofs.
Pay attention to the phrases 'أقوى متمسك فى السمع شيئان' and 'أحدهما: سؤال موسى'.
2
Analyze the first proof: Moses' request
Why does Juwayni consider this a strong proof? What is his argument about a prophet's knowledge?
He argues that a prophet would not ask for something that is impossible for God.
3
Understand the second proof: consensus of the Salaf
How does early community practice demonstrate permissibility? What does Juwayni say about claiming consensus now?
He says the early generation supplicated for rain and other things, including vision; consensus was established before divergence.
4
Evaluate the strength of these proofs
Consider how these scriptural arguments complement the rational argument from the previous lesson.

Juwayni clarifies that he does not claim consensus after the emergence of disagreement, but rather the precedent consensus of the Salaf before sects arose.

Key Terms

الإجماع
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Moses' request was a mistake or a sin.
Correction: Juwayni argues that Moses' request was based on knowledge that it is permissible, even if the time had not come.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does the request of Moses show about seeing God?
A) That it is impossible
B) That it is permissible
C) That it will happen in this world
D) That Moses was mistaken

Key Takeaway
Moses' request and the early consensus both affirm that seeing God is permissible and not impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Juwayni says the community is protected from error when they are united. Whose example do you follow in matters of faith: the early consensus or the opinions that came later? What would it take for you to align your heart with the Salaf?

The Placement of Tawhid within the Threefold Division
Juwayni defends the treatment of tawhid outside the threefold division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's reasoning for treating tawhid outside the standard tripartite division of necessary, impossible, and contingent, and why tawhid is a negation rather than a positive attribute.

Core Idea
Tawhid is not a positive attribute but a negation of any second to the One.

Juwayni’s tripartite division covers what is necessary, impossible, and contingent regarding God. But where does tawhid fit? In this section, Juwayni addresses two objections: why tawhid is not placed as a separate category and why it is not treated as a necessary attribute. His answers clarify the unique nature of tawhid as a negation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: two objections followed by Juwayni's responses.
2
Identify the two objections
The first objection asks why tawhid is not one of the three divisions. The second asks why it is not arranged under the necessary category. Understand what each objector assumes about the classification.
3
Analyze Juwayni's answers
For the first, he says the question of a second administrator is outside the scope of the divisions. For the second, he explains that tawhid reduces to negation, not a positive attribute. Connect this to the reason for its separate treatment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضل فى الوحدانية. فان قيل: لم تدرجوا اثبات الوحدانية في قسم من الأقسام الثلاثة؟ قلنا: ذكرنا ما يجب الله تبارك وتعالى ويستحيل عليه، ويجوز في حكمه فالسؤال عن تقدير مدير ثان يقع وراء الضبط المقصود. فانسل هذا الفضل المقصود عن ترتيب المعتقد، ونحن نذكر فيه بعد هذا التنبيه ما يستقل به اللبيب، اذا وقف معانيه. فان قيل: هلا رتبتم هذا الفصل على ما يجب الله تعالى، فإن الوحدانية صفته الواجبة؟ قلنا: محصول الوحدانية يؤول الى نفى من مستوى الواحد فليست صفة ثابتة.
A section on Divine Unity. For if it is said: Why did you include the affirmation of divine unity in one of the three divisions? We say: We mentioned what is necessary for God, Blessed and Exalted, what is impossible for Him, and what is permissible in His decree. So the question about the supposition of a second administrator falls outside the intended scope. So this intended section separates from the arrangement of the creed, and we will mention in it, after this reminder, what the intelligent person can independently understand if he pauses on its meanings. For if it is said: Why did you not arrange this chapter according to what is necessary for God, Exalted, for divine unity is His necessary attribute? We say: The substance of divine unity reduces to a negation of a second to the One, so it is not a positive attribute.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a short section (fadl) on tawhid consisting of two objections and their answers. The first objection asks why the affirmation of tawhid is placed within one of the three divisions (necessary, impossible, contingent). Juwayni answers that the purpose of the tripartite division was to cover what is necessary, impossible, and contingent regarding God. Asking about a second administrator (i.e., another god) is outside that scope, so this section is set apart. The second objection asks why tawhid is not arranged under the category of what is necessary for God, since tawhid is His necessary attribute. Juwayni replies that tawhid ultimately reduces to a negation (of any second to the One), so it is not a positive attribute (sifa thabita) like other necessary attributes. Thus, it is treated separately.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
الأقسام الثلاثة
الصفة الواجبة
النفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawhid is a positive attribute like other necessary attributes.
Correction: Juwayni explains that tawhid reduces to a negation of a second, so it is not a positive attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does Juwayni say tawhid is not a positive attribute?
A) Because it is impossible to describe
B) Because it is a negation of a second to the One
C) Because it is a contingent matter
D) Because it is not mentioned in scripture

Key Takeaway
Tawhid is not a separate category in the tripartite division because it is a negation, not a positive attribute, and the division covers only positive aspects of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, what 'second administrator' do you unconsciously suppose alongside God—perhaps your own plans, wealth, or status? This lesson forces you to reduce tawhid to pure negation: what must you actively negate today to make your declaration of tawhid genuine?
?
Juwayni insists tawhid is not a positive attribute but a negation. When you say 'Allah is One,' do you feel the weight of negating all rivals, or is it merely a statement you repeat without stripping away your hidden polytheisms? What is one attachment you need to negate right now to make your tawhid real in your heart?

Proof of God's Knowledge from Actions in Forgetfulness
Juwayni proves God's knowledge from the Quran and rational argument on actions in heedlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Juwayni uses the phenomenon of actions performed in forgetfulness to prove that all actions indicate God's knowledge, not the human agent's.

Core Idea
Human forgetfulness proves that actions reveal God's knowledge, not ours.

In this passage, Imam al-Juwayni presents a unique argument for God's omniscience. He cites a Quranic verse and then builds a rational proof based on actions performed in states of heedlessness. This lesson walks through the argument step by step, showing how human unawareness actually confirms God's detailed knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Get a sense of the argument without overanalyzing.
Pay attention to the verse citation and the logical flow.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Juwayni begins with Quran 67:13-14. Notice how he extracts the principle that the Creator knows all realities.
The verse asks: 'Does He who created not know?'
3
Understand the rational principle
Juwayni states a rational premise: actions indicate the knowledge of their creator. This is the key link.
Actions are signs of the agent's knowledge.
4
Apply the principle to heedlessness
Consider actions performed while asleep or distracted. The human does not know them, so the knowledge must belong to God alone.
This is the crucial move: human unawareness excludes human knowledge.
5
Conclude the proof
Since actions indicate knowledge, and the human lacks it in that state, the actions point to God's knowledge.
Thus God knows all actions, even those unknown to the doer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله سبحانه وتعالى : ( وأسروا قولكم أو أجهروا به . انه عليم بذات الصدور ألا يعلم من خلق ؟ » ( الملك ١٣ و ١٤) فدل مقتضى الآية : أن العالم بحقائق الحادثات : بارثها وخالقها . وقد تقرر في قضايا العقول أن الأفعال دالة على علم خالقها بها . فاذا صدرت رت أفعال من العبد فى حالة ذهوله عنها ، فهى دالة على علم العبد بها . فانه غير عالم بما جرت يده به في حال غفلته وذهوله . والنائم غير شاعر بتقلباته في غلبات النوم ، وغفراته . فاذا وجب أن تدل الأفعال على علم خالقها ، ثم لم تدل على علم العبد في حال قومه وذهوله دل أنها دالة على علم خالقها ومقدرها ، وهو رب العالمين
He, exalted and sublime, said: 'And conceal your speech or proclaim it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know?' (al-Mulk 13-14). So the import of the verse indicates that the Knower of the realities of contingent things is their Originator and Creator. And it has been established in the judgments of intellects that actions indicate the knowledge of their Creator. So if actions issue from the servant in a state of heedlessness of them, they are indicative of the servant's knowledge of them. For he is not knowledgeable of what his hand does in a state of inattention and heedlessness. And the sleeper is not aware of his tossings and turnings during overpowering sleep and his lapses. So when it is necessary that actions indicate the knowledge of their Creator, and then they do not indicate the knowledge of the servant in his state of alertness and heedlessness, it indicates that they indicate the knowledge of their Creator and Determiner, and He is the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a proof of God's detailed knowledge, combining a Quranic citation with a rational argument. Juwayni begins by citing Quran 67:13-14, which declares that God knows all secrets and asks rhetorically whether the Creator does not know. He draws from this that the One who knows the realities of contingent events is their Originator and Creator. He then states a rational premise: actions indicate the knowledge of their doer. Next, he applies this premise to a specific case: if a person performs an action while heedless, the action still indicates that he has some knowledge (otherwise the action could not be done), but the person is unaware of the action (as in sleep or distraction). Therefore, since the action does not indicate the human's knowledge in that state, it must indicate the knowledge of the action's true Creator and Determiner—God. The argument proceeds step by step: first establishing the general principle, then observing human unawareness, then concluding that the knowledge manifested in actions belongs to God alone.

Key Terms
علم
فعل
ذهول
غفلة
خالق
مقدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human unawareness disproves God's knowledge, because if God knows everything, why do we act without awareness?
Correction: This argument actually proves God's knowledge: our unawareness shows that the knowledge behind actions is not our own, so it must be God's.

Checkpoint
What rational principle does Juwayni use to argue that actions indicate knowledge?
A) Actions are impossible without knowledge.
B) Actions performed in heedlessness indicate the knowledge of the heedless person.
C) The Quran explicitly states that actions indicate knowledge.
D) Actions indicate the knowledge of their Creator.

Key Takeaway
Actions performed without human awareness demonstrate that the knowledge they manifest belongs to God alone, proving His detailed omniscience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you acted out of habit or in a state of complete distraction—perhaps scrolling on your phone or speaking without thinking. According to this lesson, God knows every detail of that action, even though you were unaware. How does this reality affect your accountability for actions you do not even remember? Will you now ask for forgiveness for your heedless moments and strive to be more mindful of your every movement, knowing that every action is witnessed by the One who created it?
?
When you sleep and toss and turn, you are not conscious of your own actions. Yet this passage says even those motions indicate God's knowledge. How does this expand your understanding of God's constant presence and awareness of you—even in your most vulnerable and unconscious states? What practical steps can you take to cultivate a continuous awareness that God sees and knows everything, even when you don't?
?
Juwayni argues that actions cannot 'belong' to you in your heedlessness because you lack knowledge of them, so they must belong to God. If your own actions can be taken from you while you're unaware, what does that say about your sense of ownership and control? Are you willing to acknowledge that your entire existence—every action and breath—is ultimately in God's hands, and that you are dependent on His knowledge and will at every moment? How might this shift your attitude toward pride or self-reliance?

Answering the Objection: How Can the Wise Will Foolishness?
Juwayni answers the objection that the Wise God cannot will foolishness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's response to the objection that a Wise God cannot will foolishness, including his argument that actions are neutral for God and the analogy of a wise master.

Core Idea
For God, actions are neutral; wisdom does not require preventing all sin.

This passage addresses a common objection: how can a perfectly wise God will what appears to be foolishness? Juwayni responds by clarifying that actions are equivalent for God, who neither benefits nor is harmed. He then provides an analogy to show that a wise master would not leave his slaves unchecked. This lesson unpacks his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the objection starts with 'فان قيل'.
2
Identify the objection
The objection asks: How can the Wise God will foolishness? Understand why this seems problematic: wisdom and foolishness are opposites.
3
Understand Juwayni's initial reply
Juwayni says actions are equal in relation to God because He neither benefits nor is harmed. This means no action is inherently foolish for God.
He references earlier discussions: 'قد سبق في قدر كاف شاف'.
4
Analyze the analogy
Juwayni compares God to a wise master who sees his slaves sinning. The master does not leave them unchecked. This shows that God's wisdom does not require preventing all sin.
The word 'يستدرجهم' implies gradual drawing.
5
Reflect on the personal note
Juwayni expresses his love for teaching this chapter, showing his passion for the subject. Consider how this personal touch connects to the importance of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قيل: كيف يريد الحكيم السفه؟ فقد سبق في قدر كاف شاف، لصدر كل ذى لب. وأوضحنا: أن الأفعال متساوية في حق من لا ينتفع ولا يتضرر. ولكن اذا أخبر أنه مكلف مطالب عنادة، مزيح عائلهم، فقوله الحق، وكلامه الصدق. وأقرب أمر بعا رضوان به: أن الحكيم منا اذا رأى جواريه وعبيده يموج بعضهم في بعض، وهم على محارمهم بمرآة منه ومسمع، فلا يحسن تركهم على ما هم عليه. والرب مطلع على سوء أفعال العباد ويستدرجهم من حيث لا يعلمون. وقد أطلت أنفاسي قليلا. ولكن - حرس الله مولانا - لو وجدت فى اقتباس هذا العلم من يسرد لى هذا الفصل لكان - وحق القائم على كل نفس بما كسبت - أحب الى من ملك الدنيا بحذافيرها طول أمدها.
If it is said: How can the Wise will foolishness? It has already preceded in a sufficient, curing decree for every possessor of intellect. And we have explained that actions are equal in relation to the One who neither benefits nor is harmed. But when He informs that He is a taskmaster demanding compliance, removing their excuse, then His word is the truth and His speech is the truth. And the nearest matter by which to be pleased is that the wise person among us, when he sees his slave girls and male slaves surging among each other, and they are violating their sanctities in his sight and hearing, then it is not good to leave them as they are. And the Lord is informed of the evil deeds of the servants and gradually draws them from where they do not know. And I have prolonged my breaths a little. But—may Allah guard our master—if I found in the acquisition of this knowledge someone who would recite to me this chapter, it would be—by the right of the One who stands over every soul for what it has earned—more beloved to me than possessing the entire world for its entire duration.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents another objection: How can the Wise God will foolishness (safah)? The author replies that this has already been covered: actions are equivalent in relation to the One who neither benefits nor is harmed. But when He informs that He is a taskmaster demanding compliance and removing their excuse, His word is truth. He then gives a comparison: a wise master who sees his slaves committing sins in his presence would not leave them unchecked. Similarly, the Lord is aware of the evil deeds of His servants and progressively draws them (yastadrijuhum) from where they do not know. The author then adds a personal note: he has prolonged his discussion, but if he had found someone to recite this chapter to him, it would be more beloved than the entire world.

السفه
مكلف
مطالب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's wisdom requires Him to prevent all sin.
Correction: Juwayni explains that actions are neutral for God; He may will them without foolishness, and His wisdom does not necessitate preventing all sin.

Checkpoint
How does Juwayni respond to the objection that the Wise God cannot will foolishness?
A) God's actions are beyond inquiry.
B) Actions are neutral in themselves for God, so willing them is not foolish.
C) God does not will evil, so the objection is invalid.
D) The objection is based on a misunderstanding of divine attributes.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni defends God's wisdom by showing that actions are inherently neutral for God, and that willing some evil does not contradict wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept that God's wisdom is beyond your comprehension, or do you secretly judge that God should have prevented certain sins in your life? Today, specifically, can you surrender that judgment and trust His wisdom even in the evil you see?

Are you living as if your sin matters more to God than it does (feeling overly guilty) or as if it doesn't matter at all (presuming on His patience)? Which is your tendency, and what one step will you take to correct it?
?
The analogy of the master and slaves: God sees all your sins but gradually draws you. Are you grateful for His patience, or are you taking advantage of His deferral? What specific sin are you persisting in because God hasn't stopped you yet? Will you repent today before the gradual drawing becomes a trap?

Nothing is obligatory upon God – the proof
Juwayni states the Ash'ari position that nothing is obligatory upon God and gives the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that nothing is obligatory upon God, based on the impossibility of harming or benefiting God.

Core Idea
Obligation only makes sense for beings that can be harmed or blamed; God is beyond both.

Juwayni begins by reporting the views of those who claim that reward and punishment are obligatory upon God. He then states the position of Ahl al-Sunna: nothing is obligatory upon God; His actions are either bounty or justice. The proof is concise but profound: obligation implies the possibility of blame or harm, and Allah is transcendent above such things. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing views
Read the first part of the passage where Juwayni mentions two groups who assert obligations upon God. What do they claim is obligatory?
These are likely Mu'tazili views.
2
Understand the position of Ahl al-Haqq
Notice the phrase 'nothing is obligatory upon God' and the distinction between bounty and justice.
This is the Ash'ari consensus.
3
Analyze the proof
Break down the proof: why is obligation only possible for one who can be harmed or blamed? How does this apply to God?
The key is that God is transcendent above harm and benefit.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this means for divine justice. Juwayni affirms that God's punishment is just, but not because it is obligatory.
This guards against the misconception that Ash'aris deny divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال قائلون : يجب على الله تبارك وتعالى ، أن يعاقبه ، ولا يجوز أن يعفو عنه ما لم يتب فإن تاب وجب عليه قبول توبته .. وذهب آخرون : الى أن العفو مسوغ فى العقل .. والثواب واجب على الله - تبارك وتعالى ، عن قولهم علوا كبيرا - من هذيان طويل ، وصار أهل الحق قاطبة : الى أنه لا يجب على الله شيء . فان أتاب وأنعم فيفضله ، وإن عاقب فبعدله . والدليل القاطع في تحقيق ما ارتضاه أهل الحق ، أن الوجوب انما يتحقق فى حق من لو فرض منه ترك الواجب لاستحق الذم واللائمة ، ولو ليم أو عوقب ، لناله ضرر ، والرب تبارك وتعالى يتقدس عن قبول الضر والنفع ، ولا يتحقق تفاوت الأفعال فى حكمه كما سبق .
Some said: It is obligatory upon Allah, the Blessed and Exalted, to punish him, and it is not permissible to forgive him unless he repents; and if he repents, then accepting his repentance is obligatory upon Him. And others went to the view that forgiveness is permissible in reason. And reward is obligatory upon Allah – high exalted is He above their saying – from lengthy nonsense. And the people of truth unanimously held that nothing is obligatory upon Allah. So if He grants repentance and bestows favor, it is by His bounty, and if He punishes, it is by His justice. And the decisive proof in confirming what the people of truth approved is that obligation is only realized in the case of one who, if he were supposed to abandon the obligatory, would deserve blame and censure, and if he were blamed or punished, harm would befall him. And the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, is transcendent above accepting harm and benefit, and no variation of actions is realized in His judgment, as has preceded.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Ash'ari position on divine obligation, followed by a proof. Juwayni first reports two opposing views: (1) that God must punish the sinner and must accept repentance (likely the Mu'tazili view), and (2) that forgiveness is permissible but reward is obligatory. He dismisses these as 'lengthy nonsense'. Then he states the position of 'the people of truth' (Ahl al-Haqq) that nothing is obligatory upon God; if He grants repentance and favors, it is by His bounty, and if He punishes, it is by His justice. The proof is that obligation only makes sense for a being who could be blamed or harmed by failing to do the obligatory, and God is transcendent above harm and benefit. Furthermore, actions have no inherent variation in His judgment (i.e., good and evil are not intrinsic). This proof relies on the impossibility of affecting God.

Key Terms
يجب
الوجوب
أهل الحق
الضر والنفع
تفاوت الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'aris deny God's justice; rather they affirm that God's actions are not subject to external obligation.
Correction: Juwayni's proof shows that obligation is not applicable to God, but His justice is affirmed in His punishment: 'if He punishes, it is by His justice.' The Ash'ari position does not deny divine justice; it denies that God is bound by external obligations.

Checkpoint
According to the proof given, why is nothing obligatory upon God?
A) Because God is generous and always rewards.
B) Because obligation only applies to one who can be harmed or blamed, and God is beyond harm.
C) Because the Shari'a does not impose obligations on God.
D) Because human reason cannot know obligation.

Key Takeaway
Nothing is obligatory upon God because obligation requires the possibility of harm or blame, and Allah is beyond both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe nothing is obligatory upon God, how does that reshape your plea for forgiveness tonight? Will you beg as a desperate slave, or assume He must accept your repentance?
?
When you consider your greatest sin, do you rely on the fact that God's mercy is His bounty (not an obligation)? What if He chose justice instead? Does that thought drive you to sincere repentance now?
?
If God's actions are not bound by external standards of fairness, how does that affect your trust in His decree when you face hardship? Can you still say 'He is just' without human preconceptions of justice?

The Way of the People of Truth and a Secret of Tawhid
Juwayni concludes reward/punishment and hints at a tawhid secret.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni concludes the discussion on reward and punishment by grounding it in God's promise, and you will be introduced to the idea of a profound secret of tawhid that transcends human capability.

Core Idea
Reward is by promise, not desert; tawhid holds a secret beyond human capacity.

Imam al-Juwayni brings the section on reward and punishment to a close by citing the verse of the blessed ones in Paradise. Their praise is for God's fulfilled promise — not for any inherent right. Then, without warning, he announces a secret of tawhid so weighty that all human capacity could not match its worth. This lesson unpacks that transition and the meaning of the verse, while setting the stage for the secret that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from concluding reward and punishment to the sudden announcement of a secret.
The passage ends mid-sentence. Observe how Juwayni uses the verse to affirm his doctrine.
2
Understand the significance of the verse
The verse from Surah Az-Zumar (39:74) is quoted as the meaning of the speech of the blessed ones (ahl al-jannah). Identify why Juwayni considers this verse encapsulating the doctrine of the people of truth on reward and punishment.
The key point: reward is a fulfillment of God's promise, not a due recompense for human deeds.
3
Reflect on the announcement of the secret
Juwayni declares he will reveal a secret of tawhid. Note his assessment: if compared to all human capability, it would not be equivalent. Ask yourself: what kind of secret could be so profound?
The secret is likely a theological point affirming God's absolute sovereignty and the limits of human reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا معنى قول السعداء فيما أخبر الله تبارك وتعالى عنهم وقالوا : الحمد لله الذى صدقنا وعده وأورثنا الأرض ) ( الزمر : ٧٤ ( فهذا مذهب أهل الحق في الثواب والعقاب وأنا الآن أبدى سرا من أسرار التوحيد . لو قوبل بكل ما يدخل في مقدور البشر وميسوره لما كان كفاء له . فأقول : ذهب الصائرون

Commentary

(probably beginning of the secret). This serves as a transition to the next topic.

Key Takeaway
Juwayni summarizes the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq on reward as God's fulfillment of His promise, and then signals a profound secret of tawhid that transcends all human capability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The secret of tawhid surpasses all human capability. In your daily life, do you reduce God to what you can understand, or do you embrace the mystery? Today, will you intentionally acknowledge a limit to your own understanding and submit to God’s transcendence?
?
If this secret is beyond all human capacity, then your intellect alone cannot grasp it. Are you willing to accept truths from revelation that you cannot fully rationalize? What step can you take this week to humble your intellect before divine mystery?

The Metaphorical Nature of Love for God
Juwayni refutes literal love of God and offers metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Juwayni argues that love for God cannot be literal and must be interpreted metaphorically in terms of divine intention and human obedience.

Core Idea
Divine love is not literal affection but God's intention to bless and the servant's steadfast obedience.

Juwayni confronts a common claim: that humans can truly love God. He argues that since God is transcendent and humans are driven by interests, love cannot be literal. Instead, he reinterprets it in terms of divine will and human obedience, guarding against anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the strong opening: 'And because of this, the statement of those who claim to love God truly collapses.'
Pay attention to the structure: refutation, reason, reinterpretation.
2
Identify the refutation
Juwayni refutes the claim of literal love by stating God's transcendence above being an object of interest (hazz). Humans always act to repel harm or gain benefit.
The key term is 'الحظ' (interest/fortune).
3
Understand the reason
Because God is sanctified (mutakaddis) from inclination, partisanship, tenderness, and longing, love cannot be literal.
This is based on divine transcendence (tanzih).
4
Grasp the metaphorical interpretation
Juwayni redefines love: God's love for His servant is His intention to bestow goodness; the servant's love for God is steadfastness in obedience.
This avoids anthropomorphism while preserving the scriptural terms.
5
Reflect on the goal
Ask yourself: How does this reinterpretation protect God's transcendence? Why is literal love problematic?
This connects to the broader Islamic principle of tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن هذا اضمحل قول من ادعى محبة الله حقا. فان وجوده متعال عن أن يحظى به ذو حظ. والمخلوق تداوره على الحظوظ والأغراض التي يجمعها دفع الضرر وجلب النفع والمحبة الله تبارك وتعالى غير محمولة على حقيقتها ظاهرا فانه متقدس عن الميل والتحيز والرقة والتوقان. فمحبة الله تبارك وتعالى لعبده: ارادته الانعام عليه، ومحبة العبد لربه: استقامته في طاعته. وهو متقدس لعز جلاله، عن أن يناله حظ، أو ينال حظا.
And because of this, the statement of those who claim to love God truly collapses. For His existence is transcendent above being attained by any possessor of interest. And the created being revolves around interests and aims, which are summarized as repelling harm and attracting benefit. And love of God, blessed and exalted, is not taken according to its literal reality, for He is sanctified above inclination, partisanship, tenderness, and longing. So God's love for His servant is His intending goodness for him, and the servant's love for his Lord is his steadfastness in obedience to Him. And He is sanctified by the might of His majesty from being reached by any interest, or attaining any interest.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of those who say they truly love God (mahabbat Allah haqqan). Since God is transcendent (muta'āl) and free from being an object of interest (hazz), the creature is always seeking interests (repelling harm, gaining benefit). Therefore, love of God cannot be literal; it must be interpreted. God's love for the servant means His intention to bestow goodness (irada al-in'am). The servant's love for God means his steadfastness in obedience (istiqamah fi ta'atihi). This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) regarding divine love.

Key Terms
محبة الله
الحظ
التأويل
الإرادة
الاستقامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think humans can literally love God in an anthropomorphic emotional sense.
Correction: Juwayni shows that God is beyond human emotions and attributes; love must be understood metaphorically as divine will and human obedience.

Checkpoint

A) Literal affection.
B) Steadfastness in obedience.
C) Seeking reward.
D) Annihilation in God.

Key Takeaway
Love for God is not anthropomorphic emotion but God's intention to bless and the servant's obedient steadfastness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If love for God is defined as steadfastness in obedience, where in your life do you claim to love God but lack obedience? Which specific command of His are you ignoring, and what will you do about it today?

When you worship, are you seeking God's pleasure or your own benefit? Examine your intentions this past week: did you pray to feel good, or to truly obey? Commit to one act of worship this week solely for God's sake, expecting nothing in return.
?
The passage says God cannot be attained by any interest. Are you trying to 'use' God for worldly gain? Repent from treating Him as a means to an end, and resolve to serve Him as the ultimate end.

Definition and Division of Provision
Juwayni defines rizq, divides it into halal and haram, and affirms God as sole provider.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's definition of provision (rizq), its division into halal, haram, and non-moral categories, and the affirmation that Allah alone is the Provider.

Core Idea
Provision is whatever benefits; only Allah provides.

This lesson introduces a foundational concept in Islamic theology: provision (rizq). Imam al-Juwayni defines rizq broadly to include anything beneficial, then divides it into lawful and unlawful, and even the provision of animals. He concludes by affirming that Allah alone is the Provider, reinforcing tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's definition
Carefully read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the author's own words on rizq.
Notice that the definition is functional: whatever benefits is provision.
2
Understand the broad scope
The definition covers all beneficial things, not just food or wealth.
3
Identify the three categories
Locate the division into halal, haram, and non-moral (like animal provision).
The third category is not described as halal or haram.
4
Grasp the theological conclusion
Note the final sentence: Allah is the Provider, none else provides or creates.
This connects rizq to tawhid.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some think haram is not provision, but Juwayni includes it because it still provides benefit in this world.
This highlights the difference between worldly benefit and religious approval.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الرزق: فكل ما انتفع به منتفع فهو رزقه. ثم الرزق ينقسم الى الحلال والحرام، والى ما لا يتصف بالتحليل والتحريم كرزق البهائم. فالله الرازق، ولا رازق غيره، ولا خالق سواه.
As for provision (rizq): Everything that a beneficiary benefits from is his provision. Then provision is divided into halal and haram, and into what is not described as halal or haram, like the provision of beasts. So Allah is the Provider, and there is no provider other than Him, and no creator besides Him.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of provision (rizq). The author defines it functionally: whatever brings benefit is provision for the one who benefits from it. He then classifies it into three types: halal, haram, and that which is neither (like the natural provision for animals). Finally, he asserts that God alone is the Provider (al-Razzaq) and the sole Creator, emphasizing tawhid in provision.

Key Terms

الحرام
الرازق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think that haram (unlawful provision) is not actually provision because it is sinful to consume.
Correction: Juwayni includes haram as provision because one can still benefit from it in this world, even though it is unlawful.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Provision is anything beneficial, whether lawful or unlawful, and Allah alone is the ultimate Provider.

Allah's Provision Includes Both Lawful and Unlawful
Juwayni affirms that all provision is from Allah, refuting those who exclude oppressors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all provision (rizq) comes from Allah, including both lawful and unlawful means, and that denying this contradicts Allah's universal sustenance.

Core Idea
All provision is from Allah, whether halal or haram.

Imam Juwayni concludes his discussion on divine provision by affirming a crucial point: Allah's sustenance covers all creatures, regardless of whether they obtain it through lawful or unlawful means. He warns against the mistaken belief that oppressors and wrongdoers are outside Allah's provision, which would contradict the clear Quranic verse that every creature's provision is upon Allah. This passage solidifies the universality of Allah's provision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal translation. Notice the footnote markers (1) but do not let them distract from the argument.
The markers likely indicate textual variants; the core meaning remains clear.
2
Identify the key claim Juwayni refutes
Find the statement Juwayni rejects: the claim that oppressors and those who engage in [unlawful transactions] are not included in Allah's provision. Understand why this is problematic.
Juwayni says this would exclude most creatures from being sustained by Allah.
3
Understand the Quranic evidence
Reflect on the verse from Surah Hud (11:6) that every creature's provision is upon Allah. See how it directly supports Juwayni's point that no one is outside Allah's provision.
4
Reflect on the implication for tawheed
Consider why it is important to affirm that all provision, both halal and haram, is from Allah. How does this uphold Allah's sovereignty and sustainer attribute?
It prevents a misconception that limits Allah's provision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أنه تبارك وتعالى قسم أرزاق العباد حلالا وحراما ، كما صرفهم بحكمة فى الطاعات والزلات ، توفيقا وخذلانا ، وعطاء وحرمانا . ومن زعم أن الظلمة والذين يتعاطون (۱) ، ليسوا فى رزق الله ، فقد أخرج معظم الخلائق فى معظم الأوقات (1) عن كونهم مرتزقة الله تعالى . وقال تبارك وتعالى : ( وما من دابة فى الأرض الا على الله رزقها ) هود : ٦.
Then, He (Blessed and Exalted) divided the provisions of the servants into lawful and unlawful, just as He directed them by wisdom in acts of obedience and slips, granting success and abandoning, giving and depriving. And whoever claims that the oppressors and those who engage in (1) are not in Allah's provision has removed most of the creatures most of the time (1) from being sustained by Allah the Exalted. And He (Blessed and Exalted) said: 'There is no creature on earth but its provision is upon Allah' (Hud:6).
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a concluding argument about divine provision (rizq). It affirms that Allah divides provisions into lawful and unlawful, and that He directs people by wisdom in their actions—whether obedience or sin, through granting success (tawfiq) or abandonment (khidhlan), giving or withholding. Juwayni then refutes the claim that oppressors and those who engage in [unlawful transactions] are not within Allah's provision. He argues that such a claim excludes most creatures from being sustained by Allah, which contradicts the Quranic verse (Hud:6) that every creature's provision is from Allah. The point is that all provision, whether halal or haram, comes from Allah's decree, and denying this undermines His universal sustenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only lawful provision comes from Allah, and that unlawful provision is not from Him.
Correction: Juwayni affirms that Allah provides both halal and haram. The Qur'anic verse (11:6) covers all creatures, so no one's provision is outside Allah's decree.

Checkpoint

B) They have removed most creatures from being sustained by Allah.
C) They are referring only to lawful provision.
D) They are referring to a specific group of oppressors.

Key Takeaway
Allah's provision encompasses all creatures, whether they obtain it lawfully or unlawfully, as affirmed by the Qur'an.
