Analogy of Human Internal Speech to God's Eternal Speech
Juwayni explains the eternity of God's speech using an analogy with human internal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's analogy that God's eternal speech (al-kalam al-qa'im bi nafsihi) is like human internal speech that exists before utterance, emphasizing its pre-existence and eternity.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal in His essence, just as our internal thoughts exist before we speak.

Juwayni uses a relatable human experience—planning what to say to a friend—to explain a profound theological truth: God's speech is not created but eternal. This passage anchors the doctrine of divine speech as a subsisting attribute (sifah qa'imah) in God's essence, linking it to His eternal power and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Don't worry about detailed analysis yet; let the author's flow come through.
Notice the repetition of 'لم تزل' (never ceases) which emphasizes eternity.
2
Identify the analogy
Juwayni compares God's eternal speech to human internal speech arranged before speaking. Find the sentence beginning with 'كما أن الانسان' and understand the comparison.
The analogy uses a human action (planning speech) to illustrate a divine attribute.
3
Trace the argument
Follow Juwayni's reasoning: from God's eternal knowledge to the eternity of speech and power as attributes. Notice how he links speech to power as both never ceasing.
The phrase 'كسبيل قدرته القديمة' (like the way of His eternal power) is key.
4
Understand the conclusion
The final lines affirm that God's speech never ceases, just like His power. Reflect on how this analogy resolves potential confusion about the temporal nature of revelation.
Juwayni concludes that God's attributes are eternal and never cease.

والرب فى أزله كان عالما بأنه يتعبد عباده اذا وجدوا وهو العالم المقدس عن أن يسهو أو يهفو فلا يخلو وجوده الأزلى عن معنى ما سيصل الى العباد اذا وجدوا : وسبيل ذلك الكلام القائم بنفسه كسبيل قدرته القديمة ولم تزل. يريد أن يقول : كما أن الانسان لو أراد أن يحدث صاحبا له بعد شهر فى أمر ما ، يرتب كلاما في نفسه ليقوله لصاحبه بعد شهر . فاذا جاء الشهر نطق بالكلام الذى كان قد رتبه فى نفسه ذلك. وهذا الانسان قد أراد وقد أوجد معانى فى نفسه ثم نطق بهذه المعاني . ومع هو وصفاته شيء واحد من قبل . كذلك الله وجل - والله المثل الأعلى - صفاته من قبل وما تزال الكلام القائم بنفسه كسبيل قدرته القديمة . ولم تزل.
And the Lord in His pre-eternity was knowing that He will worship servants when they exist, and He is the Holy One, far above forgetfulness or error, so His pre-eternal existence is not devoid of the meaning of what will reach the servants when they exist. And the way of that speech subsisting in His essence is like the way of His eternal power, and it never ceases. He means to say: Just as if a person wants to speak to his companion after a month about a matter, he arranges speech in himself to say to his companion after a month, then when the month comes, he utters the speech that he had arranged in himself. And this person has willed and has brought into existence meanings in himself, then he utters those meanings. And he, with his attributes, is one thing before. Likewise, God Almighty – and to God belongs the highest similitude – His attributes are from before and His speech subsisting in His essence never ceases, like the way of His eternal power, and it never ceases.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents an analogy to explain the eternity of God's speech (kalam). Juwayni begins by stating that God, in His pre-eternity, knew that He would worship His servants when they exist. God is holy and free from forgetfulness or error, so His pre-eternal existence necessarily includes the meaning of what will reach the servants. The speech that subsists in God's essence (al-kalam al-qa'im bi nafsihi) is likened to His eternal power (qudrah qadimah) – both are eternal and never cease. Then Juwayni elaborates: just as a human being, intending to speak to a friend after a month, arranges speech internally and later utters it, so God's speech is intrinsically eternal, and when He wishes to convey it, He brings it into existence in the form of revealed words. The human's internal speech exists before utterance; similarly, God's speech is eternal in His essence. The conclusion is that God's attributes, including speech and power, are eternal and never cease.

Correction: Juwayni clarifies that God's speech is eternal in His essence, like His power; it is not created but subsists in Him and is expressed in time.

The Phrase 'لم يزل' and the Inseparability of God's Speech
Juwayni defends the phrase 'لم يزل' to affirm God's speech as inseparable from His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Juwayni insists on using the phrase 'لم يزل' to affirm that God's speech is an eternal attribute inseparable from His essence, similar to His will and power.

Core Idea
God's speech, like His will and power, is eternal and never ceases.

In discussing God's speech, Juwayni emphasizes that we must use the term 'لم يزل' to affirm its eternity. He argues that just as God's will and power are eternal attributes subsisting in His essence, so is His speech. This analogy clarifies that God's command 'Be' is not a temporal event but an eternal expression that brings about creation in time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the full literal translation. Let Juwayni's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the key terms like 'لم يزل' and 'كلام الله الأزلى'.
2
Identify Juwayni's key claim
What is the central point Juwayni is making about God's speech? Look for his explicit statement that God's speech does not separate from the essence.
Also note the phrase 'لم يزل' is both a claim and a required expression.
3
Examine the analogy with will and power
How does Juwayni use the analogy of God's will (إرادة) and power (قدرة) to support his argument? What is the relationship between the eternal attribute and its temporal effect?
The example of 'Be' (كن) illustrates that the speech is eternal while creation is contingent.

ولما تحدث في « كلام الله » لم يمش على تعبيره « ولم يزل » ذلك أنه أثبت الله كلاما لم ينفصل عنه في قوله « كلام الله الأزلى لا يفارق الذات ولا يزايلها » وابن كان يقصد بهذه العبارة « النظم الدال على المعنى المتحقق لفظا ومعنى فى علم الله أزلا ( كترتيب الانسان كلام في نفسه ليؤديه الى صاحبه بعد شهر فلا اعتراض عليه . لأنه يكون كارادته و قدرته من قبل أن يحدث الله الذي أراده . فاذا أحدث الذي أراده فان الذى حدث يكون حادثا • كارادته خلق العالم أزلا فانه لما خلق العالم صار العالم منفصلا بالارادة ومخلوقا حادثا . كذلك لو تكلم فقال كن » مثلا . فان « كن » تعتبر فى المعنى كخلق العالم بعد أن كان فكرة . وكما تشاهد قدرة الله لا تزال ، كذلك كلامه لا يزال أو بتعبير الجويني نفسه « ولم يزل » لقد ظهرت قدرات كثيرة الله على طول الزمان
And when he spoke about 'the speech of God', he did not proceed with his expression 'لم يزل' because he affirmed that God has speech that is not separate from Him, in his saying: 'God's eternal speech does not separate from the essence nor does it leave it.' And Ibn [Kullab?] meant by this expression: 'The organized structure indicating the meaning realized in word and meaning in God's knowledge eternally, like the arrangement of a person's speech in himself to convey it to his companion after a month, so there is no objection to it. Because it is like His will and power before God brings about what He willed. So when He brings about what He willed, then what occurs is contingent. Like His willing the creation of the world eternally, for when He created the world, the world became separate by His will and created, contingent. Similarly, if He spoke and said 'Be' for example, then 'Be' is considered in meaning like the creation of the world after it was an idea. And just as you observe that God's power does not cease, likewise His speech does not cease, or in Juwayni's own expression 'لم يزل'. Indeed, many powers of God have appeared over time.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage discusses the theological phrase 'لم يزل' (never ceases) used for God's attributes. Juwayni explains that when the topic of God's speech (kalam Allah) is addressed, one should use the expression 'لم يزل' to affirm that God's speech is eternal and inseparable from His essence. He quotes the statement: 'God's eternal speech does not separate from the essence nor does it leave it.' This is attributed to Ibn Kullab (or Ibn?). The meaning is that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, like His will (iradah) and power (qudrah). Just as God's will to create the world is eternal and the actual creation is contingent, similarly God's command 'Be' is an eternal speech that brings about contingent creation. The analogy with a person arranging speech internally before utterance reinforces that the internal speech is prior and eternal. Juwayni concludes that just as God's power is observed to be eternal and manifest over time, so His speech is eternal. The phrase 'لم يزل' is thus appropriate for affirming the eternity of God's speech.

Key Terms
لم يزل
كلام الله الأزلى
الذات
المعنى
النظم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because God's speech is heard in time (e.g., the Quran revealed to prophets), it is a created attribute that began in time.
Correction: Juwayni argues that God's speech is eternal and inseparable from His essence; its temporal manifestation (like the command 'Be') does not imply that the speech itself is created. The speech is eternal, like His will and power.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what does the expression 'لم يزل' affirm about God's speech?
A) That it is created in time
B) That it is separate from God's essence
C) That it is eternal and inseparable from the essence
D) That it is only metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Juwayni insists on using 'لم يزل' to emphasize that God's speech is eternal and inseparable from His essence, akin to His will and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is eternal and inseparable from His essence, then every time you hear the Qur'an, you are encountering a permanent attribute of God—something that has never ceased to exist. How does that truth change the way you listen to or recite the Qur'an? What specific practice will you adopt to honor that reality starting today?
?
Juwayni uses the phrase 'لم يزل' to defend the eternity of God's speech. But examine your own heart: have you ever treated God's attributes—His speech, His will, His power—as if they could change or fail? Recall a moment when you doubted God's consistency. What step will you take to root your trust in the unchangeable nature of God?
?
The analogy of internal speech versus spoken words compares God's eternal attribute with its temporal expression. In your own life, you often express yourself through words and actions. Do you ever reflect that your words come and go, but God's speech remains eternally? How does that contrast affect your desire to align your own speech with the eternal truth of God's words?

Eternal Power Requires Eternal Speech
Juwayni argues that eternal power implies eternal speech via prophetic history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming God's eternal power logically requires affirming His eternal speech, based on the manifestation of both in prophetic history.

Core Idea
Eternal power and eternal speech stand or fall together.

Imam Juwayni presents a concise but powerful argument from the history of prophets. He points out that God's power has been at work saving prophets across centuries, and His speech has been revealed in scriptures. Since both are manifestations of divine attributes that have been active throughout time, consistency demands that if we affirm one as eternal, we must affirm the other as eternal. This lesson examines that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the names of prophets and the term 'لم تزل' (never cease).
2
Identify the two manifestations
Juwayni mentions two types of divine activity: saving prophets (power) and revealing scriptures (speech). Identify these in the text.
3
Understand the logical implication
Juwayni argues that if power is eternal, then speech must also be eternal because both are manifested similarly across time. Reflect on the logic of this analogy.
This is the core of the proof.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the misconception that because scriptures were revealed at specific times, God's speech is temporal. How does Juwayni's argument counter this?
The temporal event does not make the attribute temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد قدر على نجاة نوح عليه السلام. ومن بعثة ابراهيم عليه السلام ومن بعده موسى عليه السلام ومن بعدهم . وبين كل نبي وغيره سنين عديدة . وكذلك ظهر كلام الله تعالى في صحف ابراهيم وموسى ومحمد عليهم الصلاة والسلام .. فمن أثبت قدرات لم تزل يلزمه اثبات كلام لم يزل
For He [God] had power over the salvation of Noah, peace be upon him. And from the mission of Abraham, peace be upon him, and after him Moses, peace be upon him, and after them. And between each prophet and other [events] are many years. And likewise the speech of God Almighty appeared in the scriptures of Abraham, Moses, and Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon them. So whoever affirms powers that never cease, he must affirm speech that never ceases.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (dalil) from the history of prophets. Juwayni argues that God's power (qudrah) is eternal and has been manifested throughout history in saving prophets like Noah, Abraham, Moses, and others. Similarly, God's speech (kalam) has appeared in scriptures given to Abraham, Moses, and Muhammad. Since God's power is universally acknowledged as eternal (لم تزل), consistency demands that His speech also be eternal (لم يزل). The argument is that the same divine attribute of eternity applies to both power and speech because both are manifested in temporal events (prophets' salvation and revelation of scriptures) but their source is eternal. This counters those who might affirm eternal power but deny eternal speech.

Key Terms

كلام
صحف
نبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because scriptures were revealed at specific times, God's speech is temporal and created.
Correction: Juwayni argues that the temporal revelation of scriptures is a manifestation of an eternal attribute, just as saving prophets at specific times manifests eternal power. The events are temporal, but the attribute is eternal.

Checkpoint

A) The preservation of the Qur'an
B) The salvation of prophets and revelation of scriptures
C) The creation of the world
D) The miracles of prophets

Key Takeaway
Juwayni establishes a logical connection: the same divine eternity that applies to power must apply to speech because both are manifested in history.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Would you still prioritize reading and obeying the Qur'an if you knew it was revealed centuries ago but remains eternally relevant? How does this lesson challenge any excuse you've made for not studying it?

Hearing the Qur'an and Reconciling Its Createdness
Juwayni explains hearing the Qur'an and proposes reconciliation on createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's clarification that hearing the Qur'an means hearing the reciter's voice, which conveys the eternal speech of God, and how this distinction could reconcile the dispute over whether the Qur'an is created or eternal.

Core Idea
Hearing the Qur'an means hearing the reciter's voice, not God's eternal speech directly.

Juwayni addresses a key theological dispute: the nature of the Qur'an as God's speech. He explains that when we hear the Qur'an recited, we are hearing a created voice that conveys the uncreated meaning. This distinction, he argues, could have resolved the famous controversy over whether the Qur'an is created or eternal. In this passage, he provides an analogy and cites a Qur'anic verse to support his view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Juwayni builds his argument: first stating the fact of hearing, then distinguishing between eternal speech and recited voice.
The passage is dense, so take your time.
2
Identify Juwayni's key distinction
Find where Juwayni says that 'hearing the speech of God' does not mean hearing the eternal attribute, but rather the voice of the reciter. Note how he uses the analogy of a king's message.
This distinction is crucial for the reconciliation.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Juwayni suggests that if people had understood speech (kalam) like they understood power (qudra)—as an eternal attribute with temporal manifestations—the controversy would not have occurred. Reflect on how this applies.
Both sides agree on God's oneness and eternal attributes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقرآن الكريم كلام الله سمعه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على النحو المذكور فى هذه الآية : وما كان البشر أن يكلمه الله الا وحيا أو من وراء حجاب أو يرسل رسولا فيوحى باذنه ما يشاء انه على حكيم ( الشورى : ٥ ) وأمر بحفظه في الصدور وبكتابته في الأوراق . فالذي حفظ ويحفظ لم يسمع صوت الله كما تلقى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم .. وهذا هو معنى قول الجويني رحمه الله « يجب إطلاق القول بأن كلام الله تبارك وتعالى مسموع ، وليس المراد بذلك تعلق الإدراك بالكلام الأزلى القائم بالبارى تعالى : ولكن المدرك صوت القارىء . والمفهوم عند قراءته كلام الله سبحانه ، ولا بعد في مسموع : تسمية المفهوم مسموعا . فهذا بمثابة ما لو بلغ مبلغ رسالة ملك فيحسن ممن بلغته الرسالة أن يقول سمعت الملك ورسالته ... الخ ) ولو أن الناس في زمن الامام أحمد بن حنبل - رحمه الله - فهموا الكلام كما فهموا القدرة لما قامت فتنة القول بخلق القرآن . واستطاع بعضهم أن يعذر بعضا فيما ذهبوا اليه . بل واستطاع من يريد التوفيق بين القول بقدم القرآن وخلقه أن يوفق . حيث يجمع الكل اعتراف بوحدانية الله الكامل . الصفات من قبل خلق العالم وأنه ما يزال للكوان حديث بعجائبه . وهذه الآية الكريمة ( وما كان لبشر أن يكلمه الله الا وحيا . أو وراء حجاب . أو يرسل رسولا فيوحى باذنه ما يشاء انه على حكيم تثبت الحديث المباشر بصوت بين الله والبشر بدون رؤية البشر لذات الله تعالى وذلك واضح من قوله أو من وراء حجاب .
And the Noble Qur'an is the speech of God. The Prophet, peace be upon him, heard it in the manner mentioned in this verse: 'And it is not for any human that God should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger to reveal by His permission what He wills. Indeed, He is Most High, All-Wise.' (al-Shura 42:51) And He commanded its preservation in chests and its writing in papers. So the one who preserved and preserves did not hear the voice of God as the Prophet received it. And this is the meaning of the saying of Juwayni, may God have mercy on him: 'It is necessary to state that the speech of God, blessed and exalted, is heard, but the intent is not the attachment of perception to the eternal speech subsisting in the Creator, exalted; rather, what is perceived is the voice of the reciter. And the understood meaning upon its recitation is the speech of God, exalted. And there is no difficulty in calling the understood meaning 'heard'. This is like the case when a message of a king reaches someone, then it is appropriate for the one who received the message to say, 'I heard the king and his message.' ...' And if the people at the time of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may God have mercy on him, had understood speech (kalam) as they understood power, the trial of the saying that the Qur'an is created would not have arisen. And some would have been able to excuse others for what they held. Rather, whoever wants reconciliation between the saying that the Qur'an is pre-eternal and created could reconcile. Where all agree on the acknowledgment of the complete oneness of God, the attributes before the creation of the world, and that it never ceases, the universe has a story of its wonders. And this noble verse (42:51) establishes direct speech with a voice between God and humans without humans seeing the essence of God Almighty, and that is clear from His saying 'or from behind a veil'.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage addresses the theological controversy over the createdness of the Qur'an. Juwayni quotes verse 42:51 to show that God speaks to humans in three ways: revelation, from behind a veil, or through a messenger. The Prophet heard the Qur'an in one of these ways, and it was preserved in hearts and writings. However, what is preserved is not the eternal speech itself but the reciter's voice; the meaning conveyed is God's speech. Juwayni clarifies that saying 'the speech of God is heard' means the recited words, not the eternal attribute. He uses the analogy of a king's message: hearing the message is called hearing the king. If people during Ahmad ibn Hanbal's time had understood this distinction between God's eternal speech (as an attribute) and its temporal expression, the 'trial of the created Qur'an' would not have occurred. Reconciling the two views is possible because both affirm God's oneness and that His attributes are eternal. The verse is then re-emphasized to show that God's direct speech to prophets involves a voice but no vision of His essence.

Juwayni explains that we hear the recited Qur'an as a temporal expression of God's eternal speech, which resolves the apparent conflict between the Qur'an being created and uncreated.

Juwayni says that if we understood speech as we understand power, the conflict would dissolve. In your own life, where do you hold onto conflicts because you refuse to see the distinction between the eternal and the temporal? How can you apply this principle of reconciliation today?

The Hand of Allah: Applying the Muhkam to a Mutashabih Verse
Juwayni applies the muhkam to the hand verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni uses the muhkam verse 'Nothing is like unto Him' to determine the metaphorical meaning of a mutashabih verse about Allah's hand.

Core Idea
The muhkam verse resolves ambiguity by ruling out literal interpretations that imply similarity.

Juwayni now gives a concrete example of the principle he established. The verse about Allah's hand is a classic case of ambiguity (mutashabih). It could mean a literal hand or power. By referring to the clear muhkam verse that negates any similarity to creation, we determine that the intended meaning is power, not a limb. This demonstrates the proper method of interpreting mutashabih verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible meanings
Read the passage and note that the verse 'The hand of Allah is over their hands' admits two interpretations: a literal hand (limb) and power (qudra).
The ambiguity arises from the word 'hand' which has both literal and metaphorical uses.
2
Understand the role of the muhkam verse
Juwayni states that because the verse is mutashabih, we must refer to the muhkam verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' which has only one clear meaning: absolute dissimilarity between Allah and creation.
3
See the conclusion and the rejected phrase
The muhkam verse negates any similarity, so the literal hand is impossible; we adopt the meaning 'power'. Juwayni explicitly rejects saying 'hand but not like hands' because that still affirms a hand, violating the muhkam.
The correct affirmation is to describe Allah with perfection and transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمثال الأعضاء قوله تعالى : «يد الله فوق أيديهم» ( الفتح ۱۰ ) فان هذا القول متشابه لاحتماله معنيين. الأول : اليد الحقيقية أي الجارحة كيد الانسان والثاني : أنه ليس بمعنى اليد الحقيقية بل بمعنى القدرة أي قدرة الله فوق قدرة الناس . ولما كان هذا القول متشابها فانه يتعين الرجوع الى الآية المحكمة التي لا تحتمل الا معنى واحدا وهي ليس كمثله شيء ) ( الشورى ) (۱۱) وحيث أنها تنفي مشابهة الله للانسان فاذن يجب الأخذ بالمعنى الثاني وهو القدرة ، وترك المعنى الأول وهو اليد الحقيقية . ولا نقول الله يد ولكن ليست كأيدي البشر لأنه » ليس كمثله شيء » بل نقول : الله واحد متصف بكل كمال ومنزه عن كل نقص وليس كمثله شيء .
So an example of body parts is His saying: 'The hand of Allah is over their hands' (48:10). This saying is mutashabih because it admits two meanings. First: the real hand, i.e., the limb like the hand of a human. Second: that it is not in the meaning of a real hand but in the meaning of power, i.e., the power of Allah is above the power of people. And since this saying is mutashabih, it is necessary to refer to the muhkam verse which does not admit except one meaning, and it is 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11). And since it negates the similarity of Allah to humans, then it is obligatory to adopt the second meaning, which is power, and to leave the first meaning, which is the real hand. And we do not say 'Allah has a hand, but it is not like the hands of humans,' because 'There is nothing like unto Him.' Rather, we say: Allah is One, described with every perfection, transcendent above every deficiency, and nothing is like unto Him.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage applies the principle from the previous lesson. It takes the verse about the 'hand' of Allah – a classic mutashabih. Juwayni explains that it has two possible meanings: literal (limb) and metaphorical (power). Because the muhkam verse 'Nothing is like unto Him' negates any similarity to creation, the literal meaning is impossible, so the metaphorical meaning (power) is taken. He explicitly rejects the phrase 'hand but not like hands' because that still affirms a hand of some kind, which violates the muhkam. Instead, he affirms that Allah is described with perfection and transcends any deficiency. This refutes both anthropomorphism and the attempt to affirm attributes without ta'wil while claiming negation of tashbih.

Key Terms
يد
قدرة
محكم
متشابه
تشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is acceptable to say 'Allah has a hand but not like human hands' as a way of affirming the attribute while negating tashbih.
Correction: Juwayni rejects this because it still affirms a hand, which implies similarity. The muhkam verse 'Nothing is like unto Him' demands that we not affirm any hand at all. Instead, we interpret 'hand' as power.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, what is the correct meaning of 'hand' in the verse 'The hand of Allah is over their hands'?
A) A real hand but not like human hands
B) Power (qudra)
C) The same as a human hand
D) We should not interpret it

Key Takeaway
The muhkam verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' is the decisive criterion for interpreting ambiguous verses about Allah's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'The hand of Allah is over their hands,' does your mind instinctively try to picture a hand? Will you surrender that image to the muhkam verse, even if it feels less tangible?
?
Juwayni rejects even saying 'a hand but not like hands' because it still implies similarity. Are there areas in your understanding of Allah where you cling to comfortable comparisons, even while verbally denying them? What would it take to let go completely?
?
If 'There is nothing like unto Him' truly governed your speech, how would it change the way you describe Allah in your prayers, your conversations, and your thoughts? Will you commit to guarding your tongue from any hint of resemblance starting today?

The Salaf's Metaphorical Understanding of Forgetfulness
Juwayni uses forgetfulness verse to demonstrate salaf's metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni uses the verse 'They forgot Allah, so He forgot them' to demonstrate that the salaf interpreted certain divine attributes metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
The salaf interpreted forgetfulness as neglect, not a literal attribute of Allah.

Juwayni continues his argument against affirming unintelligible attributes by posing a challenge: what about verses that speak of Allah forgetting? He shows that the salaf understood such verses as metaphors, not literal descriptions. This lesson examines his reasoning and the examples he provides.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Juwayni's argument come through before you interpret.
Notice how he uses the same logic as the hand attribute.
2
Identify the two possible meanings
The passage presents two meanings of 'forgetfulness' in the verse: literal forgetfulness and metaphorical neglect. Find each one and see which Juwayni says is correct.
3
Understand why the salaf chose the metaphorical meaning
Ask yourself why the salaf would interpret this verse figuratively. Juwayni says it is because they always upheld tanzih (transcendence) for Allah. How does this connect to the principle of affirming attributes without similarity?
This step ties back to the earlier discussion on hand and other attributes.

وإذا لم نقل بذلك وأثبتنا اليد مع نفي المماثلة فماذا نقول في مثل قوله تعالى نسوا الله فنسيهم ؟ هل تثبت نسيانا لله مع المماثلة ؟ إن من يثبت نسيانا لله مع عدم مماثلة نسيان الله النسيان البشر يكون كافرا وبعيدا كل البعد عن رحمة الله . ومثال صفات الأحاسيس نسوا الله فنسيهم ( التوبة : ٦٧ ) وهي تحتمل معنيين النسيان الحقيقي والكناية عن الإهمال أي أهملوا تعاليم الله وأغفلوا ذكره فأهملهم الله وتركهم من رحمته . أي خلى بينهم وبين أهواتهم. والمعنى الكنائي هو المراد . لما قلنا ، وهذا هو فهم السلف . فما سمعنا عن أحد منهم غير التنزيه لله عز وجل . وإلا يكن هذا فهمهم . فما هو تأويلهم لمثل قوله تعالى : ( نسوا الله فنسيهم ) وقوله عن سفينة نوح عليه السلام : « تجري بأعيننا » ( القمر : ١٤ ) وهل كانوا يفهمون أن للمقادير - وهي معنوية - أعنة كأعنة الخيول السريعة الجري في قول الشاعر : دع المقادير تجري في أعنتها ولا تبيتن إلا خالي البالي ما بين طرفة عين وانتباهتها تغير الله من حال إلى حال ؟
And if we did not say that and we affirm the hand with negation of similarity, then what do we say about such as His saying: 'They forgot Allah, so He forgot them'? Do you affirm forgetfulness for Allah with similarity? Indeed, whoever affirms forgetfulness for Allah while there is no similarity between Allah's forgetfulness and human forgetfulness becomes a disbeliever and far from the mercy of Allah. And an example of attributes of sensations is 'They forgot Allah, so He forgot them' (9:67). It admits two meanings: real forgetfulness and kinayah (metaphor) for neglect, i.e., they neglected Allah's teachings and forgot His remembrance, so He neglected them and left them from His mercy, i.e., He left them to their desires. And the metaphorical meaning is intended, as we said, and this is the understanding of the salaf. For we have not heard from any of them except tanzih (transcendence) of Allah Almighty. If this were not their understanding, then what is their ta'wil of such as His saying: 'They forgot Allah, so He forgot them' and His saying about the ship of Nuh: 'It sails under Our eyes' (54:14)? And did they understand that fate (which is conceptual) has reins like the reins of fast-running horses, in the poet's saying: 'Leave fate to run in its reins, and do not stay except carefree; between the blink of an eye and its opening, Allah changes a state to another state'?
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage continues the argument against affirming literal attributes while negating tashbih. Juwayni poses a challenge: if you affirm a hand while negating similarity, what would you do with the attribute of forgetfulness? You would have to either affirm it literally (which implies similarity) or explain it away. He argues that affirming literal forgetfulness while denying similarity leads to kufr because it affirms an imperfection in Allah. Then he presents the example of forgetfulness (nisyan) from Quran 9:67. He explains that it has two meanings: real forgetfulness (impossible for Allah) and metaphorical neglect (kinayah). The salaf understood it as the latter. He then cites other examples: the ark sailing under Allah's 'eyes' and the poetic imagery of fate having 'reins.' The salaf would interpret these figuratively, not literally. This reinforces the method of tafwid and metaphorical interpretation when necessary, based on the muhkam principle.

تأويل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the salaf interpreted all verses literally without any figurative interpretation.
Correction: Juwayni shows that the salaf understood 'forgetfulness' in the verse as a metaphor for neglect, not a literal attribute of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The salaf interpreted verses like 'They forgot Allah, so He forgot them' as metaphors for neglect, preserving Allah's transcendence and avoiding anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The salaf were unanimous in their metaphorical understanding of such verses. Does your study of Allah’s attributes reflect the same deep reverence and caution, or have you been content with surface-level readings? What concrete step can you take today to align your understanding more closely with the salaf’s approach of tanzih?

Affirming Divine Attributes without Tashbih: The Example of Forgetting
Defends metaphorical interpretation of divine attributes like hand and forgetting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributes like 'hand' and 'forgetting' must be interpreted metaphorically to preserve divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are affirmed but never like creation; problematic ones require metaphorical interpretation.

This passage from Imam Juwayni tackles a critical issue: how to affirm attributes mentioned in the Quran without falling into anthropomorphism. Using the example of 'hand' and 'forgetting', he shows that the Salaf understood such verses through metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil) to protect Allah's transcendence. Let's examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Read the opening lines where the author affirms the attribute of 'hand' but explicitly negates any similarity to human hands. Notice the quote 'There is nothing like unto Him'.
This principle applies to all attributes.
2
Analyze the problem with 'forgetting'
The author extends the same logic to the attribute of 'forgetting'. Consider the dilemma: if we simply affirm it without clarifying, we might imply a deficiency. The verse 'They forgot Allah so He forgot them' is crucial.
Why would literal forgetting be problematic? Because it suggests change and imperfection.
3
Uncover the Salaf's solution
The author explains that the verse carries two meanings: literal forgetfulness (which is impossible for Allah) and metaphorical neglect. He states that the Salaf consistently chose the metaphorical meaning (kinayah) to preserve transcendence.
The Salaf understood 'forgetting' as Allah neglecting those who neglected Him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن ليست كأيدي البشر لأنه » ليس كمثله شيء » بل نقول : الله واحد متصف بكل كمال ومنزه عن كل نقص وليس كمثله شيء .. واذا لم نقل بذلك وأثبتنا اليد مع نفي المماثلة فماذا نقول في مثل قوله تعالى نسوا الله فنسيهم ( ؟ هل تثبت نسيانا لله مع عدم مماثلة نسيان الله النسيان البشر ؟ ان من يثبت نسيانا لله مع عدم مماثلة نسيان الله النسيان البشر يكون كافرا وبعيدا كل البعد عن رحمة الله ... ومثال صفات الأحاسيس نسوا الله فنسيهم ( ) التوبة : ٦٧ ) » وهى تحتمل معنيين النسيان الحقيقى والكناية عن الاهمال أى أهملوا تعاليم الله وأغفلوا ذكره فأهملهم الله وتركهم من رحمته . أى خلى بينهم وبين أهواتهم. والمعنى الكنائى هو المراد . لما قلنا ، وهذا هو فهم السلف . فما سمعنا عن أجد منهم غير التنزيه الله عز وجل . والا يكن هذا فهمهم . فما هو تأويلهم لمثل قوله تعالى : ( نسوا الله فنسيهم ) وقوله عن سفينة نوح عليه السلام : « تجرى بأعيننا » ( القمر : ١٤ ) وهل كانوا يفهمون أن للمقادير - وهى معنوية - أعنة كأعنة الخيول السريعة الجرى فى قول الشاعر : دع المقادير تجرى في أعنتها ولا تبيتن الا خالي البالي ما بين طرفة عين وانتباهتها تغير الله من حال الى حال ؟
But they are not like the hands of human beings because 'There is nothing like unto Him.' Rather we say: Allah is One, described with every perfection, and free from every deficiency, and there is nothing like unto Him. If we do not say that and we affirm the hand while negating similarity, then what do we say about His saying 'They forgot Allah so He forgot them'? Do you affirm forgetting for Allah while there is no similarity between Allah's forgetting and human forgetting? Indeed, whoever affirms forgetting for Allah while there is no similarity between Allah's forgetting and human forgetting becomes a disbeliever and is far from the mercy of Allah. And an example of the attributes of senses: 'They forgot Allah so He forgot them' (At-Tawbah: 67). It carries two meanings: real forgetfulness and metonymy for neglect, i.e., they neglected Allah's commands and forgot His remembrance, so He neglected them and abandoned them from His mercy, i.e., He left them to their desires. The metaphorical meaning is intended, as we said, and this is the understanding of the Salaf. We have not heard from any of them anything other than glorifying Allah Almighty. If this is not their understanding, then what is their interpretation of such verses as 'They forgot Allah so He forgot them' and His saying about the ship of Nuh (peace be upon him): 'It sails under Our eyes' (Al-Qamar: 14)? And did they understand that the decrees — which are spiritual — have reins like the reins of fast-running horses in the poet's saying: 'Leave the decrees to run in their reins, and do not stay up except with an empty mind, between the twinkling of an eye and its blink, Allah changes from one state to another?'
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the metaphorical interpretation of divine attributes. The author starts by affirming the attribute of 'hand' but immediately negates any similarity to created hands. He then extends the same logic to the attribute of 'forgetting'. He argues that simply affirming the attribute while denying similarity is not enough; one must clarify that such verses are meant metaphorically. For example, 'They forgot Allah so He forgot them' is interpreted by the Salaf as a kinayah (metonymy) for neglect, not literal forgetfulness. He supports this by citing another verse and a line of poetry, showing that even spiritual concepts like 'decrees' are described with physical terms metaphorically. The author's point is that the Salaf consistently interpreted problematic attributes in a way that preserves transcendence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply affirming an attribute like 'hand' or 'forgetting' while denying similarity is sufficient to avoid anthropomorphism.
Correction: The author shows that for attributes that imply deficiency (like forgetting), further metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil) is necessary to avoid attributing imperfection to Allah. The Salaf interpreted such verses as metonymy, not literal attributes.

Checkpoint

B) Metaphorical neglect, not literal forgetting
C) Both literal and metaphorical meaning

Key Takeaway
The Salaf interpreted problematic divine attributes metaphorically to protect Allah's transcendence from any deficiency or anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Salaf chose the metaphorical meaning to protect Allah's perfection. Are you willing to let go of a literal understanding of a verse if it leads to a deficiency in your concept of Allah? Which verse challenges you the most, and how will you seek its correct interpretation?
?
If Allah's 'forgetting' is actually a just response to your neglect, how does that change the way you view your relationship with Him? Will you examine where you have been neglecting His commands, and commit to a specific change this week?

Juwayni's View on Human Action and the Charge of Determinism
Juwayni's explanation of how acts occur and the critique that it implies determinism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Juwayni's explanation of how human actions occur and the critique that his view implies determinism.

Core Idea
Al-Juwayni's view reduces human action to a predetermined machine.

This passage opens with a strong assertion: al-Juwayni's statements lean toward determinism. It then presents his own description of how Allah creates motives and capacity, and the rhetorical critique questions whether this leaves any real human agency. Let's examine his words and the commentator's challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's own words
Read the passage where Juwayni describes how Allah creates the capacity and motives in the servant, and how actions occur by the servant's created power according to divine knowledge and will.
Notice the role of divine will in every detail.
2
Identify the deterministic elements
Look for phrases that suggest the servant has no real choice: Allah 'strips knowledge of details,' 'prepares causes,' and actions occur exactly as known and willed.
3
Consider the rhetorical critique
The commentator asks if this makes man a machine executing a pre-written script. Reflect on whether the description allows for genuine human agency.
This is the key critique of Juwayni's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجويني لم يذهب الى ما ذهب اليه أهل الكتاب فى التوفيق - وإن كان قد حاوله - وانما نطق بعبارات هى الى الجبر أقرب منها الى الاختيار . بل هي جبر . انه يقول » أحدث الله تبارك وتعالى القدر فى العبد على أقدار أحاط بها علمه وهياً أسباب الفعل وسلب الله العلم بالتفاصيل وأراد من العبد أن يفعل فأحدث فيه دواعي مستحثة وخيرة واردة .. وعلم أن الأفعال ستقع على قدر معلوم فوقعت بالقدرة التي اخترعها العبد على ما علم وأراد ( هل معنى هذا الا أن الانسان آلة يوقع الفعل المرسوم له من قبل الله من قبل أن يخلقه الله ؟ وأى فرق بين هذا الرأى ورأى الأشعرى الذى نقده امام الحرمين ؟ يقول الأشعرى رحمه الله - بقدرة الله وقدرة للعبد مقترنان عند حدوث الفعل من العبد فالعبد فى الظاهر فاعل . والله فى الحقيقة واضع يده مع العبد . ويقول امام الحرمين له « ولا سبيل الى المصير الى وقوع فعل العبد بقدرته الحادثة ، والقدرة القديمة . فالفعل الواحد يستحيل حدوثه بقادرين اذ الواحد لا ينقسم فان وقع بقدرة الله سبحانه استقل بها وسقط أثر القدرة الحادثة ، ويستحيل أن يقع بعضه بقدرة الله عز وجل ، فان الفعل الواحد لا بعض له »
Al-Juwayni did not go to what the People of the Book went to in reconciliation—although he attempted it—rather he uttered expressions that are closer to determinism (jabr) than to free choice. Rather, they are determinism. He says: 'Allah, blessed and exalted, created the capacity in the servant according to measures that His knowledge encompassed, and prepared the causes of the act, and Allah stripped knowledge of details, and He willed from the servant that he act, so He created in him impelling motives and an incoming choice... And He knew that actions would occur according to a known measure, so they occurred by the power that the servant invented, according to what He knew and willed. Does this mean anything but that man is a machine that performs the act prescribed for him from Allah before Allah created him? And what difference is there between this opinion and the opinion of al-Ash'ari that Imam al-Haramayn criticized? Al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him, says: By the power of Allah and a power for the servant, both co-existing at the occurrence of the act from the servant, so the servant is apparently an agent, and Allah in reality places His hand with the servant. And Imam al-Haramayn says to him: 'There is no way to arrive at the occurrence of the servant's act by his originated power and the eternal power. So a single act is impossible to occur by two agents, since the one is not divisible. If it occurs by the power of Allah, He alone suffices for it and the effect of the originated power falls away, and it is impossible for part of it to occur by the power of Allah, mighty and majestic, for a single act has no part.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of al-Juwayni's position on human action and predestination. It begins by stating that al-Juwayni did not adopt the reconciliation of the People of the Book (likely a reference to earlier attempts to harmonize divine sovereignty and human freedom) but instead made statements that lean heavily toward determinism (jabr). The author then quotes al-Juwayni's own words: Allah creates the capacity in the servant according to predetermined measures, prepares the causes, removes knowledge of details, and creates motives and choice, so that actions occur by the servant's created power exactly as Allah knew and willed. The commentator questions whether this reduces humans to mere machines. He then contrasts al-Juwayni's view with that of al-Ash'ari, who posits two co-existing powers—divine and human—at the moment of action, making the servant an apparent agent while Allah is the true agent. Al-Juwayni objects to this, arguing that a single act cannot be produced by two agents because it is indivisible; if it occurs by Allah's power, then the effect of the servant's power is nullified, and it cannot be partially by both. Thus, al-Juwayni rejects the Ash'ari notion of two powers cooperating.

Key Terms
قدرة حادثة
جبر
دواعي مستحثة
خيرة واردة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Juwayni's view affirms genuine human agency because he mentions the servant's created power.
Correction: The passage shows that even the 'created power' is predetermined by divine will and knowledge, and the servant's motives are created by Allah, leaving no room for independent choice.

Checkpoint
According to the critique, what does al-Juwayni's description imply about human action?
A) Humans have genuine free will.
B) Humans are machines executing a divine script.
C) Both divine and human powers cooperate equally.
D) Humans create their own actions independently.

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's description of human action, if taken literally, implies a deterministic system where the servant has no real choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your daily choices—your prayers, your work, your relationships—do you genuinely feel you are actively choosing, or do you sense that your actions are merely unfolding as predetermined? How does Juwayni's description challenge your personal sense of moral responsibility? What would change in your life if you truly believed every motive was created for you?
?
Juwayni's critics argue that his view reduces man to a machine. In what specific area of your life are you most likely to act like a passive recipient of fate, avoiding real struggle and accountability? Confront that area honestly: are you using divine decree as an excuse for complacency?
?
If every impulse and choice comes from Allah, then where does your repentance fit in? How can you sincerely turn back to Allah when your very desire to repent may itself be created? Does this thought lead you to despair or to deeper reliance on Allah's mercy? Answer with your heart, not your theology.

Juwayni's Critique of the Ash'ari Two-Power Theory
Juwayni refutes the Ash'ari position that an act can be from two co-existing powers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Juwayni's logical argument that a single act cannot be produced by two agents, refuting the Ash'ari theory of two powers.

Core Idea
A single act is indivisible, so it cannot come from two separate agents.

After presenting his own view, the passage turns to contrast it with al-Ash'ari's two-power theory and then presents al-Juwayni's decisive objection. Al-Ash'ari claims that an act occurs by both divine and human powers co-existing, but al-Juwayni argues that a single act is indivisible and cannot be attributed to two agents. Let's follow this logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ash'ari's view
Al-Ash'ari states that at the occurrence of the act, both Allah's power and the servant's power are present. The servant appears to be the agent, but Allah is the true agent.
This is the 'acquisition' theory (kasb).
2
Understand al-Juwayni's objection
Al-Juwayni argues that a single act cannot be from two agents because it is one and indivisible. If it is by Allah's power alone, then the servant's power has no effect. If it is partially by Allah, an act has no parts.
The logic is based on the unity of the act.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this argument is a fundamental critique of the Ash'ari attempt to preserve both divine sovereignty and human responsibility.
Al-Juwayni concludes that the Ash'ari position is logically impossible.

Source Text

D) Allah's power is limited.

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's argument shows that the Ash'ari attempt to combine divine and human power in one act is logically untenable because a single act cannot be split between two agents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a moment when you achieved something praiseworthy, did you silently attribute it to your own skill and effort, or to Allah's grace? Juwayni's argument forces you to choose: if it was truly from Allah, then your power added nothing. Examine your heart: which attribution do you truly rely upon when no one is watching? Commit today to verbally acknowledge Allah's sole power in every success, big or small.
?
If the act of sin is also a single act, and Allah's power is involved in its existence (as Ash'aris hold), does that make you feel less responsible? Juwayni shows that the Ash'ari attempt to share power logically collapses. How does that affect your sense of accountability before Allah? Will you now repent more sincerely, recognizing that your power is real and that you cannot blame divine decree for your choices? Decide now to take full ownership of your sins and turn to Allah with a broken heart.

Juwayni on Reward as Favor and Punishment as Justice
Juwayni's statement on reward and punishment and the opposing view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's view that divine reward is a favor and punishment is just recompense, and the contrasting view that reward is obligatory upon God.

Core Idea
For Juwayni, reward is grace; punishment is justice; but others see reward as God's duty.

This lesson presents two perspectives on divine reward and punishment. Juwayni emphasizes God's absolute freedom, while another school argues that God obligated Himself to reward the obedient. We will examine the scriptural basis for each view.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's position
Read how Juwayni describes reward and punishment as tafaddul and jaza' wifaq respectively.
2
Identify the opposing view
Notice the differing opinion: others say reward is wajib upon God, citing the verse about mercy being prescribed.
The verse is from Qur'an 6:54.
3
Compare the two positions
Contrast the implications of each view: God's freedom vs. His self-imposed obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحدث الجويني عن الثواب والعقاب . فبين أن الله يثيب الطائع على عمله الخير تفضلا منه ، ويعاقب العاصى على عمله السىء جزاء وفاقا بينما يقرر غيره ان اثابة الله للطائع ليست تفضلا من الله ، بل هو أمر واجب على الله .. أوجبه هو على نفسه بقوله تعالى « كتب ربكم على نفسه الرحمة ) ( الأنعام : ٥٤ ( وللتوفيق بين رأى الجويني وغيره يمكن القول بأن الله تعالى تفضل أزلا بخلق الخلق . ثم نص للخلق على أنه كتب الرحمة وكتب العذاب ، ليحملهم على عدم العذر اليه
And Juwayni discussed reward (thawab) and punishment ('iqab). He explained that God rewards the obedient for their good work as a favor (tafaddul) from Him, and punishes the disobedient for their evil work as a just recompense (jaza'an wifaqan), while others assert that God's rewarding of the obedient is not a favor from God, but rather a matter obligatory upon God, which He made obligatory upon Himself by His saying: 'Your Lord has prescribed mercy for Himself' (Qur'an 6:54). And to reconcile between Juwayni's view and others, it can be said that God Almighty favored (tafaddala) from eternity by creating creation. Then He declared to creation that He prescribed mercy and prescribed punishment, in order to remove any excuse from them towards Him.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents Juwayni's view on divine reward and punishment. Juwayni holds that God rewards the obedient as a favor (tafaddul), not because He is obligated, and punishes the disobedient as a just recompense (jaza' wifaq). The commentator notes that others disagree, arguing that God's reward is obligatory upon Him, citing the verse 'Your Lord has prescribed mercy for Himself' (6:54), implying God obligated Himself. The commentator then attempts a reconciliation: God's original act of creation was a favor, and then He announced the prescription of mercy and punishment to leave no excuse for humanity. This preserves both God's freedom and the idea of obligation as self-imposed.

Key Terms
الثواب
العقاب
التفضل
الجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Juwayni denies any form of divine obligation entirely.
Correction: Juwayni's view is that reward is not inherently obligatory; but the passage shows others argue for obligation based on a self-imposed divine decree.

Checkpoint
According to Juwayni, how does God reward the obedient?
A) As an obligatory right of the servant
B) As a favor from Himself
C) As a repayment for the servant's effort
D) As a necessary consequence of justice

Key Takeaway
Juwayni sees reward as a gift, not a debt; others see it as a self-imposed divine duty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you obey God, do you feel He owes you something in return? How does Juwayni's teaching that reward is purely a favor—not a wage—challenge that sense of entitlement in your heart?
?
If you truly believed that every blessing, including your salvation, is a gift of God's grace and not a debt He must pay, how would your gratitude change today? Can you name one blessing you've been taking for granted?
?
The opposing view says God made reward obligatory on Himself. But Juwayni insists it remains a favor. Which perspective makes you more humble in your worship—seeing yourself as a worker earning wages, or as a beggar receiving charity? Why does that matter for your relationship with God?

Reconciling Divine Favor and Self-Imposed Obligation
Reconciliation between Juwayni and the opposing view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a proposed reconciliation between Juwayni's view of reward as favor and the view that God obligated Himself to reward.

Core Idea
God's initial creation is the ultimate favor; His prescribed mercy and punishment remove excuses.

The commentator offers a way to harmonize the two perspectives: God's eternal favor in creation preceded any specific reward. The announcements of mercy and punishment serve to remind humanity and cut off excuses. This preserves both grace and obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the reconciliation
Read the proposed solution: God favored creation from eternity, then prescribed mercy and punishment.
2
Understand the two acts
Distinguish between the initial favor (creating) and the declarative act (prescribing mercy/punishment).
3
Reflect on the purpose
The prescription is to remove excuses from people, not to impose a debt on God.

Juwayni's Rational Argument and the Primacy of Revelation
Juwayni argues for rational possibility of ru'ya; commentator refutes using scriptural distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's rational argument for the possibility of seeing God and why the commentator insists that creedal beliefs must be based on definitive revelation, not rational possibility.

Core Idea
Revelation, not reason alone, is the foundation of Islamic creed.

This passage presents Juwayni's attempt to prove the possibility of seeing God using rational reasoning, and the commentator's immediate rebuttal that revelation clearly distinguishes between hearing God's speech and seeing Him. The commentator argues that definitive scriptural texts, such as Moses being told 'You will not see Me,' settle the matter, and that Juwayni's reliance on what reason deems possible is misguided.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's argument
Notice how Juwayni argues that it is not impossible for God to create a perception in the servant, so seeing God is rationally possible.
Juwayni's argument is purely based on rational possibility.
2
Identify the commentator's criticism
The commentator points out that revelation distinguishes between hearing God and seeing Him, and that Moses himself was denied vision.
3
Understand the principle
The commentator asserts that beliefs are established by divine texts, not by what reason deems permissible.
This is a key methodological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأثبت الجوينى جواز رؤية الاله تبارك وتعالى . وفاته أن نصوص. آيات الكتاب والسنة تفرق بين صوت الله وبين رؤية الله . وهى صريحة فى هذا التفريق ، وصريحة أيضا فى اثبات الصوت ونفى الرؤية ، فموسى عليه السلام كلم الله تكليما ، وموسى نفسه الذي كلم الله وقهم المراد م الكلام طلب رؤية الله له « لن تراني » وعلى ذلك لا عکس مراد الله في محكم آياته فنثبت الرؤية وننفى الكلام وليس من دليل للتجوينى الا قوله « لا يمتنع فى قدرة الله سبحانه أن يخصص من أراد بصفة هى فى التعلق بوجوده بالاضافة الى العلم كالادراك المطلق بالمدركات ، شاهد بالأضافة الى العلم بها على الغيب من غير درك ثم تلك الصفة من مقدورات البارى تبارك وتعالى وهى لا تتناهى ومن لم يحله العقل التحق بالجائزات » . يعنى أن الله اذا أراد أن يرى نفسه للعبد خلق فى العبد ادراكا به يراه. وهذا جائز في العقل . ودليله واضح البطلان فان العقائد تثبت بنصوص سماوية لا تقبل الجدل ولا تثبت بما يجوزه العقل . فإن عقل البعض من الناس حكم بأن الله هو المسيح بن مريم وبأن الله ثالث ثلاثة ، وعقل البعض سوغ لهم السير على سنن الآباء والأجداد

ان

( صريح القرآن الكريم » لا تدركه الأبصار » ( الأنعام : ١٠٣ ) وهذا هو المحكم .. وأما المتشابه فهو ) وجوه يومئذ ناضرة الى ربها ناظرة » ( القيامة : ٢٢ - ٣٣ ) فانها تحتمل الرؤية الحقيقية وتحتمل
And Juwayni affirmed the permissibility of seeing God (ru'yat al-ilah) Almighty. He missed that the texts of the Book and the Sunnah distinguish between the voice of God and the vision of God. They are explicit in this distinction, and also explicit in affirming the voice and denying the vision. For Moses, peace be upon him, God spoke directly to him, and Moses himself, to whom God spoke and who understood the intended meaning of the speech, asked to see God, and He said: 'You will not see Me' (Qur'an 7:143). Upon that, there is no reversal of God's intent in His definitive verses: so we affirm the vision and deny the speech! And Juwayni has no evidence except his saying: 'It is not impossible in the power of God Almighty that He should specify whom He wills with an attribute that, in its relation to existence, is like absolute perception of perceptibles, witnessing by relation to knowledge of them, to the unseen without perception; then that attribute is among the capabilities of the Creator Almighty, and they are unlimited, and what reason does not deem impossible belongs to the category of possibilities.' That is, God, if He wills to show Himself to a servant, creates in that servant a perception by which he sees Him. And this is permissible according to reason. But his proof is clearly invalid, for beliefs are established by divine texts that admit no argument, and are not established by what reason deems permissible. For the reason of some people judged that God is the Messiah son of Mary and that God is the third of three, and the reason of others permitted them to follow the ways of their fathers and forefathers.

But the clear text of the Qur'an says: 'Vision does not comprehend Him' (Qur'an 6:103). That is definitive (muhkam). As for the ambiguous (mutashabih), it is: 'Faces on that day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' (Qur'an 75:22-23). For it may imply real vision or may imply [something else].
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents Juwayni's argument for the possibility of seeing God (ru'ya) and the commentator's rebuttal. Juwayni argues that it is not impossible for God to create a special perception in a servant by which he sees Him, and whatever reason does not deem impossible is permissible. The commentator strongly criticizes this, stating that creedal beliefs must be based on definitive revelation, not rational possibility. He cites the distinction in revelation between hearing God's speech and seeing Him: Moses heard God but was told 'You will not see Me.' The commentator insists that the definitive verse 'Vision does not comprehend Him' (6:103) is clear (muhkam) and must take precedence over the ambiguous verse about faces looking at their Lord (75:22-23), which could be interpreted metaphorically. Juwayni's reliance on rational possibility is dismissed as invalid because reason can lead to error, as shown by those who claim Jesus is God or the Trinity.

Key Terms
الرؤية
الجائز
النصوص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Juwayni's rational argument for the possibility of seeing God is valid because reason does not deem it impossible.
Correction: The commentator argues that creedal beliefs are established by definitive revelation, and reason alone is insufficient; moreover, revelation explicitly denies the vision of God in this world.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what did Moses ask for and what was he told?
A) To speak to God, 'I will speak to you'
B) To see God, 'You will not see Me'
C) To hear God, 'You will hear Me'
D) To touch God, 'You cannot touch Me'

Key Takeaway
Creedal matters are settled by definitive revelation, not by rational possibility alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological issue that seems logically sound but contradicts a clear verse, do you instinctively try to reinterpret the verse, or do you submit to its apparent meaning? Why?
?
Think of one area in your life where you rely on your own reasoning more than on revelation—whether in belief or practice. Will you consciously subject that area to scripture today?
?
Moses heard God’s speech but was denied sight. Does your heart yearn for God’s vision with the same desperation as Moses? If not, what does that reveal about your relationship with the Creator?

Definitive and Ambiguous Texts on the Vision of God
Commentator cites muhkam and mutashabih verses to settle the ru'ya debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator uses the definitive verse 'Vision does not comprehend Him' (6:103) to refute the possibility of seeing God, and how the ambiguous verse about faces looking at their Lord is interpreted.

Core Idea
Definitive (muhkam) verses take precedence over ambiguous (mutashabih) verses.

Having established that revelation is the foundation, the commentator now cites specific Qur'anic texts. He presents the verse 'Vision does not comprehend Him' as definitive (muhkam) and decisive, while the verse 'Faces on that day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' is ambiguous (mutashabih) and cannot override the clear text.

Guided Path
1
Read the two verses presented
Identify the definitive verse (muhkam) and the ambiguous verse (mutashabih).
2
Understand the commentator's method
He uses the principle that the ambiguous must be interpreted in light of the definitive, not the other way around.
This is a standard method in Islamic theology.
3
Reflect on the lesson for creedal methodology
This demonstrates the importance of prioritizing clear texts over those open to multiple interpretations.

Juwayni's Proof for the Beatific Vision and Its Refutation
Juwayni's proof for beatific vision and its Quranic refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's rational argument for the beatific vision and why it is refuted based on the Quranic distinction between muhkam and mutashabih verses.

Core Idea
The beatific vision is denied by decisive Quranic texts, despite rational possibility.

In this passage, the author presents Juwayni's argument that seeing God is rationally possible and then refutes it by appealing to the primacy of revelation. Juwayni claims God can create perception, but the author counters that creedal beliefs must be grounded in definitive scriptures, not mere rational speculation. The key is the distinction between muhkam (clear) and mutashabih (ambiguous) verses, where the clear verses deny vision.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's Argument
Read Juwayni's proof that God can create perception. Notice it is based on rational possibility.
2
Understand the Refutation
The author rejects this by stating that beliefs come from revelation. Identify the key citing of Quranic verses.
3
Apply the Muhkam-Mutashabih Principle
See how the author uses the decisive verse 'Visions comprehend Him not' to interpret the ambiguous 'looking at their Lord' metaphorically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأثبت الجوينى جواز رؤية الاله تبارك وتعالى . وفاته أن نصوص آيات الكتاب والسنة تفرق بين صوت الله وبين رؤية الله . وهى صريحة فى هذا التفريق ، وصريحة أيضا فى اثبات الصوت ونفى الرؤية ، فموسى عليه السلام كلم الله تكليما ، وموسى نفسه الذي كلم الله وفهم المراد من الكلام طلب رؤية الله له « لن تراني » وعلى ذلك لا عکس مراد الله في محكم آياته فنثبت الرؤية وننفى الكلام وليس من دليل للتجوينى الا قوله « لا يمتنع فى قدرة الله سبحانه أن يخصص من أراد بصفة هى فى التعلق بوجوده بالاضافة الى العلم كالادراك المطلق بالمدركات ، شاهد بالأضافة الى العلم بها على الغيب من غير درك ثم تلك الصفة من مقدورات البارى تبارك وتعالى وهى لا تتناهى ومن لم يحله العقل التحق بالجائزات » . يعنى أن الله اذا أراد أن يرى نفسه للعبد خلق فى العبد ادراكا به يراه. وهذا جائز في العقل . ودليله واضح البطلان فان العقائد تثبت بنصوص سماوية لا تقبل الجدل ولا تثبت بما يجوزه العقل . فإن عقل البعض من الناس حكم بأن الله هو المسيح بن مريم وبأن الله ثالث ثلاثة ، وعقل البعض سوغ لهم السير على سنن الآباء والأجداد وصريح القرآن الكريم « لا تدركه الأبصار » ( الأنعام : ١٠٣ ) وهذا هو المحكم .. وأما المتشابه فهو « وجوه يومئذ ناضرة الى ربها ناظرة » ( القيامة : ٢٢ - ٣٣ ) فانها تحتمل الرؤية الحقيقية وتحتمل المعنى المجازى عن نعمة الله وحيث النص متشابه فليرجع الى المحكم الذي ينفي الرؤية . ويقوى المحكم قول الله لموسى « لن ترانی » وقد كان سؤال موسى عن غير ذهول منه عن الغيب . والا كان يعاد السؤال مرة أخرى . وما كان الله عز وجل يؤكد على الأمة الاسلامية أن يسألوا بما سألت عنه الأمة الأولى فقد قال تعالى : ( أم تريدون أن تسألوا رسولكم كما سئل موسى من قبل ؟ » ) البقرة : ١٠٧ )
And Juwayni affirmed the permissibility of seeing God, Blessed and Exalted. He missed that the texts of the Book and the Sunnah distinguish between God's voice and seeing God. They are explicit in this distinction, and explicit also in affirming the voice and denying the vision. Thus Moses, peace be upon him, was spoken to by God directly, and Moses himself, who was spoken to by God and understood the intended meaning of the speech, asked to see God, and God said, 'You will not see Me' (Al-A'raf 7:143). Accordingly, there is no reversal of God's intention in His decisive verses, so we affirm the vision and deny speech? There is no evidence for Juwayni except his saying: 'It is not impossible in the power of God Almighty that He should specify for whom He wills a quality which, in relation to its connection with existence, is like absolute perception of perceptibles, witnessing in addition to knowledge of them in the unseen without [direct] perception; then that quality is among the capabilities of the Creator, Blessed and Exalted, and they are infinite. And whatever the mind does not deem impossible is included among the possibilities.' This means that if God wants to show Himself to the servant, He creates in the servant a perception by which he sees Him. This is intellectually permissible. But his proof is clearly invalid, because beliefs are established by divine texts that are not open to debate, not by what the mind deems permissible. Indeed, the minds of some people judged that God is the Messiah, son of Mary, and that God is the third of three, and the minds of others allowed them to follow the ways of their fathers and forefathers. The explicit Quran says, 'Visions comprehend Him not' (Al-An'am 6:103). This is the decisive (muhkam). As for the ambiguous (mutashabih), it is 'Faces on that Day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' (Al-Qiyama 75:22-23), for it may bear the meaning of real vision or the metaphorical meaning of looking at God's favor. And since the text is ambiguous, it should be referred to the decisive which denies vision. And the decisive is strengthened by God's saying to Moses, 'You will not see Me.' And Moses' question was not from unawareness of the unseen; otherwise, he would have repeated the question. And God Almighty emphasized to the Muslim community not to ask as the first community asked, for He said: 'Or do you wish to ask your Messenger as Moses was asked before?' (Al-Baqarah 2:108).
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Juwayni's argument for the beatific vision. It begins by stating that Juwayni affirmed the possibility of seeing God, but he overlooked that scriptural texts distinguish between hearing God's speech and seeing Him, affirming the former and denying the latter, as seen in Moses' case. Juwayni's proof is quoted: God can create a perception in the believer to see Him, and this is not impossible. The refutation then argues that religious beliefs are based on definitive texts, not on mere rational possibility. The author points to the danger of relying on reason alone, as some reason wrongly concluded that God is Christ or a trinity. The decisive (muhkam) verse 'Visions comprehend Him not' denies vision, while the ambiguous (mutashabih) verse about 'looking at their Lord' is interpreted metaphorically. This is supported by God's response to Moses and the prohibition of asking improper questions.

Key Terms
رؤية الله
كلام الله
محكم
متشابه
لن تراني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational possibility is sufficient to establish a creedal belief.
Correction: The author shows that creed requires definitive scriptural texts, not mere rational possibility.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author refutes Juwayni's proof for the beatific vision?
A) It is logically impossible for God to create perception.
B) Beliefs must be based on definitive scriptural texts, not rational possibilities.
C) Moses himself saw God, contradicting Juwayni.
D) The Quran is silent on the issue.

Key Takeaway
The beatific vision is impossible because the clear Quranic texts deny it, and ambiguous verses must be interpreted accordingly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any beliefs you hold about God that you have accepted simply because they 'make sense' to your mind, rather than because they are firmly grounded in a clear Quranic text or authentic Sunnah? Will you submit your reason to the decisive revelation even when it challenges your intellectual comfort?
?
When you read God's words to Moses, 'You will not see Me,' do you truly accept that you will never see your Lord in this life or the next? Or does some part of you still long for a sensory encounter with Him on your own terms? How does this submission—or lack of it—reveal the state of your heart towards His sovereignty?
?
Have you ever interpreted an ambiguous verse of the Quran in a way that suited your desires or preconceived notions, without referring it back to the clear, decisive texts? What would it take for you to commit to the principle that the ambiguous must be explained by the clear, even if it means giving up a cherished interpretation?

The Possibility of Pre-Creation of Paradise and Hell
Juwayni states the possibility and addresses an objection about the interpretation of 'أعدت'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Juwayni's assertion that Paradise and Hell can be created before Judgment Day, based on the verse 'Prepared for the righteous' and the refutation of the objection that this implies future creation.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell can be created before Judgment Day; the Qur'an's past tense indicates certainty.

Imam Juwayni addresses a key theological question: were Paradise and Hell created before the Day of Judgment? He argues that there is no impossibility in this, citing the Qur'anic verse 'Prepared for the righteous.' Opponents, however, interpret 'prepared' as a future event. Let's examine his argument and the response.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's position
Read Juwayni's opening statement that there is no impossibility in pre-creating Paradise and Hell. Identify his proof text.
The verse 'Prepared for the righteous' uses the past tense.
2
Examine the objection and response
Opponents reinterpret 'prepared' to mean 'will be prepared' in the future. Understand Juwayni's counter that the past tense indicates certainty of occurrence.
Juwayni compares it to the verse 'The command of Allah has come.'
3
Reflect on the argument
Consider why this interpretation matters for the debate on pre-creation. Juwayni shows that the verse does not necessitate pre-creation but is compatible with it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبين الجويني عبد الملك أنه «لا استحالة في تقديم خلق الجنة والنار على يوم الجزاء» وقد دفعه إلى هذا القول قوله تعالى «أعدت للمتقين». ودفع غيره إلى القول بأن الجنان خارجة عن أقطار السموات والأرض فكيف تنطوي عليهما السموات. تفسيرهم بمعنى «أعدت» كما في قوله «أتى أمر الله» والمراد «يأتي»، وعبر الله بالماضي لتحقق الوقوع، وأن هذا الأمر كائن لا محالة. وفهمهم المعارضة بين قوله تعالى «مثل الجنة التي وعد المتقون تجري من تحتها الأنهار أكلها دائم وظلها» وبين قوله تعالى «كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه» فإن دوام الأكل معارض بهلاك كل شيء غير ذات الله، وعليه لو كانت الجنة مخلوقة لوجب هلاك أكلها فلا يدوم. وأيضا استدلوا بقوله تعالى «عرضها السموات والأرض» ولا يتصور ذلك إلا بعد فناء السموات والأرض لامتناع تداخل الأجسام إن لم يكن التعبير كناية عن عظم الاتساع.
And Juwayni, Abd al-Malik, clarified that 'there is no impossibility in the creation of Paradise and Hell being before the Day of Recompense.' He was driven to this statement by His saying: 'Prepared for the righteous.' And others were driven to say that the Gardens are outside the regions of the heavens and the earth, so how could the heavens encompass them? Their interpretation of 'prepared' is like His saying 'The command of Allah has come' — the intended meaning is 'will come' — and Allah expressed it in the past tense to indicate the certainty of occurrence, and that this matter is inevitably going to happen. And they understood a contradiction between His saying 'The parable of Paradise which the righteous are promised, beneath it rivers flow, its food is perpetual and its shade' and His saying 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' For the perpetuity of the food is opposed by the perishing of everything other than Allah's essence, and accordingly, if Paradise were created, its food would necessarily perish and not endure. And they also adduced His saying: 'Its expanse is the heavens and the earth,' but that cannot be conceived except after the annihilation of the heavens and the earth, due to the impossibility of interpenetration of bodies — unless the expression is a metaphor for vastness.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Juwayni's own position on the creation of Paradise and Hell, along with the objections of others and his implicit response. Juwayni asserts that there is no logical impossibility (istihalah) in Paradise and Hell being created before the Day of Judgment. He bases this on the Qur'anic verse 'Prepared for the righteous' (3:133), which uses the past tense and implies that Paradise already exists. Some opponents, however, argued that Paradise must be outside the heavens and earth because otherwise the heavens would encompass it, which is impossible. Juwayni notes that they interpret 'prepared' (أعدت) as meaning 'will be prepared' in the future, analogous to the verse 'The command of Allah has come' (16:1) where the past tense actually indicates future certainty. Next, the opponents raise an objection: the description of Paradise as having perpetual food contradicts the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88). If Paradise is created, its food would be subject to perishing, so it cannot be eternal. Juwayni does not explicitly refute this here, but his mention of their 'understanding' (فهمهم) suggests he considers their interpretation flawed. Finally, the opponents cite the verse 'Its expanse is the heavens and the earth' (3:133) to argue that Paradise must be as vast as the heavens and earth, and since the heavens and earth are finite and will be replaced, Paradise cannot be created until after they perish — otherwise there would be interpenetration of bodies. Juwayni notes that this expression could be a metaphor for immense vastness, not literal dimensions. The passage thus juxtaposes Juwayni's stance with the opposing arguments, implying that the objections can be met with reinterpretation.

Key Terms
خلق الجنة والنار
استحالة
أعدت
أتى أمر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence Juwayni uses for his position?
A) Verse about food
B) Verse about expanse
C) Verse 'Prepared for the righteous'
D) Hadith

Key Takeaway
Juwayni bases his view on the Qur'anic verse 'Prepared for the righteous', interpreting the past tense as indicating certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that Paradise is 'prepared' for the righteous using a past tense that signals certainty. Is your certainty in Allah's promise of Paradise as real as if you already saw it? What would change in your life today if you lived with that level of conviction?
?
Juwayni argues that the past tense indicates certainty, not necessarily past time. When you recite Qur'anic promises like 'قد أفلح المؤمنون', do you feel the weight of that certainty? What sin or doubt are you holding onto that contradicts that sure promise?
?
The objection that Paradise cannot be pre-created because it is outside the heavens reflects a human limitation of imagination. Where in your own faith do you limit Allah's power based on your own understanding? Repent and ask Him to expand your tawheed.
